# BATU EXPORT — Build Decisions Log

Tracks decisions made during implementation that aren't already locked in `docs/SPEC.md`. Append-only; newest entry at the bottom of each section. If a decision later supersedes the spec itself, update `SPEC.md` and add a Changelog line there too.

Format per entry:

```
## YYYY-MM-DD — Short title
**Context:** why this came up
**Decision:** what was chosen
**Alternatives considered:** (optional)
```

---

## 2026-07-12 — Phase 0 scaffold choices
**Context:** Setting up the Vite + React + TS + Tailwind PWA shell per `PHASE0.md`.
**Decision:**
- Tailwind CSS v4 via `@tailwindcss/vite` (CSS-first config, no `tailwind.config.js` needed) instead of the classic v3 PostCSS setup.
- `vite-plugin-pwa` (`registerType: 'autoUpdate'`) for the offline-first requirement (§2.6), rather than hand-writing a service worker.
- No router yet — `App.tsx` does a plain `session ? <HomePage /> : <LoginPage />` check. Role-based routing (§1.1, per-role home screens) is deferred to the auth/roles step, since adding `react-router-dom` now would be unused scaffolding.
- Auth state read via a small `useSession` hook wrapping `supabase.auth.getSession()` + `onAuthStateChange`, rather than a full context provider — revisit if more than one component needs session state.

## 2026-07-12 — Phase 0 database migrations
**Context:** Turning SPEC §8 + PHASE0 Part B into numbered SQL migrations in `/supabase/migrations`.
**Decision:**
- Followed PHASE0's file grouping but numbered/split it as 7 files so master data always precedes anything that references it: `0001_master_data`, `0002_serial`, `0003_operational`, `0004_storage`, `0005_notes_audit`, `0006_views`, `0007_rls`.
- `next_serial()` is `security definer` (search_path pinned to `public`) so it can write to `serial_counter` even though that table itself carries **no RLS policies at all** — the function is the only door in or out of it. Matches "the database is the source of truth" (§2.15) without opening a side channel.
- `my_role()` is also `security definer` so it can read `profiles` regardless of the caller's own row-level access.
- RLS is enabled on all 20 tables that exist after these migrations (not just the sample list PHASE0 spelled out), including `serial_counter`, `product_categories`, `product_types`, `calibres`, `settings_limits`, and `profiles`. Verified locally: with RLS on, a `rahbar`-role user is refused an `insert` into `kirim_orders`, and a `menejer`-role user succeeds — the exact test PHASE0 Part F asks for.
- `audit_log` SELECT is restricted to `rahbar` (not "any authenticated user") since it's raw compliance/oversight data with no operational screen reading it directly; every other operational table keeps the broad "any authenticated user can read" policy PHASE0 used, since Kuzatuv/traceability need cross-role visibility.
- Added `created_by uuid references profiles` to `gate_weighings` for consistency with the other operational tables (`kirim_orders`, `chiqim_requests`, etc. all record who created the row) — PHASE0's sample SQL omitted it, likely an oversight.
- SPEC §8's `USER_PREFS` (user_id, language) was **not** created as a separate table — `profiles.language` (from PHASE0's B1) already satisfies §2.8's per-user Uz/Ru toggle, and a second table would just be a duplicate write target.
- Smoke-tested all 7 migrations against a real local Postgres 16 instance (not just reviewed): they apply cleanly in order, `next_serial()` returns `DDMMYY-NNN` using Tashkent's date, `net_kg` computes as a generated column and can't be overridden by an insert, and the RLS refusal/success behavior above was verified with actual role-switching.

## 2026-07-12 — Auth method: phone number, not email
**Context:** BATU has no SMS provider budget and no real inboxes for staff logins — an email-based flow (verification links, password reset) doesn't work for a warehouse/gate/lab workforce logging in by phone.
**Decision:**
- Login screen collects **phone number + password**. Under the hood this is still Supabase email/password auth: the phone is converted to a synthetic address `<digits>@batu.local` (see `src/lib/phoneAuth.ts`, shared by the login screen and the admin function) before calling `signInWithPassword` / `createUser`. No SMS provider, no per-login cost.
- **Consequence:** Supabase's built-in "forgot password" (magic link to a real inbox) is unusable — there is no inbox behind `@batu.local`. No self-service signup or forgot-password UI was built; public signup stays disabled (Supabase Auth setting, outside this repo). The login screen shows a static "contact Rahbar" hint instead.
- Replacement: a Supabase Edge Function (`supabase/functions/admin-users`) using the `service_role` key, is the only way to create a user or reset a password. It checks the caller's own JWT, looks up their `profiles.role`, and returns 403 unless it is `rahbar` and `active` — enforced in the function itself, not just by hiding the "Foydalanuvchilar" screen (§2.12's server-side-enforcement principle, applied to admin actions too).
  - `create_user`: `{ phone, password, role, full_name }` → `auth.admin.createUser` + matching `profiles` insert (with the new `profiles.phone` column added in `0008_profiles_phone.sql`, used to look users up by the number they actually log in with). If the `profiles` insert fails, the orphaned auth user is deleted so a retry with the same phone doesn't collide — this is an admin API cleanup of Supabase's own `auth.users`, not a `DELETE` against any of our operational tables, so it doesn't break the "never DELETE, only void" house rule (§2.15).
  - `reset_password`: `{ phone, new_password }` → looks up the id by `profiles.phone`, then `auth.admin.updateUserById`.
- Added a **"Foydalanuvchilar"** nav item + screen (`src/pages/admin/UsersAdminPage.tsx`), visible only when `profile.role === 'rahbar'`, with the two forms above calling the Edge Function via `supabase.functions.invoke`.
- This is the first role-gated screen, so `App.tsx`/`HomePage.tsx` now fetch the caller's `profiles` row (`useProfile` hook) after login. Still no router — the rahbar's home/users toggle is local `useState`, same reasoning as the earlier "no router yet" decision. Full per-role home screens and a route guard are still deferred to the dedicated auth/roles step.

## 2026-07-12 — Routing: react-router-dom, one route tree per role
**Context:** Implementing per-role home screens (SPEC §1.1) and a route guard, now that there's more than one screen (`HomePage` + the rahbar-only Foydalanuvchilar admin page). The earlier "no router yet" decision was explicitly scoped to "revisit when more than one component needs session state" — this is that point.
**Decision:**
- Reintroduced `react-router-dom`. `App.tsx` now wraps everything in `AuthProvider` (a small context wrapping `useSession` + `useProfile` so both are fetched once, not once per page) and a `<Routes>` tree.
- One placeholder home route per role: `/rahbar`, `/menejer`, `/qorovul`, `/ombor`, `/laborator`. `/rahbar` is a nested route (`RahbarLayout` + `Outlet`) so `/rahbar/foydalanuvchilar` (the existing admin screen) shares its header/nav; the other four roles have nothing to nest yet, so they're flat routes for now.
- `RoleRoute` (`src/routes/RoleRoute.tsx`) is the guard: it reads `profile.role` from `useAuth()` and renders `<Navigate to={\`/${profile.role}\`} />` if the current route's `allow` list doesn't include it — e.g. a `qorovul` hitting `/ombor` bounces straight to `/qorovul`. Logged-out users bounce to `/login`.
- `/` and any unmatched path redirect to the caller's own role home (or `/login` if signed out); `/login` itself redirects to the role home if already authenticated, so there's no dead end in either direction.
- 🔒 This client-side guard is a UX nicety, not the security boundary — the actual enforcement is server-side RLS (§2.12, `0007_rls.sql`), which already refuses cross-role writes regardless of what the UI lets you navigate to.
- Extracted the shared header/sign-out chrome all five role pages needed into `src/components/RoleShell.tsx`, and deleted the old single `HomePage.tsx` now that each role has its own page.

## 2026-07-13 — admin-users Edge Function wired up; action names finalized
**Context:** Wiring the Foydalanuvchilar screen to the Edge Function for real instead of leaving it a placeholder.
**Decision:**
- Renamed the function's actions from the earlier `create_user` / `reset_password` to **`create-user`** / **`reset-password`** to match the naming actually specified for this function; nothing else in the codebase referenced the old names, so this was a clean rename.
- `reset-password` now accepts **either** `{ phone, new_password }` or `{ user_id, new_password }` — not phone-only as originally built. The Foydalanuvchilar reset form takes a single "phone or user ID" field and picks which key to send based on whether the input matches a UUID pattern; the function looks up the `profiles` row by phone first only when `user_id` wasn't given directly.
- Re-confirmed the server-side rahbar check is the actual security boundary here, not just the frontend route guard from the previous entry: the function reads the caller's own JWT via `admin.auth.getUser(jwt)`, looks up *their* `profiles.role`, and 403s before looking at the request body at all if it isn't `active` `rahbar` — so hitting the function directly (curl, a modified frontend, another role's session) is refused the same way a UI click would be.
- Verified end-to-end except for the parts that require a live Supabase project (which this sandbox can't reach — see the earlier network-policy note): `npm run build`/`lint` clean, and a headless-browser smoke test confirms the app still boots and renders `/login` with no console errors after the change. The actual create-user / reset-password round trip against real Auth + `profiles` still needs to be clicked through once migrations are applied and a first rahbar account exists.

## 2026-07-13 — Edge Function secret renamed to SERVICE_ROLE_KEY
**Context:** `npx supabase secrets set SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=...` was rejected — the Supabase CLI reserves the `SUPABASE_` prefix for its own auto-injected environment variables and refuses to let you set a custom secret under that prefix.
**Decision:** The service-role secret for `admin-users` is set and read as **`SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`** (no `SUPABASE_` prefix), not `SUPABASE_SERVICE_ROLE_KEY`. Updated `supabase/functions/admin-users/index.ts` accordingly (`Deno.env.get('SERVICE_ROLE_KEY')`). `SUPABASE_URL` is unaffected — that one is one of the platform's own auto-injected vars, not a user-set secret, so it keeps its name.
**Action required outside this repo:** set the secret and redeploy — `npx supabase secrets set SERVICE_ROLE_KEY=<your service_role key>` then `npx supabase functions deploy admin-users`. This sandbox cannot reach `api.supabase.com` (network policy blocks it), so both commands need to be run from a machine with real network access to Supabase.

## 2026-07-13 — CORS headers on admin-users
**Context:** The browser was blocking the call from the Foydalanuvchilar screen — `supabase.functions.invoke` sends a CORS preflight (`OPTIONS`) before the real `POST`, and the function had no CORS handling at all, so the preflight got a plain 404/405 with no `Access-Control-Allow-Origin` and the browser refused to even attempt the POST.
**Decision:**
- Added a shared `CORS_HEADERS` object (`Access-Control-Allow-Origin: *`, `Access-Control-Allow-Headers: authorization, content-type, apikey, x-client-info`, `Access-Control-Allow-Methods: POST, OPTIONS`) and an explicit `OPTIONS` branch at the top of `Deno.serve` returning `204` with just those headers, no body.
- Routed **every** other response — success and every error path (401 missing/invalid session, 403 non-rahbar, 400 validation, 404 not found, 405 wrong method) — through the existing `json()` helper, and added `...CORS_HEADERS` to the headers it sets. Because every `return` in the function goes through `json()` (or the new OPTIONS branch), there's no code path that can respond without CORS headers — including the 403 rahbar-check rejection, which is exactly the kind of error response that's easy to forget when only the "happy path" gets CORS treatment.
- `apikey` and `x-client-info` are included in `Access-Control-Allow-Headers` alongside `authorization`/`content-type` because the supabase-js client sends those on every request by default; leaving them out would have caused the same preflight failure for a different header.
**Action required outside this repo:** redeploy — `npx supabase functions deploy admin-users`. Same network caveat as above: this sandbox can't reach Supabase to do it directly.

## 2026-07-13 — Temporary diagnostic markers (OPTIONS still 405ing after redeploy + --no-verify-jwt)
**Context:** After redeploying with `--no-verify-jwt`, `curl -X OPTIONS` against the function still returned the function's own `{"error":"Method not allowed"}` (the 405 body from `json()`), even though `if (req.method === 'OPTIONS')` is the literal first statement in `Deno.serve` — there is nothing in this file that runs before it and could reject the request first. That points at the deployed bundle not matching this file (wrong linked project, a deploy that silently didn't take, etc.) rather than a logic bug in the handler.
**Decision:** Added temporary, clearly-marked diagnostic code (search `TEMPORARY DIAGNOSTIC` to find/remove it later):
- A `DIAG_VERSION` string logged once at module load (`console.log`, so it shows up in `supabase functions logs admin-users` even for requests that never reach the handler at all).
- The same marker echoed as an `X-Admin-Users-Diag` response header on **every** response (added to `CORS_HEADERS`, which both `json()` and the OPTIONS branch already use) — so `curl -i` shows it directly without needing log access.
- A `console.log` as the literal first line inside `Deno.serve`, before the OPTIONS check, logging method + URL + the version string.
If `curl -i -X OPTIONS <url>` still comes back without `X-Admin-Users-Diag` after redeploying this version, the request is not reaching this function's code at all — the problem is upstream (project link, deploy target, routing), not in this file. If the header *is* present but still 405, the bug is genuinely inside this handler and needs a different fix. Remove this block once the real CORS behavior is confirmed working.

## 2026-07-13 — Supabase client exposed on window in dev, for manual RLS testing
**Context:** Needed a fast way to run ad-hoc `supabase.from(...).insert(...)` / `.select(...)` calls from the browser console — signed in as whatever role is currently logged in — to manually confirm RLS actually refuses/allows what §2.12 and `0007_rls.sql` say it should, without writing a throwaway test harness for it.
**Decision:** In `src/lib/supabase.ts`, added:
```ts
if (import.meta.env.DEV) {
  (window as unknown as { supabase: typeof supabase }).supabase = supabase
}
```
right after the client is created, marked `TEMPORARY DIAGNOSTIC` (search that string to find/remove it later, same convention as the Edge Function markers above). `import.meta.env.DEV` is a Vite build-time constant, so this isn't just hidden behind a runtime check — verified the production build (`npm run build`) contains **zero** trace of `window.supabase` or the `DEV` branch (Vite dead-code-eliminates it entirely), and separately confirmed in a running dev server that `window.supabase.from` is actually callable. Nothing here changes what the anon-key client is allowed to do — RLS is still the only thing standing between this console access and the database, which is the whole point of exposing it this way rather than, say, a debug-only service-role shortcut.

## 2026-07-13 — Layout bug: shared main content had no consistent alignment
**Context:** Every page looked like content was "pushed far to the right with a large empty gap on the left" on wide screens. Confirmed visually (screenshotted at 1280px and 1920px, bypassing the auth guard temporarily to render each role page) rather than guessing from source: the header bar (`RoleShell`) is left-aligned (`px-4`), but every page's body content was independently centered in the *full viewport width* — the four placeholder pages used `flex items-center justify-center ... text-center` on a full-width div, and `UsersAdminPage` separately used `mx-auto max-w-xl`. Two different ad hoc centering strategies, neither anchored to the header's left edge, is why it was a shared-layout bug and not a per-page one.
**Decision:** Fixed it once, in `RoleShell.tsx`, instead of patching each page:
- `<main>` now has `mx-auto max-w-5xl px-4 py-8` — one consistent inset (matching the header's `px-4`) and a sane max width, so content starts flush under the header's left edge on any screen size instead of floating wherever each page's own wrapper happened to center it.
- Removed the per-page `flex items-center justify-center ... text-center` wrapper from all five placeholder home pages (`RahbarHome`, `MenejerHome`, `QorovulHome`, `OmborHome`, `LaboratorHome`) — they now just render their placeholder `<p>` directly, letting `RoleShell`'s container handle positioning.
- Removed `UsersAdminPage`'s own `mx-auto max-w-xl px-4 py-8` outer wrapper (which duplicated/fought the shared one) down to just `max-w-xl space-y-8`, so its forms sit at the same left edge as every other page instead of narrower-and-centered-within-centered.
- Verified across pages, not just one: screenshotted `rahbar`, `rahbar/foydalanuvchilar`, `menejer`, `qorovul`, `ombor`, and `laborator` at both 1280px and 1920px viewports (via a temporary unguarded `/_debug/*` route added only for this check and reverted before committing — auth isn't reachable from this sandbox, so this was the only way to actually see the rendered pages instead of trusting the Tailwind classes by eye). All six now align flush-left under the header at both widths.

## 2026-07-13 — Diagnostic cleanup
**Context:** Both temporary diagnostics from the CORS/RLS debugging session had served their purpose and needed cleaning up before they became permanent clutter (or, in the Edge Function's case, permanently-served debug headers).
**Decision:**
- `supabase/functions/admin-users/index.ts`: removed `DIAG_VERSION`, its module-load `console.log`, the `X-Admin-Users-Diag` response header, and the entry-point `console.log` — the function is back to exactly the CORS-fix version from the earlier entry, nothing else changed.
- `src/lib/supabase.ts`: kept the `window.supabase` exposure rather than deleting it, since it's already gated behind `import.meta.env.DEV` — a Vite build-time constant, not a runtime check — and was already verified to be fully absent from the production bundle. Reworded the comment (dropped "TEMPORARY DIAGNOSTIC — remove once...") since this is staying as a permanent dev-only debugging convenience, not something waiting to be deleted. Re-verified after this pass: `npm run build` output still has zero occurrences of `window.supabase`.
**Action required outside this repo:** redeploy — `npx supabase functions deploy admin-users`. Same network caveat as every other Edge Function change in this log: this sandbox can't reach Supabase to do it directly.

## 2026-07-14 — Serial is per type-line, not per truck
**Problem:** a serial was defined as one-per-truck. A multi-type delivery (e.g. one truck carrying Subxon + Isfara) therefore shared a single Barcode #1, a single lab result, and a single `STORAGE_STOCK` row across two different products — silently applying one type's moisture/SO₂ reading to another, and making per-type traceability impossible. Three existing rules (Barcode #1 per type-pile, Laborator's one-sample-per-serial, `STORAGE_STOCK` keyed by serial) were only *approximately* true because of this — they described what should happen per type, while the data model only tracked per truck.
**Decision:** mint one serial per type line, not one per truck. `next_serial()` is now called once per KIRIM type row, not once per KIRIM order. A serial is therefore single-type **by construction** — the three rules above go from approximate to actually correct.
**Rejected alternative:** keep one serial per truck and apportion the gate's net weight pro-rata across the truck's types. Rejected because it invents a weight nobody measured — and the storage manager physically separates the piles into their own stacks anyway when unloading, so the real per-type number is available for free instead of being estimated.
**What changes:**
- **Manager (§3.1):** a KIRIM order is now a *delivery envelope* (one truck-trip); each type row on it mints its own serial. The quantities on the form are the manager's **declared** figures — never overwritten.
- **Storage (§5.1):** enters the **actual** measured weight per serial while unloading, and does so against a form that always shows the matching declared figure next to it (Seriya · Tur · Buyurtma (kutilgan) · Aniq), with live variance and a "Kam chiqdi" flag — so a shortfall is caught on the floor during unloading, while the pile is in front of him, rather than surfacing later in a report. Prints Barcode #1 per serial.
- **Laborator (§5.5):** "one sample → whole parent serial" is now genuinely correct, since the parent serial can no longer span more than one type.
**Does NOT change:** Qorovul's workflow. He still weighs one truck, twice — one Гружёный, one Пустой, one net — regardless of how many types/serials are on it. Multi-serial trips are display-only at the gate.
**Consequence:** `GATE_WEIGHINGS.ref` now points at the trip (`order_id` for KIRIM / `request_id` for CHIQIM), never at a serial — one weighing belongs to a truck-trip, not to any single type on it. The gate's net is reconciled against the manager's declared **Jami avto** (truck total vs. truck total), not split across serials. Declared (manager, §3.1) and actual (storage, §5.1) are separate persisted quantities; their gap is what "Kam chiqdi" means, and it is a finding to be recorded, never a number to be corrected away.

## 2026-07-14 — Phase 1 Step 1: KIRIM_ORDERS/KIRIM_LINES migrated to v1.9; discovered a bigger FK ripple than scoped
**Context:** Building the Menejer's KIRIM tab against the v1.9 schema (previous entry). Phase 0's `kirim_orders`/`kirim_lines` still had the old one-serial-per-truck shape (serial lived on `kirim_orders`), with no application built against them and no real data — so `0009_kirim_serial_per_type.sql` drops and recreates both tables in the new shape rather than migrating data.
**Discovered while migrating, not anticipated by the task scope:** the task said "GATE_WEIGHINGS changes — not touched by this step," but the actual dependency graph is much wider. Six tables (`gate_weighings`, `storage_intake`, `moyka_sends`, `finished_pallets`, `wash_cycles`, `lab_results`) all carry a `serial` column with a foreign key to `kirim_orders(serial)`, and the `v_serial_balance` view is built entirely on `kirim_orders.serial` as its join anchor. Once `serial` moves off `kirim_orders`, none of that is satisfiable as written — this isn't optional cleanup, the migration cannot run at all otherwise (Postgres refuses to drop a column that six FKs and a view depend on).
**Decision — minimal fix only, most of it deliberately not done here:**
- Dropped `v_serial_balance` outright (its definition is invalid the moment `kirim_orders.serial` is gone) and dropped the six now-unsatisfiable FK *constraints*. The six tables keep their `serial` **column** — just unconstrained for now — nothing about their shape or behavior otherwise changed.
- Did **not** re-point those FKs at `kirim_lines(serial)` and did **not** rebuild the view. That's real design/implementation work belonging to Gate (§4), Storage §5.1, Laborator (§5.5), and Kuzatuv (§3.4) respectively — none of which are in scope for this step, per the task's explicit instructions and its own "GATE_WEIGHINGS not touched" carve-out extended to the same principle for the other five.
- **Flagging this loudly rather than silently fixing it**, matching the same policy used for the SPEC v1.9 doc scan: whoever builds those next steps needs to know `storage_intake.serial`, `moyka_sends.serial`, `finished_pallets.serial`, `wash_cycles.serial`, `lab_results.serial`, and `gate_weighings.serial` are currently **not** FK-enforced against anything, and `v_serial_balance` does not exist at all until it's rebuilt against `kirim_lines`.
**Also added, as necessary supporting infrastructure (not scope creep):** a `kirim-photos` Supabase Storage bucket + RLS policies (`0010_kirim_photos_bucket.sql`), since `doc_photo` is documented as "storage path" and the KIRIM form's Hujjat rasmi field is explicitly required for this step — no bucket existed anywhere in the project yet. Same read-all/menejer-writes shape as every other RLS policy in this schema. Could not be verified locally (this sandbox's Postgres has no `storage` schema — that only exists on an actual Supabase project), unlike every other change in this migration, which was verified end-to-end against a real local Postgres instance: all four SQL statements types (drop view, drop constraints, drop/recreate tables, RLS policies) applied cleanly in order; a two-type order produced two distinct serials referencing the same `order_id`; a `menejer` insert succeeded and a `qorovul` insert was refused with SQLSTATE `42501`, both against the new table shape.
**UI scope note:** `declared_qty`/status display in the live order list shows the *order's* status next to each line, not a per-line status — `kirim_lines` in the required v1.9 schema has no status column of its own (status lives on `kirim_orders`); nothing in §8 v1.9 suggested adding one, so nothing was added.

## 2026-07-14 — Phase 1 Step 2: Qorovul KIRIM gate; gate_weighings finished migrating to v1.9
**Context:** Building Qorovul's KIRIM two-stage weighing tab. The task asked to add `order_id` to `gate_weighings` and treat `request_id` as "unconstrained for now (chiqim_requests doesn't exist yet)."
**Correction to the task's assumption, found by inspecting the live table first (as instructed) rather than trusting the prompt:** `chiqim_requests` already exists — it was created in Phase 0's `0003_operational.sql` and never removed — and `gate_weighings.request_id` already had a working FK to it. So `request_id` needed no change at all; only `order_id` was new. `net_kg` was also already a generated column, and RLS on `gate_weighings` already exactly matched the required pattern (read-all select, qorovul insert, qorovul update). The only real gap was the old `serial` column (unconstrained since the previous entry's migration) and its check constraint, which referenced a column that no longer means anything under v1.9.
**Decision (`0011_gate_weighings_order_id.sql`):** added `order_id` (FK → `kirim_orders`), replaced the old `serial`-based check constraint with `num_nonnulls(order_id, request_id) = 1` (a weighing belongs to exactly one trip, KIRIM or CHIQIM, never both, never neither), dropped `serial`.
**Status flip (`0013_gate_weighings_complete_kirim.sql`):** `kirim_orders.status` flips `kutilmoqda → qabul_qilindi` via a `security definer` trigger on `gate_weighings`, firing only when `completed_at` transitions from null to set on a `kirim`-direction row. This has to be a trigger, not a client-side update: `qorovul` has no write policy on `kirim_orders` at all (by design, per §2.15 — only `menejer` may insert there), so the app itself is structurally incapable of flipping this status from anywhere except stage-2 completion. Same established pattern as `next_serial()`/`my_role()`.
**Storage (`0012_gate_photos_bucket.sql`):** a `gate-photos` bucket, same read-all/role-writes shape as `kirim-photos`, for the plate photo + two tarozi photos.
**How this was verified — directly against the live project, not a local sandbox:** a Supabase MCP connection became available this session, letting the migrations be applied and tested against the real project (`qohoqbapevrcjqxbstxi`) rather than a disposable local Postgres — confirmed with the user first, since applying schema changes to a live project is not something to do silently. Real results, not simulated: `menejer` insert into `gate_weighings` refused with `42501`; `qorovul` stage-1 insert succeeds; stage-2 update on the same row returns `net_kg = 8000` (12000 − 4000) computed by Postgres, never sent by the client; `kirim_orders.status` reads `kutilmoqda` immediately after stage 1 and `qabul_qilindi` immediately after stage 2, with no code anywhere but the trigger touching that column. This leaves the one pre-existing test order (plate `01test888b`) now completed in the live data — flagged to the user in case they want it reset before their own testing pass.
**Security advisor finding, checked rather than dismissed:** `get_advisors` flagged `complete_kirim_stage2()` as a `SECURITY DEFINER` function publicly callable via `/rest/v1/rpc/complete_kirim_stage2`. Verified directly (`select complete_kirim_stage2();`) that Postgres refuses this outright — `0A000: trigger functions can only be called as triggers` — since it's a `RETURNS TRIGGER` function, not a normal callable one. This is a generic-linter false positive for trigger functions specifically (the same warning category already existed for `my_role()`/`next_serial()`, which genuinely are callable, from Phase 0); not a real hole, but worth recording rather than silently waving off an advisor warning.
**Bug found and fixed in this step's own new code, not pre-existing:** `useKirimTrips`'s data-loading function had no error handling — if its `Promise.all` ever rejected, `setLoading(false)` would never run and the whole tab would stay blank forever. Wrapped in `try/finally`. Caught this because this sandbox's network proxy causes Supabase requests to hang rather than fail promptly, which happened to be exactly the failure mode this bug needed to manifest — confirmed the fix is correct, though a hang (vs. a reject) still can't resolve on its own; that's expected on a live project with real connectivity, not a further bug to chase. Noted for awareness, not fixed (out of scope, already-shipped code): `useOwners`/`useProductTypes`/`KirimOrdersList` from Phase 1 Step 1 have the identical unguarded `.then()` pattern and would have the same latent issue.

## 2026-07-15 — Fixed the flagged KirimOrdersList loading-state bug
**Context:** The previous entry flagged, but deliberately didn't fix, the same stuck-loading pattern in `KirimOrdersList.tsx` (and `useOwners`/`useProductTypes`) as out of scope for that PR. This entry closes that out for `KirimOrdersList.tsx` specifically, as its own small isolated fix.
**Decision:** Rewrote the effect's bare `.then(({ data }) => {...})` (no error handling — a rejected promise would skip `setLoading(false)` entirely and leave the screen blank forever) as an `async` function wrapped in `try/finally`, same pattern as `useKirimTrips.refresh()`. Captured `profile.id` into a local `profileId` before defining the nested `load()` function rather than reaching into `profile.id` from inside it — TypeScript's control-flow narrowing from the earlier `if (!profile) return` guard doesn't carry into a separately-defined nested function, so referencing `profile.id` directly inside `load()` failed to typecheck (`'profile' is possibly 'null'`); capturing the already-narrowed value avoids a non-null assertion.
**Not touched:** `useOwners.ts` and `useProductTypes.ts` still have the same latent pattern — still flagged, not in scope for this fix either (this PR is scoped to `KirimOrdersList.tsx` only, per the task).

## 2026-07-15 — Storage §1 intake: dropped trip-level reconciliation; declared-vs-actual + Barcode #1
**Context:** Building Storage's KIRIM intake screen. This step carried two explicit product-decision revisions to what §5.1's prose previously said, both now reflected inline in `SPEC.md` §5.1 (not silently contradicted) and recorded here.
**Revision 1 — dropped the trip-level reconciliation.** §5.1 previously described *two* reconciliations: (a) sum of storage's per-serial entries vs. the gate's truck-level net, and (b) each serial's entry vs. its declared qty. (a) is dropped entirely. Rationale: storage's job is to check and receive raw product; his per-type entries sum to the gate total *by definition* (there's nowhere else for the weight to go), so counter-checking them adds no information — it would just be re-deriving a number that's already guaranteed to match. Only (b), the per-serial declared-vs-actual check, remains. The gate's figures are still visible on demand, in the full-story detail view (item 5) — reference only, not something storage reconciles against.
**Revision 2 — acceptance no longer waits for gate stage 2.** §5.1 previously said storage "arrives pre-filled after gate Yakunlandi" (i.e., after both weighings). Now: a trip is *visible* to storage the moment the manager submits the KIRIM order (read-only, no accept button — lets storage see what's coming), and becomes *acceptable* the moment gate **stage 1** exists (`gruzheny_kg` set), not waiting for stage 2/net weight. Matches how trucks actually move on the floor: a truck can be weighed in, then go unload at storage, before it's weighed out empty on the way back through the gate later. Storage does not need the net weight to do his job — he's measuring the pile in front of him, not reconciling against the gate (revision 1).
**Schema — inspected before assuming, same discipline as Steps 1–2, though this session had no live DB/MCP access (see "no live access" note below):** the migration files (last confirmed live as of Step 2's PR) show Phase 0's `storage_intake` table (`0004_storage.sql`) has only `serial` (PK), `confirmed_at`, `pile_photo`, `barcode1`, `confirmed_by` — no `actual_qty`/`status`/`komment`/`namligi`/`sulfur` ever existed, even though §8's own STORAGE_STOCK pseudocode listed them from the start. Same FK ripple as `gate_weighings` in Step 2: its FK to `kirim_orders(serial)` was dropped in `0009` (kirim_orders no longer has a serial) and never re-pointed — `0014_storage_intake_v1_9.sql` re-points it at `kirim_lines(serial)` and adds the missing columns. RLS on `storage_intake` already matched the required pattern exactly (read-all, `ombor` insert/update) from Phase 0 — nothing to change there.
**Barcode #1 value — had to interpret an underspecified format.** §2.2's table gives Barcode #2 an explicit ID format (`PLT-<serial>-<calibre>`) but lists Barcode #1's ID format as literally "—". Read this as: unlike a pallet (a new entity distinct from its serial, needing a derived ID), a serial is *already* a stable, globally unique, human-readable identifier — so Barcode #1's value is simply the serial itself, stored explicitly in `barcode1` at accept time (never recomputed on later views, satisfying "generate-once"). The "Encodes: serial + turi + egasi + sana" row is what's *displayed alongside* the code (joined from `kirim_lines`/`kirim_orders`/`owners` at render time), not packed into the stored value.
**Duplication flagged, not resolved:** `storage_intake.moisture_pct`/`so2_mg_kg` (added per this step's explicit instruction, left null, Laborator's job) duplicate fields that already exist for exactly this purpose on `lab_results` (from Phase 0, designed for "one sample → whole parent serial"). Whoever builds Laborator (§5.5) needs to resolve whether `storage_intake`'s copy is denormalized/synced from `lab_results`, or whether one of the two should be dropped — not decided here.
**New config key:** `settings_limits.kam_chiqdi_pct` (default 5) — §2.14 lists three thresholds (sulfur-overdue, Moyka-idle, abnormal-loss), none of which is the declared-vs-actual shortfall this step needed; added as a fourth, same shape as the others.
**Verification, in two passes.** This session initially had no live DB/MCP access (the connection from Step 2's session wasn't available, and this sandbox's direct network to `*.supabase.co` is still blocked) — `0014`/`0015` were first verified end-to-end against a disposable local Postgres only: all 15 migrations (0001–0015) apply cleanly in order; a two-type order → two independent serials; gate stage-1-only (no stage 2) correctly leaves a row with `gruzheny_kg` set and `pustoy_kg`/`completed_at` null; `ombor` insert into `storage_intake` succeeds with `barcode1` = serial and `moisture_pct`/`so2_mg_kg` null; `menejer` insert refused with `42501`; the new FK genuinely rejects a nonexistent serial (`23503`).

The Supabase MCP connection then became available later in the same review cycle. Applied `0014`/`0015` to the live project (`qohoqbapevrcjqxbstxi`) and re-ran the identical test against real data — not a repeat of the local result, an independent confirmation against the actual schema and actual RLS: created a fresh KIRIM order + line (serial `150726-001`) as `menejer`; ran gate stage 1 only as `qorovul` (`gruzheny_kg=12000`, `pustoy_kg`/`completed_at` both null) and confirmed `kirim_orders.status` was still `kutilmoqda` at that point — proving storage's "acceptable" tier genuinely has to check `gate_weighings.gruzheny_kg` directly, it cannot rely on order status; accepted at storage as `ombor` with a real shortfall (declared 3000, actual 2700, −10%, above the 5% threshold) — succeeded, `status='skladda_turibdi'`, `barcode1='150726-001'`, `moisture_pct`/`so2_mg_kg` null, proving both "never blocks" and that acceptance has no dependency on the gate net (none existed yet for this trip); `menejer` and `qorovul` both refused inserting into `storage_intake` with `42501`; a nonexistent serial refused with `23503`. Security advisors showed no new warnings beyond the pre-existing set already reviewed in Step 2.

This leaves real test rows in the live database: order `712baa80…` (plate `03Step3Test`) and its `storage_intake` row (serial `150726-001`) — left in place, flagged to the user, not deleted (same policy as Step 2's leftover test order).

## 2026-07-15 — Barcode #1 rendered as a real Code128 label PNG + share-to-printer (Phase 2 partial)
**Context:** Step 3 shipped Barcode #1 as on-screen *text only* (the serial in a monospace box) — not scannable. This step turns it into a real Code128 barcode and adds a print/share action, per SPEC §2.2/§5.1 and PHASE0.md Part E (the JsBarcode + Web Share pattern). **No schema change** — the stored `storage_intake.barcode1` value is still the serial itself, exactly as Step 3 decided; only the *rendering* changed. No migration, nothing to apply live.
**Library — JsBarcode, not bwip-js.** JsBarcode is what PHASE0.md Part E explicitly names, it's lightweight (~50KB), and renders Code128 straight to a canvas/SVG. bwip-js supports dozens of symbologies we don't need and is heavier — no reason to take it for a single Code128 use. Removed the separately-installed `@types/jsbarcode`: JsBarcode ships its own `jsbarcode.d.ts` and the DefinitelyTyped package would just be a second, drifting source of truth (verified the bundled types resolve via `npm run build`).
**Label geometry, documented in `src/lib/barcodeLabel.ts`:** Detonger P1 is 203dpi → 203/25.4 = 7.992 dots/mm → a 50×30mm label is 400×240 native dots. The PNG is exported at a **2× integer supersample (800×480)** so WePrint downsamples cleanly back onto the 400×240 grid without fractional resampling that would misalign barcode modules and hurt scannability; 2× also gives better text/edge quality than rendering at native 400×240. Module (narrowest bar) width is 2px×2 = 0.25mm at native res — comfortably above the ~0.19mm Code128 floor for a 203dpi head. **50×30mm is hardcoded** with a `TODO(config)` comment: rolls range 20–55mm and this should become an Administration setting later, but the config UI is explicitly out of scope this step.
**Label content** (task's field list, which correctly *overrides* PHASE0.md Part E — that doc listed "calibre" for Barcode #1, but calibre is a Barcode #2 / finished-pallet concept; a raw serial isn't graded yet): Code128 bars, then the serial large and human-readable directly under the bars (standard barcode convention), then four small lines in order — **Tur · Buyurtmachi · Og'irlik · Sana**, nothing else. "Og'irlik" uses the storage `actual_qty` for that serial. "Sana" uses the **order/delivery date** (`kirim_orders.order_date`), matching §2.2's "sana" in the KIRIM context (the date the goods arrived) — not the intake timestamp. Overlong fields ellipsize rather than shrink, keeping text legible ("larger over more", per the task).
**Share + fallback.** "Chop etish / Ulashish" uses `navigator.share({ files })`, but **feature-detects with `navigator.canShare({ files })` first** — some browsers expose `navigator.share` yet can't share files, so a bare `typeof navigator.share` check isn't enough. When file-sharing is unavailable it falls through to a PNG download; there's also an always-present explicit "Yuklab olish" (download) button. The on-screen scannable bars stay visible too (readable off the screen in a pinch). A dismissed share sheet (`AbortError`) is treated as a no-op, not an error.
**Verification.** The sandbox Chromium has neither `navigator.share`/`canShare` nor the native `BarcodeDetector`, so: (1) drove the real `Barcode1Display` component via a temp debug route — confirmed the SVG renders real `<rect>` bars (70 across two labels), not text; (2) generated the actual composed label PNG and decoded it with a real Code128 decoder (`@zxing/library`, added test-only then removed) — **both serials round-tripped exactly**: `150726-001` → "150726-001", `150726-002` → "150726-002", format CODE_128, confirming the two-type-truck case yields two distinct correctly-encoded labels; (3) confirmed the share button, with sharing unsupported, correctly falls through to a valid PNG download (PNG magic bytes verified, filename `<serial>.png`); (4) visually confirmed the 800×480 label is legible with all four fields + serial + bars. Both real call sites (`OmborIntakeTab` second-window button, `IntakeDetailView` full-story) construct the identical `Barcode1LabelData` shape passed to the verified component (enforced by the type checker).
**Bundle note:** JsBarcode pushes the main chunk over Vite's 500KB advisory threshold (475→542KB). Left as a static import rather than lazy-loading it — a one-time cached load in a PWA, and code-splitting was out of scope; flagged here in case it's worth revisiting when Barcode #2 also needs rendering.

## 2026-07-15 — Phase 1 Step 4: Hisobotlar (history) + top-tab nav for Qorovul & Ombor
**Context:** Both Qorovul and Ombor needed a read-only, filterable history of their own past entries, plus top-tab navigation (their single operational screen becomes one tab, Hisobotlar a second). Built to be *extended* for Laborator later (Phase 4), not rebuilt.
**Nav pattern — route-based, matching Rahbar.** The project already had two per-role patterns: Rahbar uses route-based nav (`NavLink` + `Outlet` + nested routes in App.tsx), Qorovul/Ombor were flat single routes. Per "match however the project already structures per-role screens," I converted QorovulHome/OmborHome into layouts (RoleShell + tabs in the header `nav` slot + `<Outlet/>`) with nested routes — the index route is the operational tab, `hisobotlar` the second. Adding a future tab (Qorovul CHIQIM; Ombor Moyka/finished/dispatch) is one `RoleTab` entry + one nested `<Route>`. Extracted the shared tab bar into `RoleTabs` (the same NavLink pattern RahbarLayout already used; left RahbarLayout untouched to avoid scope creep). State is intentionally not preserved across tabs (route-based, same as Rahbar) — expected, not a bug.
**Reusable shell, role-specific hooks (not a generic framework).** `HistoryView` is a small presentational shell (filter-bar slot + results slot + empty/loading states + result count); each role plugs in its own filter controls, data hook, and row rendering. This is the piece Laborator's Hisobotlar reuses later — a new role adds filters + a hook + rows, not a new shell. Deliberately did **not** build a generic table/column framework (task warned against over-engineering).
**Schema realities drove two different hooks:**
- **`useIntakeHistory` (Ombor):** `storage_intake` has its own `confirmed_at` timestamp, so date range + seriya (ilike) are pushed **server-side** with `.order().limit(200)` — bounds both fetch and render. tur/owner live on joined rows, filtered client-side after enrichment. Rows are shaped as `IntakeLine & { intake }` so the Step 3 **`IntakeDetailView` is reused verbatim** for row-expand (task item 4 — no second detail view). Kam-chiqdi variance uses the same `settings_limits.kam_chiqdi_pct` threshold as Step 3.
- **`useGateHistory` (Qorovul):** queried **direction-agnostically from `gate_weighings`** (embedding BOTH `kirim_orders` and `chiqim_requests` parents) so nothing hardcodes KIRIM — CHIQIM rows just don't exist yet. Derived status per Step 2's design (no stored enum): `completed_at` set → `yakunlandi`, else `kirdi_boshatilmoqda`. Note "kutilmoqda"/awaiting-gate is **not** a gate_weighings state (such trips have no weighing row), so it isn't a filter option — this is the honest outcome of "check the real status source."
**🚩 Schema limitation flagged, NOT fixed (no migration, per task):** `gate_weighings` has **no own timestamp** (only nullable `completed_at`) and a random-uuid PK, so it can't be time-ordered or date-bounded server-side. `useGateHistory` therefore fetches with a hard `.limit(500)` cap and does date filter / sort client-side on the parent trip's sana (`order_date`). Fine for current data volume; if gate history ever grows large this wants a `created_at` on `gate_weighings` (or a parent-anchored query) — a migration, which this step's scope explicitly excluded, so flagged here and in the PR rather than added.
**No RLS/schema change.** Confirmed (not assumed) `read_all` select policies already exist on both `gate_weighings` and `storage_intake` (`0007_rls.sql`) — both views are read-only, no new policy needed. Role isolation (Qorovul only sees gate history, Ombor only storage) is the existing `RoleRoute` guard + route nesting, unchanged — not new RLS.
**Default 30-day date range** (`defaultDateRange` in `lib/dateRange.ts`) so lists don't render unbounded on a phone (task item 6).
**Verification — no live access this session (same as Step 3's session), stated plainly.** No Supabase MCP connected and the sandbox's network to `*.supabase.co` is blocked (403), so live-data testing wasn't possible. Instead: (1) **Local Postgres** seeded with data mirroring the documented live test rows (completed gate trip, stage-1-only trip, two storage intakes with shortfalls) — verified the enrichment joins produce the right shapes, the derived gate status is correct (in-progress vs `yakunlandi` with net=8000 from the generated column), and every filter narrows correctly (gate: status/plate/date; intake: server-side date bound incl. the +1-day inclusive upper edge, seriya ilike, tur, owner; variance −10% flags Kam chiqdi at the 5% threshold, −4% doesn't). (2) **Headless browser** via temp debug routes — confirmed both layouts render their tabs with correct labels + hrefs, the `<Outlet/>` switches child content by URL, each role's filter controls render (Qorovul: date×2+plate+status; Ombor: date×2+seriya+tur/owner), inputs are controlled, the default 30-day range populates, and no console errors. The PostgREST embed itself is validated by-construction (the `gate_weighings→kirim_orders` and `→chiqim_requests` FKs exist). Needs a click-through on the Netlify preview against the real Steps 2-3 data to fully close the loop.

## 2026-07-15 — Phase 1 Step 5: Ombor Moykaga Chiqarish (send raw to washing)
**Context:** Ombor's §5.2 screen — send received raw material to Moyka (washing/production). §5.2's spec text is terse ("Send raw to production; partial sends accumulate; no new barcode (#1 travels). Two-window; send form with live 'qoladi'; ⋯ per-send history; Qaydlar qo'shish."), so several interpretations had to be resolved against the real schema and prior steps.
**(a) Two-window / history interpretation.** Went with **two windows by remaining balance** — "Yuborish uchun" (available > 0; the send form lives here) and "To'liq yuborilgan" (fully sent) — matching the Faol/Yakunlangan two-window pattern from Steps 2-3. The spec's "⋯ per-send history" is a **per-serial expand** within either window (chronological send log + Qaydlar), **not a third window**. Reasoning: a separate history window would duplicate serials already shown by balance; the ⋯ expand is exactly how Step 3's intake and Step 4's history rows already surface per-row detail, so this is the consistent reading.
**(b) How MOYKA_SENDS and WASH_CYCLES actually relate (the flagged ambiguity — resolved, no STOP needed).** Inspected both real tables: `moyka_sends` = (id, serial, wash_cycle default 1, sent_date, qty_kg, created_by); `wash_cycles` = (id, serial, cycle_no, status, final_loss_pct, voided_at). **The real `wash_cycles` has NO `sent_qty`/`received_qty`/`loss_pct` columns** — §8's pseudocode listed them, but Phase 0 never built them. So the schema already fits interpretation (a): `moyka_sends` is the append-only event log, and any running sent-total is **derived by summing it** — there is no stored `sent_qty` to maintain. This step doesn't touch `wash_cycles` at all (it's re-wash infrastructure, §2.13, a later step; all sends here are `wash_cycle` 1). Likewise `storage_intake` has no `sent_to_moyka_qty` column (§8 pseudocode listed it, real table doesn't) — **available balance is derived**: `actual_qty − Σ moyka_sends.qty_kg`, per §2.15 "store events, derive numbers." No stored-balance column was added.
**(c) Notes/Qaydlar — this is the FIRST implementation of the pattern.** The `notes` table (0005) + its append-only RLS (0007: INSERT + SELECT policies, deliberately **no** update/delete policy for anyone, making §2.5 append-only real at the DB) has existed since Phase 0 but was **used nowhere in the UI** until now. Built a reusable `useNotes(entityType, entityId)` hook + `EntityNotes` component (list + "Qaydlar qo'shish" add form, no edit/delete controls by design) against that existing table — Moyka uses `entity_type='moyka'`, `entity_id=serial`. Intended for reuse anywhere notes are needed later.
**Schema change — one migration (`0016_moyka_sends_fk.sql`), the same FK-ripple fix Step 3 applied to storage_intake.** `moyka_sends.serial`'s FK to `kirim_orders(serial)` was dropped in 0009 (when serial moved to kirim_lines) and never re-pointed, leaving it unconstrained text. This step is the first to write Moyka sends, so it re-points the FK to `kirim_lines(serial)` to restore integrity. Nothing else on `moyka_sends` changed (no komment column — Qaydlar uses the `notes` table). RLS was already correct (`read_all` + `ombor_writes`, 0007) — confirmed, not assumed.
**Over-send is blocked (hard), unlike intake's soft Kam-chiqdi warning.** You can't send more raw than is available — a negative balance is nonsensical (there's no discretion, unlike the declared-vs-actual variance at intake which is a real finding to record). The send form blocks submit if qty > available; "Qoladi" is shown live (available − in-progress input) and turns red on over-send.
**No new barcode** anywhere in this flow — Barcode #1 (Step 3) already identifies the serial and conceptually travels with it (§5.2); a send only records an event.
**Verification — no MCP/Supabase network this session (same as Steps 3-4), stated plainly; asked nothing to apply live (nothing was).** Local Postgres, all 16 migrations apply cleanly in order; seeded a received serial (actual 2700) and verified: FK re-point enforces (`23503` on a bad serial); **partial sends accumulate correctly** (send 1000 then 700 → available 2700−1700 = 1000, derived by summing the log); per-send history chronological; `ombor` insert into `moyka_sends` succeeds, `menejer`/`qorovul` refused (RLS, 42501-class); `ombor` note insert succeeds; notes are **append-only** (UPDATE affects 0 rows, DELETE refused, the notes stay intact). Headless browser: `MoykaSendForm` live "Qoladi" (1000→700→0→−200) and over-send blocking verified in isolation; Ombor now shows 3 tabs (Skladga KIRIM · Moykaga Chiqarish · Hisobotlar), no console errors. The Moyka tab's data-loaded rendering (window split, ⋯ expand, notes round-trip) still needs a Netlify-preview click-through against real data — the sandbox browser can't reach Supabase, so the data hooks don't resolve there.

## 2026-07-15 — Phase 1 Step 6: Finished pallet receipt + Barcode #2 (§5.3)
**Context:** Ombor's §5.3 Tayyor Mahsulot tab — receive finished pallets out of Moyka, one pallet per save, each getting a Barcode #2; Tugallash locks the final yield-loss.
**Schema — inspected first (CLAUDE.md), one migration needed.**
- `finished_pallets.serial` AND `wash_cycles.serial` FKs were dropped in 0009 (serial-per-type ripple) and never re-pointed — the last two dangling tables. `0017_finished_wash_fk.sql` re-points both → `kirim_lines(serial)`, same fix as Steps 2/3/5. RLS was already correct on both (`read_all` + `ombor_writes` + `ombor_updates`) — confirmed, not assumed. Verified on local Postgres (bad serial → `23503`).
- **Totals are DERIVED, nothing stored** (CLAUDE.md): Yuborilgan = Σ `moyka_sends.qty_kg` (from Step 5), Qabul qilingan = Σ `finished_pallets.weight_kg` (non-void), Jarayonda = the difference (neutral wording, not "loss" until Tugallash). `wash_cycles` has NO `sent_qty`/`received_qty` columns (§8 pseudocode listed them; Phase 0 never built them) — consistent with deriving.
- **Tugallash** locks the final yield-loss into the existing `wash_cycles.final_loss_pct` with `status='final'` (idempotent upsert on `(serial, cycle_no)`), computed `(sent − received)/sent × 100`. A finalized serial (has a `final` cycle-1 row) leaves the active list = "files to history". No `active` wash_cycles row is created before Tugallash — absence of a `final` row means still-active, which is enough. `wash_cycle` = 1 throughout (re-wash §2.13 is a later step).
**🚩 Spec gap found and resolved (SPEC §2.2 updated inline, not silently): Barcode #2 format needed a per-pallet uniquifier.** §2.2's `PLT-<serial>-<calibre>` collides when a serial yields multiple pallets of the same calibre — which "one sticker per physical pallet" + atomic pallets explicitly allow, and which "partial receipts across multiple saves" (the test plan) requires — because `finished_pallets.barcode2` is the PK. Resolved to **`PLT-<serial>-<calibre>-<seq>`** (`<seq>` = 1-based per serial+calibre; Konditirskiy → `…-KN-<seq>`). Marked/struck the old text in §2.2 and logged here per CLAUDE.md ("if a build reveals the spec text is wrong/superseded, update SPEC.md inline… never contradict silently"). `<seq>` is computed client-side from the already-loaded pallets; the `barcode2` PK is the concurrency backstop (single ombor manager, one-pallet-per-save → collision risk is low; a collision errors and the manager retries). Verified on local Postgres: two K4 pallets → `-04-1`, `-04-2` (no collision), Konditirskiy → `-KN-1`, and re-using a barcode2 fails the PK.
**🚩 `calibres` table is EMPTY on the real project — flagged, not silently seeded.** The receipt form's Kalibr dropdown reads `calibres` (filtered to the serial's category), but the table was never seeded (Administration §6.4 isn't built). Not seeding it in a migration: master data is Administration's domain and the project precedent (Step 1 owners/product_types) is user-seeds-via-SQL. Ready-to-run seed SQL is in the PR. The form shows an explicit "kalibrlar sozlanmagan" message when empty. (Local test DB was seeded with the apricot set incl. Konditirskiy to verify the flow.)
**Reuse (CLAUDE.md).** `barcodeLabel.ts` refactored to a generic `renderLabel(code, fields)` with thin `renderBarcode1Label`/`renderBarcode2Label` wrappers; `Barcode2Display` mirrors `Barcode1Display`'s share/download. **Refactoring the label renderer surfaced a real bug:** Barcode #2's longer `PLT-…` code was being downscaled (nearest-neighbour) to fit 50×30mm, which destroyed the thin bars and made it **fail to decode**. Fixed by choosing the largest integer Code128 module width whose natural barcode fits the label, drawn 1:1 (no rescale). Verified with a real ZXing decoder: Barcode #1 still decodes to the serial (regression intact), and both Barcode #2s decode exactly (`PLT-150726-001-04-1`, `PLT-150726-001-KN-1`). At very large per-serial+calibre pallet counts the seq could lengthen the code further and re-tighten the bars — flagged for if it's ever hit.
**Verification — no MCP/network this session (per CLAUDE.md, said explicitly), nothing applied live.** Local Postgres (17 migrations): FK re-point + `23503`; barcode2 sequencing + Konditirskiy + PK collision backstop; derived totals (sent 2700 / received 1400 / jarayonda 1300); Tugallash yield-loss `48.1%` into `wash_cycles` + finalized-exclusion; RLS ombor-writes succeeds, laborator refused (42501) on both `finished_pallets` and `wash_cycles`. Headless browser + ZXing: both #1 (regression) and #2 labels decode; receipt form generates the right barcode2 for K4 (seq) and Konditirskiy; #2 label visually correct with §2.2's fields. **Still needs:** `supabase db push` of `0017` + a `calibres` seed + a Netlify-preview click-through against real data (the data-loaded tab, Tugallash round-trip, share sheet).

## 2026-07-16 — Tayyor Mahsulot completion (fix on §5.3)
**Context:** Step 6's receipt form (`OmborTayyorTab.tsx` / `FinishedReceiptForm.tsx` / `useMoykaOutput.ts`, all live and merged since 2026-07-15) had a real Storage Manager reachable via MCP re-flag it: the form stayed mounted after every save (never auto-closed, so it read as "auto-reopening" — nothing actually forced it shut except the manual `Yopish` button), `Tugallash` required a manual double-confirm even when the sent amount was exactly or more-than accounted for, and `Jarayonda` (`sent − received`) could go negative with no indication that the batch had been over-received. Fixed all three; SPEC §5.3 updated inline (see the struck text there) rather than silently changed.
**(a) Form now closes on every successful submit, no auto-reopen.** `activeForm` is cleared only after the full save succeeds (pallet insert, plus the conditional auto-finalize upsert below, if either fails the form stays open with the error visible — clearing state before the network call resolves would unmount `FinishedReceiptForm` mid-await and orphan its own error handling). A new entry needs an explicit click on the same button, relabeled **"+ Yana qo'shish"** once at least one pallet exists (still `+ Qabul qilish` for the very first one) — this is the "explicit add-another" the task asked for; no second button was introduced; reusing the existing hide/show toggle was simpler and matches the two-window/toggle idioms already used elsewhere (CLAUDE.md "reuse, don't rebuild"). The last pallet's Barcode #2 (`lastB`) was moved **out of** the `activeForm === serial` block so the sticker stays visible/printable across the auto-close — previously it was only shown while the form was open, which would have made it disappear the instant the fix closed the form.
**(b) No fixed tolerance — cumulative received ≥ sent auto-completes the cycle.** `handleReceipt` computes `newReceived = serial.received + weightKg` right after the insert succeeds; if `newReceived >= serial.sent` it immediately runs the same `wash_cycles` upsert Tugallash already used (`status='final'`, idempotent on `(serial, cycle_no)`) — no confirmation dialog, because once the full sent amount is accounted for there's no ambiguity left to confirm. This reuses the finalize write path instead of duplicating it (extracted into a small `tayyorCompletion.ts` module, `isCycleComplete`/`computeFinalLossPct`, imported by both the auto-path and the manual button). Manual `Tugallash` (double-confirm, unchanged) is kept for the opposite case — closing a serial out **early**, before it will ever reach the sent amount, accepting a real shortfall as the final loss. Once a serial auto-completes it leaves the active list (same "finalized → excluded" mechanism `useMoykaOutput` already had for manual Tugallash), so the manual button is naturally unreachable for it afterward — no extra "stop offering entries" flag was needed.
**(c) Jarayonda floors at 0; overage shows as non-blocking `Ortiqcha`.** `jarayonda(sent, received) = max(0, sent − received)` and a new `excess`/`ortiqcha(sent, received) = max(0, received − sent)` are both derived (CLAUDE.md "derive, don't store" — no new column). When `excess > 0` the UI shows `Ortiqcha: +N kg` next to Jarayonda, amber, non-blocking — same mechanism as `Kam chiqdi` (§5.1, `IntakeAcceptForm.tsx`): a colored, appended flag that never prevents the save. The locked `final_loss_pct` itself is also floored at 0 (`computeFinalLossPct`) — an overage is Ortiqcha, never a negative "loss".
**Reuse.** Extracted the four pure functions (`jarayonda`, `ortiqcha`, `isCycleComplete`, `computeFinalLossPct`) into `src/lib/tayyorCompletion.ts` — dependency-free (no React/Supabase imports), so they're both the single source of truth shared between `useMoykaOutput.ts` (row totals) and `OmborTayyorTab.tsx` (auto-finalize trigger + manual Tugallash), and independently testable without mocking the network.
**Testing.** No test runner existed in the repo (`package.json` had no `test` script, no vitest/jest). Added one (`node --test`, Node 24's built-in runner — no new dependency) plus `src/lib/tayyorCompletion.test.ts`: exact-match (sent=received → complete, 0% loss, 0 jarayonda, 0 ortiqcha), overage (received>sent → complete, loss floors to 0%, jarayonda floors to 0, ortiqcha positive), shortfall (not complete, positive loss/jarayonda, 0 ortiqcha), a boundary case (one kg under vs. exactly at target), and a sent=0 degenerate case (must not divide by zero — can't occur in practice since a serial only appears in Tayyor Mahsulot once it has `moyka_sends`, but the function has to not misbehave if ever called that way). All 6 pass; `tsc -b` clean except the pre-existing, unrelated `jsbarcode` module-resolution error (reproduced on unmodified `main`, not caused by this change — `node_modules` isn't installed in this sandbox).
**🚩 Live/local DB verification NOT done this session — flagged, not silently skipped.** Supabase MCP (which had live access earlier this week — see the Step 6 entry above and the separate live-verification note) returned `403` on every call this session (`get_project`, `list_tables`, `execute_sql` all failed); no local Postgres binaries (`psql`/`initdb`) are available in this sandbox either. Per CLAUDE.md's fallback ("no MCP → disposable local Postgres, say so explicitly, flag live testing still needed") — neither path was available, so this is stated plainly instead of substituted with something that looks like verification. What **is** covered: the pure completion math (all three requirements) via the unit tests above, and a static trace of `handleReceipt`'s ordering (state only clears after both writes succeed) confirming the auto-close race described in (a) doesn't occur. The actual Supabase `insert`/`upsert` calls (RLS, FK, real `wash_cycles` idempotency under the new auto-trigger) were **not** re-exercised against a live or local database — needs a run before merge, same as any other DB-touching change per CLAUDE.md.

## 2026-07-16 — Tugallangan window (Window 2 on §5.3)
**Context:** §5.3's original v1 design (`BATU-Storage-S3-Tayyor-Mahsulot-v1.pdf`) and the two-window pattern already used at §5.1/§5.2/gate weighings both imply a completed-cycles list, but Step 6 and the completion-math fix only ever built the active window — `useMoykaOutput` filtered finalized cycles **out** with no counterpart query, so a finalized serial just vanished. Added Window 2 (Tugallangan) to surface it.
**Extended `useMoykaOutput` instead of a new hook.** It already does the exact join (`kirim_lines` → `kirim_orders` → owner, `product_types`) Window 2 needs, so a second hook would have duplicated three Supabase round-trips for the same data. Refactored the per-serial row builder into a shared `baseRow(serial)` closure used by both the active list and the new `completed` list. **This also fixed a real bug in the old code**, not just added a feature: the early return was `if (activeSerials.length === 0) { setSerials([]); return }` — if *every* sent serial happened to be finalized, this returned before ever computing a completed list (which didn't exist yet, so it was silently correct-by-accident), but it's exactly the kind of bug that would have quietly broken Window 2 the day it shipped if the early-return condition wasn't corrected to `serialList.length === 0` (the true "nothing sent at all" case).
**`CompletedCycle.lossPct` is the LOCKED `wash_cycles.final_loss_pct`, not recomputed** — it's the one place in this feature that intentionally reads a stored figure instead of deriving it, because that's the whole point of Tugallash: the yield-loss is locked at finalize time and shouldn't drift if, hypothetically, more `finished_pallets` rows were ever added after finalization (they shouldn't be, but the row's own historical figure is what "locked" means). `sent`, `received`, and `excess` (Ortiqcha) stay derived as always.
**Badge logic extracted as a pure function, not inline JSX.** `completionBadge(lossPct, excess)` in `tayyorCompletion.ts` returns a `{kind:'ortiqcha', excessKg}` or `{kind:'loss', pct}` discriminated union; **Ortiqcha always wins when `excess > 0`**, regardless of what `lossPct` says — because exact-match and overage both lock `final_loss_pct` at 0 (floored, per the prior fix), the only thing that distinguishes them is `excess`. The component just renders whichever kind it's handed. Pulling this out of JSX made it directly unit-testable instead of needing a DOM/render harness.
**Reused, not duplicated, the pallet list.** Extracted Window 1's inline pallet `<ul>` (barcode2 · kalibr · og'irlik · reprintable `Barcode2Display`) into a shared `palletList(serial, typeId, ownerId, pallets)` function used by both windows — Window 2's requirement ("reuse Window 1 pallet-list pattern") was literal, not just similar-looking.
**Row field order intentionally differs from Window 1.** The task specified "serial, owner · type" for Window 2, vs. Window 1's existing "serial, type · owner" — kept as specified rather than "fixing" it to match, since nothing indicated the mismatch was a bug and unifying it wasn't in scope.
**Testing.** Added three tests to `tayyorCompletion.test.ts` for `completionBadge`, one per required case: exact-match → `{kind:'loss', pct:0}`; overage → `{kind:'ortiqcha', excessKg:300}`; shortfall → `{kind:'loss', pct:18.2}`. All 9 tests (6 prior + 3 new) pass; `tsc -b` clean (same pre-existing unrelated `jsbarcode` error as before).
**Live verification via MCP — access restored this session (last session's `403`s are gone).** Queried the real finalized cycles: `150726-003` (sent 5000 = received 5000, locked loss 0%) and `150726-002` (sent 5000, received 5200, locked loss 0%) are real production Window 2 rows. `150726-001` (sent 2200, received 2700) surfaced something worth flagging on its own:
**🚩 Found, not fixed: a real negative `final_loss_pct` (`-22.7`) is already stored on `150726-001` in production** — written before the completion-math floor fix existed, presumably via the old unfloored Tugallash formula. Ran the exact client logic against it: `completionBadge(-22.7, ortiqcha(2200, 2700)=500)` → `{kind:'ortiqcha', excessKg:500}` — **Ortiqcha wins regardless**, so the stale negative value never reaches the screen; the badge logic is provably robust to this legacy data without needing a data migration. Deliberately did **not** correct the stored `-22.7` value itself — it's a live business record (a finalized yield-loss figure) and rewriting historical finalized data wasn't asked for and is out of this task's scope; flagging it here so it can be addressed deliberately (e.g., a one-off data-correction migration) rather than silently touched in passing.
**Constructed the one scenario real data didn't have (shortfall/manual-Tugallash):** all three real finalized serials happen to be exact-match or overage. Used `140726-001` (a real `kirim_lines` serial that had never been sent to Moyka) to insert a synthetic `moyka_sends` (1000kg) → `finished_pallets` (700kg) → `wash_cycles` (`final`, `final_loss_pct=30.0`, matching `computeFinalLossPct(1000,700)`) — confirmed `completionBadge(30.0, 0)` → `{kind:'loss', pct:30}`, i.e. the UI would show `-30.0%` in red. Deleted all three synthetic rows afterward (`wash_cycles`, `finished_pallets`, `moyka_sends` for `140726-001`); verified 0 rows remain. All four scenarios (exact-match, two overages, one synthetic shortfall) now confirmed against the exact query shape `useMoykaOutput` runs.

## 2026-07-16 — History list ordering (newest-first, app-wide)
**Context:** completed/history lists across the app were inconsistent — some already sorted newest-first, some had no ordering at all (arbitrary DB row order), one had a real bug where a sort was computed but silently discarded. Audited every "second window"/completed/history list app-wide (per CLAUDE.md — inspected each hook's query and each consuming component before touching anything) rather than guessing which ones were broken.
**Already correct, verified, left untouched (no change made):**
- `useIntakeHistory` (Ombor Hisobotlar) — `.order('confirmed_at', {ascending:false})` server-side. Newest-first already.
- `useGateHistory` (Qorovul Hisobotlar) — client-side `.sort((a,b) => (b.sana??'').localeCompare(a.sana??''))`. Newest-first already.
- `useKirimTrips` → `QorovulKirimTab`'s "Yakunlangan" window — `kirim_orders` fetched with `.order('created_at', {ascending:false})`; `completed = trips.filter(...)` preserves that order (`Array.filter` never reorders). Newest-first already, inherited correctly.
- `KirimOrdersList` (Menejer, own KIRIM submissions) — `.order('created_at', {ascending:false})`. Newest-first already. Not a two-window completed/active split, but checked anyway since it's a history-shaped list.
**Deliberately NOT touched — chronological (oldest-first) is the correct reading, not a bug:** `useNotes` (Qaydlar, `.order('created_at', {ascending:true})`) and the per-serial `moyka_sends` history inside `OmborMoykaTab`'s row-expand (sorted ascending in `useMoykaSerials`). Both are conversation/event-timeline logs for a *single* entity — read top-to-bottom like a chat, not scanned for "which of these many items is newest." Reversing these would make them harder to read, not easier; excluded as out of scope for "completed/history list" in the task's sense (a list of many items where you want the newest one at top), not silently missed.
**Three real bugs found and fixed**, all via a new shared `sortByDateDesc(items, getDate)` in `src/lib/sortByDate.ts` (extracted so it's one tested implementation, not three ad-hoc `.sort()` calls — nulls sort last, ISO date/timestamp strings compare correctly as plain strings, doesn't mutate its input):
1. **`useMoykaOutput`'s `completed` (Tugallangan, Window 2) had no ordering at all** — built from `sentBySerial`'s Map-iteration order (itself the DB's default row order for `moyka_sends`, unrelated to anything meaningful). Added `lastReceivedDate` (max `finished_pallets.received_date` per serial — `wash_cycles` has no finalized-at timestamp, so this is the closest real signal for "when this cycle completed") and sorted by it descending.
2. **`useMoykaSerials` → `OmborMoykaTab`'s "To'liq yuborilgan" window had no ordering** — same shape of bug. Added `lastSentDate` (last of the already-chronologically-sorted `sends`) to `MoykaSerial`, and sort **only the `fullySent` filter** by it in the component — deliberately did not touch the hook's own array order, since that same array also backs the active "Yuborish uchun" window, which isn't a completed/history list and wasn't asked to be reordered.
3. **`useIntakeLines` → `OmborIntakeTab`'s "Qabul qilingan mahsulotlar" window had a real bug, not just a missing sort**: the `orders` query *was* fetched with `.order('created_at', {ascending:false})`, but `combined` is built by `.map()`-ing over `kirim_lines` (no `.order()` of its own) and looking up each line's parent order — so the orders' sort was computed and then silently thrown away. Fixed by sorting the `received` filter in the component by `intake.confirmed_at` descending (the actual "completed" event for this window — when storage confirmed the intake — rather than the order's date, which is when the trip arrived, an earlier and less relevant event).
**🚩 Flagged, not fixed: `finished_pallets.received_date` and `moyka_sends.sent_date` are `date` columns (no time component)** — so same-day completions can't be told apart chronologically; `sortByDateDesc` still puts today above yesterday correctly, but ties within a day fall back to whatever order the array already had (stable sort), which isn't necessarily true intra-day chronology. This is the same category of limitation already flagged for `gate_weighings` (no own timestamp) in the Step 4 Hisobotlar work — a schema change (adding a real timestamp) wasn't in this task's scope, so noting it here rather than fixing it silently or ignoring it.
**Testing.** `src/lib/sortByDate.test.ts` (5 cases: reorders ascending input, stays stable on already-descending input, nulls sort last, doesn't mutate its input, full timestamps — not just dates — compare correctly same-day). All 14 tests in the repo (5 new + 9 prior) pass; `tsc -b` clean (same pre-existing unrelated `jsbarcode` error).
**Live verification via MCP (access available this session).** Real production data confirmed all three fixes:
- `storage_intake.confirmed_at` (OmborIntakeTab fix) — four distinct timestamps, unambiguous: `140726-003` (07:25:36 today) → `150726-003` → `150726-002` → `150726-001` (all previous day, in that order). The fixed `received` window now returns exactly that order; before the fix, `useIntakeLines`'s discarded sort meant this was arbitrary.
- `finished_pallets` max `received_date` (Tugallangan fix) and `moyka_sends` max `sent_date` (OmborMoyka fix) — all four/most serials share today's date (the schema-limitation case above), but `150726-002`'s last send (previous day) correctly sorts below the same-day serials in the "To'liq yuborilgan" window — a real, verifiable improvement over the prior arbitrary order, even though same-day ties aren't fully resolved.
- Incidental confirmation the earlier completion-math fix is live in production: `150726-001`'s previously-flagged negative `final_loss_pct` (`-22.7`, found two sessions ago) is now `0` — the real Ombor manager re-finalized it after that fix shipped, correcting the historical bad value through normal use rather than a data migration.
- A new real serial, `140726-003`, appeared in production since the last session (intake → Moyka send → finished receipt, finalized at 3.7% loss) — used as real data for the intake-ordering check above; nothing synthetic was needed for that one.

## 2026-07-16 — Section mirroring / derived stage membership
**Context:** §5.1 KIRIM's Window 2 ("Qabul qilingan mahsulotlar") filtered on `intake !== null` — presence of a `storage_intake` row. Since `storage_intake.status` defaults to `'skladda_turibdi'` at accept time and **nothing in the app ever issues an `UPDATE` on it** (confirmed by grep — the only write is the single `insert` in `OmborIntakeTab.handleAccept`), the row's status was permanently `skladda_turibdi`, and the row itself never left Window 2, even long after every kg of that serial's raw material had been sent to Moyka. That's the reported bug, root-caused by inspection before any code was touched (CLAUDE.md).
**The real fix is a model change, not a status update.** Rather than teaching `storage_intake.status` to track stage (a stored, syncable field — the opposite of "derive, don't store"), membership in each §5 window is now **entirely derived from the same event logs already used elsewhere** (`moyka_sends`, `wash_cycles`) — no new column, no migration, `storage_intake.status` untouched and still defaulting to `skladda_turibdi` (requirement: don't rewrite or drop it, just stop reading it for placement).
**Named the recurring shape: section mirroring.** Once the derivation was written out, the boundary between every pair of adjacent §5 sections turned out to be the exact same relationship: **Window N of section K = Window (N−1) of section K+1**. Formalized as a named pattern in SPEC.md's §5 intro (with the concrete table) and a one-line pointer in CLAUDE.md's Reuse list, so a future prompt can say "section mirroring" instead of re-deriving or re-explaining the boundary each time. The two predicates that ARE this pattern (not just "happen to compute the same value the same way twice") live in one new file, `src/lib/stageMembership.ts`:
- `hasRawRemainder(actualQty, sent) = actualQty − sent > 0` — §5.1 KIRIM Window 2 = §5.2 Moyka Window 1.
- `isInMoyka(sent, finalized) = sent > 0 && !finalized` — §5.2 Moyka Window 2 = §5.3 Tayyor Window 1.
**How the reuse is actually wired, not just conceptually aligned:**
- `OmborIntakeTab` now also calls `useMoykaSerials()` (previously only the Moyka tab used it) purely to get each serial's `sent` total, and filters its own richer `useIntakeLines()` data with `hasRawRemainder` — the exact same computation `useMoykaSerials` already made for its own "Yuborish uchun" window, not a second copy of `actual_qty − sent`. The stale `{line.intake.status}` display in that row was replaced with the derived remainder ("Qoldiq: N kg") — the literal fix for "stuck showing `skladda_turibdi`."
- `OmborMoykaTab`'s Window 1 (`toSend`) now filters with `hasRawRemainder(s.actual_qty, s.sent)` instead of the old `s.available > 0` — same value, but now the named shared predicate, not an inline expression that could silently drift from KIRIM's copy.
- `OmborMoykaTab`'s Window 2 is a full replacement, not a tweak: the old `fullySent` (`available <= 0 && sent > 0` — "fully sent") is **gone**. Window 2 now renders `useMoykaOutput().serials` **directly** — literally the same hook instance/array §5.3 Tayyor's own Window 1 already renders, imported into a second tab. This is the cleanest possible instantiation of "reused, not duplicated": there is exactly one implementation of "sent, not finalized," period, and two components display it. Window 2 lost its send action and ⋯ expand (send/notes/history belong to Window 1; managing a serial once it's in Moyka is §5.3's job) and gained a new read-only row (serial · type · owner · Yuborilgan · Jarayonda/Ortiqcha, matching Tayyor's own display language) and a new heading, "Moykada — jarayonda" (the old "To'liq yuborilgan" heading became actively wrong under the new membership rule, since a merely-partially-sent serial can now appear here too).
- `useMoykaOutput`'s own internal filter (previously `!finalizedSerials.has(s)`, over a `serialList` already pre-filtered to `sent > 0` by construction) was refactored to call `isInMoyka` explicitly too — a pure refactor (verified behavior-identical: `serialList` only ever contains `sent > 0` serials, so `isInMoyka(sent, finalized)` and the old `!finalized` check agree in every case), done so the S2W2/S3W1 boundary is backed by the same NAMED predicate on both sides of the mirror, not just "this file's version happens to be equivalent."
