UPDATE own rows," which would have meant restricting `laborator_updates` to `tested_by = auth.uid()` — but the *existing* Phase 0 policy (confirmed live before touching anything) was already unrestricted (`my_role() = 'laborator'`, no ownership check), matching every other role's update policy in this app (`ombor_updates`, etc.). Flagged the operational cost of tightening it (one laborator becoming unavailable would permanently strand any row they started) rather than silently applying either interpretation; user confirmed keeping it unrestricted.
**Systemic gap found, flagged not fixed: no table in this app has ever had audit logging, despite SPEC.md §2.7.** `audit_log` (table + RLS) has existed since Phase 0 (`0005_notes_audit.sql`) but grepped every migration and every `src/` file — zero triggers write to it, zero app code inserts into it. This is not specific to `lab_results`; it's every operational table, since the beginning. Per explicit instruction, **not** retrofitting this onto every existing table as a side effect of the Laborator schema — that's its own dedicated task, and should be scoped together with deciding whether Rahbar gets a UI to actually read `audit_log` (nothing does today either). Added a generic, reusable `log_audit()` trigger function (didn't exist before) and attached it only to `lab_results` — not `security definer`, since `audit_log`'s existing insert policy already permits any authenticated session, unlike `complete_chiqim_stage2` which needs the elevation because Qorovul has zero write access to `chiqim_requests` directly.
**Verification:** live column-shape query + `pg_trigger` query both confirm the migration applied exactly as designed. Stopped short of a synthetic insert-then-delete smoke test of the trigger — `lab_results` has zero rows and no void concept, and manufacturing then deleting a fake row here would cut against this project's own never-delete convention for no real benefit; functional round-trip proof (a real Laborator insert firing the trigger) is left to 2b's Playwright test, the first point a real insert actually happens.
**Out of scope, not touched (per the agreed split):** Laborator KIRIM/CHIQIM screens (2b/2c), hard gate on `useAvailableFinishedStock` (2c), re-wash cycle-awareness retrofit + void/re-entry (2d), audit-log retrofit onto any other table, Rahbar's audit-log UI.

## 2026-07-18 — Step 8 prompt 2, split 2b: Laborator KIRIM screens (§5.5.2)
**Context:** First real Laborator UI — three windows (Tahlil kutilmoqda / Sera kutilmoqda / Yakunlangan) against `lab_results` as reshaped in 2a. Descriptive check only, no verdict (KIRIM never gates anything, per v1.9).
**Resolved ambiguity, not stopped on:** v1.9's §5.5.2 text says the Tahlil form has "sampled pallet (dropdown)," inherited verbatim from the old v1.5 mirror design. KIRIM has no pallet concept at intake — Barcode #2/`finished_pallets` doesn't exist until §5.3; the KIRIM subject is the raw serial itself (Barcode #1), single-type by construction (§2.1), nothing to choose from a dropdown. Built with no `sampled_pallet` input on the KIRIM Tahlil form at all — the column stays `null` for `scope='kirim'` rows. Also resolved: the Tahlil form **never** shows an SO₂ input, sulfured or not — `so2_mg_kg` is only ever written later via "Sera kiritish" (W2), matching the original v1.5 locked text ("SO₂ left blank") and the schema's own shape (INSERT never touches `so2_mg_kg`; only a later UPDATE does). Whether a target exists only decides the row's initial `status` (`moisture_in` → W2, or straight to `complete` → W3), not what the form itself asks for.
**Reuse over new pattern:** `GatePhoto.tsx` made additive (`bucket` prop, defaults to `gate-photos`, same shape as `GateStageForm`'s `dir`/`requireDepartureDoc`) instead of copy-pasting a second signed-URL component for `lab-photos`. `LaboratorHome.tsx` stays flat (no KIRIM|CHIQIM tab bar yet) — same precedent every other role followed (Menejer/Qorovul/Ombor were all flat pages until their CHIQIM tab actually existed); the tab bar arrives with 2c, not pre-stubbed.
**`lab-photos` storage bucket** — same `read_all` + `<role>_insert` shape as every other photo bucket (`gate-photos`/`kirim-photos`/`intake-photos`). Permissions-gated (schema-adjacent), SQL shown, applied only after explicit confirmation.
**Testing — real chain, three roles, one fixture identifier landed clean on the 5th attempt.** `tests/e2e/laborator-kirim.spec.ts`: Menejer creates a KIRIM order (Subxon sulfured, both targets; Isfara natural, moisture target only) → Qorovul gate stage 1 → Ombor accepts both lines (the real W1 trigger) → Laborator tests both. Confirms the natural line skips "Sera kutilmoqda" entirely and lands straight in "Yakunlangan," while the sulfured line goes through the two-step flow, ending with a real DB check that Isfara's `so2_mg_kg` is a genuine SQL `null`, not `0`/`''`. **Four real bugs caught and fixed during test authoring, all in the test, not the app:**
1. Reading the just-saved serials from the confirmation panel before the placeholder ("seriya: kutilmoqda") had actually resolved to the real value — fixed by waiting for the serial regex pattern, not just element count.
2. Qorovul's gate-stage-1 photo fields use `PhotoField.tsx`'s async `compressImage` before calling the parent form's `onChange` — clicking submit immediately after `setInputFiles` can race ahead of that, submitting with `platePhoto`/`scalePhoto` still `null` and silently failing form validation (no exception surfaces to Playwright, since the click itself succeeds). Fixed by waiting for "Siqilmoqda…" to clear before submitting, and added an explicit post-submit visibility check (the red in-progress border) that CHIQIM's existing tests already had and this one initially skipped.
3. Scoping Ombor's per-line accept button via `.locator('div', {hasText: serial}).last()` broke once the line's own accept form was open — `IntakeAcceptForm` repeats the bare serial in its own `<div>`, so `.last()` picked that inner display div instead of the row. Fixed by matching the header `<span>` (never repeated) and walking up via `xpath=ancestor::div[contains(@class,"rounded-md")][1]` — XPath's `ancestor::` axis returns nearest-first, so `[1]` is the row, not the outer group.
4. The postcondition after each Ombor accept (`expect(...).toHaveCount(0)`) was a false-positive trap: once a line is genuinely accepted it leaves "Kutilmoqda" entirely (not just loses its button), so the locator chain becomes unmatched either way — on real success **or** on an unrelated broken-locator failure, both read as "0 buttons found." This is exactly how bug #3 above passed silently for the first line while masking that the second line's accept never actually persisted (`actual_qty` stayed `null` in the DB). Replaced with a positive check: confirm the serial now appears in the "Qabul qilingan mahsulotlar" section.
Fixture identifiers `TEST-LAB-KIRIM-01` through `-04` each caught one of the above (or were fresh restarts after one), left in place per void-not-delete (none reached a state with anything real to void — `kirim_orders`/`gate_weighings` have no void mechanism regardless, same standing gap). `-05` is the clean passing run.
**Out of scope, not touched (per the agreed split):** Laborator CHIQIM screens + verdict + hard gate (2c), re-wash retrofit (2d), any tab-bar/nav change beyond the flat KIRIM page.

## 2026-07-18 — Step 8 prompt 2, split 2c: Laborator CHIQIM screens (§5.5.3) + hard gate (part D)
**Context:** Decisive lab check on Moyka output, plus the hard gate that makes an untested or re-wash-flagged pallet invisible to both Menejer's feasibility checker and Ombor's scan screen. Builds directly on 2a's schema and 2b's KIRIM conventions.
**W1 trigger resolved by reasoning, not left ambiguous.** v1.9's own text ("finished batches awaiting sampling, appearing when a wash cycle produces pallets (§5.3 Tugallash)") reads as two different triggers at once — individual pallet saves (continuous through the day) vs. Tugallash (one deliberate lock). Chose Tugallash: `wash_cycles.status='final'` is the trigger, not each `finished_pallets` insert. Reasoning: "jami kg"/"pallet soni" describing a moving target before the cycle is locked doesn't make sense for a decisive test, and every other finalize-style action in this app (Tugallash itself, Yakunlash) is already manual-only by named invariant — sampling a still-open cycle would be the first exception to that pattern, not a natural extension of it.
**Verdict placement resolved the same way.** The task's window list only ever names three windows for CHIQIM (same as KIRIM), with "verdict step" described as an action, not a fourth window. Built accordingly: a natural line's verdict happens on the Tahlil form itself (two buttons, `O'tdi`/`Qayta yuvish`, instead of a generic Saqlash); a sulfured line's verdict happens at Sera kiritish instead, bundled with the SO2 entry. No SO2 field on the Tahlil form regardless of scope, mirroring 2b's KIRIM decision exactly (SO2 is always a separate later capture, never entered alongside moisture).
**Soft-warn direction is a judgment call, documented as such:** "misses target" is read as the reading exceeding the client's maximum (the standard direction for both moisture and sulfur specs in this domain) — never blocks, same philosophy as every other soft-warning in this app (Kam chiqdi, Tugallash's warnings).
**Hard gate — one shared helper, not two independent implementations.** New `src/lib/labVerdict.ts`'s `currentCycleLabStatus(serials)` is used by both `useAvailableFinishedStock.ts` (Menejer's bulk feasibility check) and `OmborChiqimTab.tsx`'s per-scan check (via a new `not_lab_passed` reason threaded through `chiqimScan.ts`'s `resolveScan`) — SPEC.md v1.9 §8's "one derived truth, all consumers," same reasoning as every other derived-balance rule already in this app. "Current wash cycle" = highest `cycle_no` with a `wash_cycles` row for that serial (a row only exists once Tugallash has run); absence of a row, or a row with no matching `lab_results` verdict yet, both read as `untested`, never defaulting to available.
**Testing — real chain, five roles, two independent verdicts, thirteen fixture identifiers to land clean.** `tests/e2e/laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts`: one KIRIM order, two lines (Subxon → `qayta_yuvish`, Isfara → `o_tdi`), driven through gate → intake → Moyka → Tayyor receipt → Tugallash → both Lab verdicts → then both directions of the gate checked for real: Menejer's feasibility hint correctly reads Subxon as unavailable (`0 kg` available) and Isfara as fine; Ombor's scan screen refuses the Subxon barcode (`not_lab_passed`) and accepts the Isfara one. Confirmed both directions deliberately, not just the new/scary one — a broken gate that blocks *everything* would have passed a negative-only test.
**Bugs found and fixed, seven of them, all in the test — worth recording precisely since a couple are real, non-obvious Playwright/React lessons, not just locator typos:**
1. `selectOption({ label: /PLT-/ })` — Playwright's `selectOption` label matcher takes a literal string, not a regex. Fixed with `{ index: 1 }` (only one pallet per cycle in this test).
2. `row.click()` to expand a Tayyor Mahsulot card landed on the card's bounding-box center, which can miss the toggle button entirely once the totals line below it makes the card taller than the button itself — the button only wraps the header line. Fixed by targeting the button specifically (`row.locator('button', { hasText: '⋯' })`).
3. `row.getByText(barcode)` after a successful receipt hit Playwright's strict-mode violation — the barcode legitimately renders twice (the pallet list item and the separate "Oxirgi Barcode #2" display). Fixed with `.first()`.
4. **A genuine React-controlled-input race**, the most interesting one: filling the Moyka send form's qty field and clicking submit immediately after, on the *second* of two back-to-back sends on the same page, reproducibly left the field showing the correct value via `toHaveValue` (a raw DOM-attribute read) while the component's own *derived* "Qoladi" text still read as if qty were `0` — proving React's controlled state (`onChange`-driven) hadn't actually picked up the fill by the time the submit fired, despite the DOM attribute being correct. An explicit blur (`press('Tab')`) between fill and submit did not reliably fix it.
5. The actual fix for #4: re-navigate away and back via the real nav links between each send/receipt, forcing a fresh component mount rather than reusing state across two rapid interactions on the same mount. `page.reload()` was tried first and made things worse in this dev environment specifically — a hard reload on a nested client-side route (`/ombor/moyka`) lands back on the parent's default tab (`/ombor`) instead of the requested route, confirmed via the page snapshot, not assumed.
6. The feasibility-hint assertion itself was wrong: expected `"Bu tur/kalibr uchun omborda pallet yo'q"`, but `checkFeasibility`'s empty-stock case returns `nearestBelow=0` (not `null`), so that fallback message is actually unreachable — the real, correct message is `"eng ko'p: 0 kg"`. Confirmed by reading `chiqimFeasibility.ts` directly rather than continuing to guess at the copy.
7. The second CHIQIM request (built to give Ombor's scan screen something to test against) initially saved as **Subxon**, not the intended **Isfara** — the type/calibre dropdowns were still on Subxon from the feasibility check two steps earlier, never reselected before the final save. A real leftover fixture (`chiqim_requests`/`chiqim_lines`, Subxon, 1000 kg, permanently unscannable since Subxon never passes) — left in place per void-not-delete, same standing gap flagged repeatedly for these tables.
Twelve earlier fixture identifiers (`TEST-LAB-CHIQIM-01` through `-12`) each caught one of the above or were restarts after one; `-13` is the clean passing run.
**Out of scope, not touched (per the agreed split):** re-wash cycle-awareness retrofit, Ombor's "Qayta yuvishga yuborish" void action, the red flag on Menejer's KIRIM list and Ombor's §5.3 (all 2d).

## 2026-07-19 — Step 8 prompt 2, split 2d: re-wash cycle retrofit + void/re-entry (SPEC.md v1.9 §5.5.4/§5.5.5) — closes Step 8
**Context:** The final, highest-risk split, flagged as such when the task was first proposed: retrofitting cycle-awareness into §5.2/§5.3 code that has been shipped and working since Step 6/7, not building new screens against a blank slate. Landed without regressing the existing single-cycle flow (confirmed: 61/61 unit tests pass throughout, including every pre-existing §5.1–§5.3 test).
**Core design: the active cycle number is derived, never stored.** `rewash.ts`'s `activeCycleNo(voidedCycleNos)` = 1 if a serial has never been voided into a re-wash, otherwise `max(voided cycles) + 1`. No new counter column anywhere — matches CLAUDE.md's "derive, don't store" exactly the way `useAvailableFinishedStock`'s hard gate already does. `activeCycles.ts`'s `fetchActiveCycles()` is the one shared I/O layer around it, used by `useMoykaSerials.ts` and `useMoykaOutput.ts` so both hooks can never independently disagree about which cycle a serial is "in" (SPEC.md v1.9 §8: "one derived truth, all consumers").
**A cycle's re-wash input is also derived, not stored:** the sum of voided, non-Konditirskiy `finished_pallets.weight_kg` for the previous cycle (`cycleInputKg()`). This is what makes §5.2's existing "send by weight against a serial" pattern work completely unchanged for a re-wash send, per the task's own §5.5.5 resolution — no new columns on `moyka_sends`/`storage_intake` were needed, only a different *source* for the "how much can this serial send" figure.
**The pending-rewash flag is self-clearing by construction.** `usePendingRewash.ts` checks whether the serial's CURRENT active cycle carries a `qayta_yuvish` verdict. The moment Ombor voids that cycle's pallets, `activeCycleNo` derives a new, higher active cycle, and the same query on the same historical `lab_results` row no longer matches — no "already actioned" flag to remember or clear separately. Shared by Menejer's `KirimOrdersList.tsx` (text only, no action — SPEC.md v1.9 §5.5.4: "Menejer sees it, Ombor acts on it") and Ombor's `OmborTayyorTab.tsx` (flag + the void action), so the two can never show conflicting state.
**No new RLS needed for the void action** — confirmed live before writing any code: `finished_pallets` already has an unrestricted `ombor_updates` policy (`my_role() = 'ombor'`), same as every other role's update policy in this app.
**A real app bug found and fixed via the e2e test, not a test-authoring mistake this time:** `FinishedReceiptForm.tsx`'s Barcode #2 sequence numbering (`nextBarcode2`) counted `serial.pallets`, which the cycle-awareness retrofit correctly scoped to the ACTIVE cycle only for display purposes — but `barcode2` is a permanent primary key (void-never-delete), so a re-wash cycle's first same-calibre pallet collided with the (now-voided, but still-existing-as-a-row) original cycle's barcode, e.g. both cycles trying to mint `PLT-<serial>-06-1`. The insert would have failed on the PK constraint in real use. Fixed by adding a second, deliberately UN-scoped field to `OutputSerial` — `barcodeSeqByCalibre`, counting every pallet ever made for that serial+calibre across all cycles and statuses — used only for the next sequence number, while `pallets` stays cycle-scoped for everything display-related. This is exactly the kind of consequence the split's own risk assessment anticipated (retrofitting cycle-awareness into shipped code touching more than the obviously-related fields) — caught by the e2e test actually exercising a second cycle's receipt form, not by inspection.
**Testing — full real chain, one serial, two wash cycles, five roles, matching the task's own worked example numbers exactly (5000kg → 4500kg re-wash input).** `tests/e2e/rewash-full-cycle.spec.ts`: 5000kg raw → Moyka → received as Kalibr 6 (4500kg) + Konditirskiy (500kg) → Tugallash (0% loss, cycle 1) → Lab CHIQIM verdict `Qayta yuvish` → Ombor sees the red flag, voids → confirmed live: the Kalibr 6 pallet (4500kg) voided, the Konditirskiy pallet (500kg) untouched, `in_stock` → serial reappears in §5.2 Window 1 showing exactly 4500kg available, not the original 5000kg → sent 4500kg → received as Kalibr 6 (4000kg) + a SECOND, separate Konditirskiy pallet (300kg, its own barcode) → Tugallash, loss correctly computed as 4.4% against the 4500kg re-wash input (not 14% against the original 5000kg) → Lab CHIQIM verdict `O'tdi`. Final DB check: two `lab_results` rows (`qayta_yuvish` then `o_tdi`, correct order), four `finished_pallets` rows total — cycle 1's calibre pallet `bekor_qilindi`, cycle 1's Konditirskiy still `in_stock`, cycle 2's calibre pallet `in_stock`, cycle 2's Konditirskiy `in_stock` with its own distinct barcode.
**Nine real issues found and fixed during test authoring — the barcode bug above plus eight test-side ones, several genuinely non-obvious:**
1. `page.click()` on a Tugallangan row's outer card missed the toggle button (same bounding-box-center issue documented in the 2c entry) — now targets the `⋯`-containing button specifically, same fix applied at every occurrence.
2. Row locators hardcoded to `border-slate-200` broke for a re-wash row, which now legitimately renders `border-amber-300` (this session's own new styling) — fixed by scoping to the section container and matching on `.rounded-md` alone, not a specific border color.
3. **The same React-controlled-input race from the 2c entry recurred here**, this time in the Tayyor Mahsulot receipt form across two pallets received in sequence on one mount — confirmed by the "0 received" symptom matching the earlier diagnosis exactly (a derived UI figure disagreeing with a value `toHaveValue` had already confirmed). Fixed the same way: forced a fresh component mount (client-side away-and-back navigation) before every single receipt, not just once per Tugallash cycle.
4. The Laborator CHIQIM window's cycle-number label reads "yuvish sikli N", not "sikl N" (that shorter form is Ombor's own label, a different string) — a test-assertion mismatch, not an app inconsistency.
5. Once a serial has two `lab_results` rows (one per cycle), Laborator's own Yakunlangan window legitimately shows BOTH — the serial alone no longer uniquely identifies a row there; had to add the cycle number to the locator's filter. Flagged separately below as a real, positive finding for §G.
6. One run failed at the very first step after ten minutes, having created nothing in the database — an isolated, non-reproduced slow/transient environment hiccup, not chased further (immediate retry with the same plate passed cleanly in just over a minute).
Eight fixture identifiers (`TEST-REWASH-01` through `-07`) each caught one of the above (or were restarts after the transient failure); `-08` is the clean passing run.
**§G — serial passport data-model check (documentation only, nothing built, per the task's explicit instruction):**
- **Per-cycle loss calculated independently: fully supported.** `wash_cycles` is one row per `(serial, cycle_no)`, each with its own `final_loss_pct`, computed against that cycle's own derived sent/received — confirmed live in the test (0% then 4.4%, never blended).
- **Konditirskiy tracked per-cycle with its own barcode: fully supported.** Confirmed live: two independent `finished_pallets` rows, `PLT-<serial>-KN-1` and `PLT-<serial>-KN-2`, both `in_stock` simultaneously, both permanently distinct.
- **Cumulative totals derivable: yes, nothing blocks it.** `finished_pallets.wash_cycle` and `moyka_sends.wash_cycle` are real per-row columns; a cross-cycle total (or a weighted lifetime loss %) is a plain `GROUP BY serial` query away, no schema change needed, consistent with "derive, don't store."
- **Multiple cycles visible: real, PARTIAL gap, found by the test rather than assumed — flagging, not fixing.** Laborator's own CHIQIM Yakunlangan window already shows every cycle's `lab_results` row simultaneously (it happened to be keyed by `lab_results.id`, not `serial`, from 2c — a pleasant accident, not a deliberate passport feature). **Ombor's own §5.3 Tugallangan window does NOT** — `useMoykaOutput`'s `completed` list is one row per serial, reflecting only the serial's current ACTIVE cycle; once a serial re-washes, its previous cycle's finalized record (still fully intact and correct in `wash_cycles`, never touched by the void) becomes invisible in Ombor's own history view, even though Laborator can still see it. A real serial passport screen will need to query `wash_cycles`/`finished_pallets` directly by serial (not through either hook's active-cycle-scoped shape) to show a true multi-cycle history — deliberately not built here, per the task's explicit "document, don't build."
**This closes Step 8 prompt 2 (Laborator: schema, KIRIM screens, CHIQIM screens + hard gate, re-wash retrofit + void/re-entry).** All four splits (2a–2d) are complete: `lab_results` reshaped with full RLS and audit logging, both Laborator tabs built end to end, the hard gate wired into every dispatch-availability consumer, and re-wash now works as a real, cycle-aware loop rather than a single-pass design that could only ever model one wash per serial.
**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** serial passport UI itself, lab history/Tekshiruvlar tarixi (§5.5.6), Menejer reporting sections (§3.2–3.5), Rahbar exceptions, offline/PWA.

## 2026-07-19 — Step 9 prompt 1: effective_qty derivation + provisional-weight display (SPEC.md v1.10 §2.16)
**Context:** applied only the weight-authority half of the attached SPEC-reporting-v1.10-revision.md (pasted verbatim at docs/SPEC-reporting-v1.10-revision.md so nothing is lost) — the §3.2 unified reporting layer in the same document is explicitly deferred to a future prompt, not touched here.

**Section-number collision, found before editing SPEC.md, not after.** The revision document numbers its new section "§2.15" — but SPEC.md already has an existing, unrelated §2.15 ("Technical architecture," stack/RLS/serial-generation, present since v1.8). Renumbered the new section to **§2.16** throughout (including its own internal §2.15.1/§2.15.2 subsection references, now §2.16.1/§2.16.2) when merging into SPEC.md. The raw revision file keeps its original numbering unchanged, since it's a verbatim reference copy, not the merged document — a future prompt applying its §3.2 will need the same renumbering treatment for any cross-references it makes back to "§2.15."

**Priority order of effective_qty's three cases, resolved by reasoning and confirmed with the user before coding.** §2.15.1 (now §2.16.1) lists three bullets — single-line→gate net, multi-line→intake, before-gate-stage-2→intake-provisional — that read as independent branches but aren't: implemented as an ordered rule (gate-stage-2-done gates provisional/final; single-vs-multi then decides which figure becomes the value), per weightAuthority.ts's deriveEffectiveQty. Consequence, stated explicitly to the user and confirmed: **a multi-line truck's effective_qty never becomes gate net, even after gate stage 2 completes** — only its provisional flag flips off; the value stays the per-line intake figure permanently, with gate net feeding only the truck-level reconciliation variance. This reading follows §2.16.1 (the formula section) over §2.16.2's more narrative "updates to gate net" sentence, which describes the single-line/norm case.

**"Materially different" (the §2.15.2/§2.16.2 edge case) has no defined threshold, and the task explicitly said not to build one.** Reused the existing settings_limits.kam_chiqdi_pct (already 5%, already governs declared-vs-actual variance at §5.1) as the materiality bar for both the truck-level variance highlight and the "sent while provisional, later differed" flag — reuse of existing config, not a new one.

**"Sent while provisional" timing is date-granularity only, a documented limitation, not a blocker.** moyka_sends.sent_date is a date; gate_weighings.completed_at is a timestamptz. There is no created_at on moyka_sends to get finer precision. fetchEffectiveQty compares sent_date <= completed_at.slice(0,10) — same-day ordering can't be resolved, same limitation this codebase already accepts elsewhere for date-only comparisons.

**A real live-data anomaly, found via inspection, not invented.** Serial 140726-003 (already documented in earlier sessions as a debugging artifact) has gate_weighings.completed_at **before** storage_intake.confirmed_at — gate stage 2 finished two days before intake was even recorded, which violates §2.16.2's assumed sequencing (gate arrives after intake). Its gate net (3000kg) is less than what's already been sent to Moyka (5000kg), so switching the cycle-1 cap from actual_qty to effective_qty would make available go negative for this serial. Not touched (the underlying data is out of scope to fix, same as every prior session's policy on this exact row) — but useMoykaSerials.ts's available is now floored at 0 (Math.max(0, cycleInputKg - sentThisCycle)), matching the existing Ortiqcha/Jarayonda floor-and-flag convention already used everywhere else in this codebase, so no screen ever displays a negative "available to send." Because this row's send predates its own gate completion by two days on the wrong side (gate finished first), it does NOT trigger the "sent while provisional" flag above — confirmed correct: that flag is specifically about the ordinary case (provisional at send time), and this row was never provisional at send time by the same date check.

**No other existing loss/yield figures change, verified by design, not merely asserted.** Locked wash_cycles.final_loss_pct values are read directly at display time, never recomputed (useMoykaOutput.ts's existing comment already states this — confirmed unaffected). Already-recorded moyka_sends/finished_pallets rows are events, unaffected retroactively by a change to the cap they were once checked against. computeFinalLossPct(sent, received) itself was not touched — cycle-1's sent figure (from the event log) is what it always was; only the forward-looking cap on future sends (and therefore any not-yet-finalized serial's eventual locked loss%, going forward) now derives from effective_qty. Live-queried the whole kirim_lines/storage_intake/gate_weighings/moyka_sends join before writing any code specifically to find and report this distinction with real numbers, per the task's own "loss/yield are money paths, report before/after explicitly" instruction.

**One real, currently-live multi-line variance this change newly surfaces, not a bug:** order 97ea53d0… (serials 140726-001/140726-002), gate net 8000kg vs declared_total 5500kg — a 2500kg/45% gap that was never computed or shown anywhere in the app before this prompt (gate net was previously only visible in the detail view, never used as a computational input). Both serials' own effective_qty (multi-line → per-line intake, per the priority-order decision above) are unchanged from before (500kg and 5000kg respectively) — only the new truck-level variance display is new, on both Menejer's KIRIM list and Ombor's §5.1 Window 2.

**Implementation shape mirrors rewash.ts/activeCycles.ts deliberately** (named by the user as the pattern to mirror): weightAuthority.ts holds the pure rule (deriveEffectiveQty, computeVariance, isMaterialVariance, unit-tested, 11 new cases in weightAuthority.test.ts), effectiveQty.ts is the I/O + combination layer (fetchEffectiveQty, batched by ORDER not just the requested serials — a multi-line reconciliation needs every line on the trip even if the caller only asked about one — plus a thin useEffectiveQty hook for the two screen-level consumers that read it directly).

**Consumers switched:** useMoykaSerials.ts (cycle-1 cycleInputKg argument — the pure cycleInputKg() function itself untouched, only which figure its cycle-1 arg carries; available floored at 0), OmborIntakeTab.tsx (§5.1 Window 2 membership test + display, was hasRawRemainder(actual_qty, ...), now effective_qty), OmborMoykaTab.tsx (send-list row shows provisional/variance, already correct math via useMoykaSerials), KirimOrdersList.tsx (Menejer's KIRIM list, previously showed only declared_qty — now shows effective_qty/provisional alongside declared, unchanged). **Not touched, deliberately:** useMoykaOutput.ts (never read storage_intake directly — its sent/received are pure event-log sums, already correct; the cycle-1 remainder check OmborTayyorTab.tsx needs already flows through the now-fixed useMoykaSerials.cycleInputKg), IntakeAcceptForm.tsx/OmborHisobotlar.tsx's existing declared-vs-actual "Kam chiqdi" check (a distinct, still-valid floor-level sanity check at accept time, before gate net is typically even known — the spec's "never intake-vs-declared" language is about the accounting variance, not this one; see the new §5.1 SPEC.md bullet), LaboratorKirimTab.tsx/useLaboratorKirim.ts (descriptive-only per §5.5, quality independent of quantity, confirmed by spec's own words).

**Testing.** weightAuthority.test.ts: 11 cases covering all four deriveEffectiveQty branches (including the multi-line-never-adopts-gate-net case and the defensive null-gate-net fallback) plus computeVariance/isMaterialVariance. npm test → 72/72 passing (61 pre-existing + 11 new). npx tsc -b --noEmit → clean.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** §3.2 reporting screens/query engine/passport/client report/stock-on-hand/WIP/aggregates (deferred, source pasted verbatim), variance notification thresholds (§7 item 12, deliberately left open), audit_log retrofit, any UI redesign beyond the inline additions described above.

## 2026-07-19 — Step 9 regression pass on the operational loop after effective_qty (SPEC.md v1.10 §2.16)
**Context:** inspection/testing only, no feature changes, per the task. Ran the full existing Playwright suite together (not per-file), plus targeted walkthroughs of the four flows effective_qty touches. Found and fixed one real test-infrastructure bug; found and left three pre-existing, unrelated fixture-rot issues; confirmed zero functional regressions in application code.

**Real finding #1 — the full-suite sweep uses 2 workers by default, not 1, despite the config's own stated intent.** `fullyParallel: false` (playwright.config.ts) only serializes tests *within one file* — Playwright still spins up multiple worker *processes* across different files unless `workers` is set explicitly. A first full-suite run (`npx playwright test`, no flags) used 2 workers and produced session-collision symptoms in tests that pass reliably alone: a stray 403 console error, a login button click that hung until timeout, and elements appearing/disappearing depending on which worker's session was active at the moment — all in tests that have nothing to do with `effective_qty`. Re-running the identical suite with `--workers=1` made every one of those specific symptoms disappear. This is exactly the failure class the config's own comment ("shared test accounts — avoid concurrent sessions colliding") was written to prevent, but the setting never actually enforced it. **Fixed:** added `workers: 1` to playwright.config.ts, with a comment explaining why `fullyParallel: false` alone wasn't sufficient. Confirmed the fix holds: a subsequent bare `npx playwright test` (no flags) now reports "Running 12 tests using 1 worker" and reproduces the single-worker results exactly.

**Real finding #2 — `effective_qty` measurably increased per-refresh query cost on `useMoykaSerials`/`useMoykaOutput`, enough to push two already-tight existing tests past their 30s default budget.** `fetchEffectiveQty` (called on every refresh of both hooks) adds full-table-scan queries against `storage_intake` and `moyka_sends` on top of the ones those hooks already ran directly — a real, measurable latency increase, not imagined. Two pre-existing tests doing unusually long real chains (`rewash-full-cycle.spec.ts`, two full wash cycles; `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts`, two full lines end to end) were already close to the 30s ceiling and started failing on timeouts, not logic errors — confirmed by re-running each with an extended timeout (`--timeout=90000`): `rewash-full-cycle` then passed cleanly end to end (~1 minute), and `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate` progressed correctly through its ENTIRE hard-gate chain (KIRIM, Moyka, Tayyor, both lab verdicts, the hard gate hiding the failed serial) before hitting an unrelated, pre-existing issue (see finding #4). **Fixed:** added `test.setTimeout(90_000)`/`test.setTimeout(120_000)` to both, matching the precedent already set in `effective-qty.spec.ts`. **Not fixed, flagged as a follow-up:** the underlying redundancy — `fetchEffectiveQty` re-fetches `storage_intake`/`moyka_sends` independently even when called from a hook that already has that data in hand — should eventually be collapsed into a single fetch per hook refresh rather than working around it with longer timeouts indefinitely; out of scope for a testing-only prompt.

**Real finding #3 — four pre-existing CHIQIM tests cannot run at all, unrelated to effective_qty.** Checked live data *before* running anything: `chiqim-flow.spec.ts`, `chiqim-full-chain.spec.ts`, `chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts`, and `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts` all depend on hardcoded `finished_pallets` barcodes seeded once, long ago, via direct SQL rather than built fresh by the test itself (`PLT-TEST-CHIQIM-01-06-*`, `-04-06-*`, `-08-06-*`, `-10-06-*`) — every one of those rows is now `status='bekor_qilindi'` (voided), for reasons predating this session (not caused by anything in Step 8 or Step 9). None of these tests can pass without a fresh reseed, which none of them do themselves. Separately, `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts`'s own `REAL_PLATE` ('01A778AA') already has one genuinely completed (`olib_ketildi`) request from whenever it last passed — its own "not visible before completion" assertion can now never pass again on a live, unreset DB, a design limitation independent of the voided-barcode issue. **Left alone, not fixed** — reseeding correctly requires reconstructing an entire KIRIM→Moyka→Tayyor chain via SQL to produce matching barcodes, real effort disproportionate to "testing only, no feature changes," and not something this prompt's scope covers. Flagged as its own follow-up: either give each of these four tests its own self-seeding setup (matching every other spec in this suite) or accept they're single-use and rebuild them per real regression pass.

**Real finding #4 — `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts`'s one remaining failure (after the timeout fix) is a stale, unrelated test assertion, not a hard-gate bug.** With the timeout fixed, the test reaches Menejer's feasibility-hint check and gets `"Butun palletlar bilan aniq mos kelmaydi — eng yaqin: 0 kg yoki 4,000 kg"` where it expects `"...eng ko'p: 0 kg"` (the two different message shapes `ChiqimForm.tsx`'s `checkFeasibility` produces, per DECISIONS.md's own "split 2c" entry documenting this exact class of stale-copy mismatch previously). The test's own assumption — that Subxon/Kalibr 6 stock is completely empty at that point — no longer holds, because other tests in this same shared, never-reset live DB (this session's own `effective-qty.spec.ts` included) have left real, still-`in_stock` Subxon/Kalibr 6 pallets behind. This is CLAUDE.md's own documented, accepted limitation ("no branch… tests run directly against the main Supabase project") surfacing again, not a regression. **The thing actually under test — the hard gate itself — is confirmed correct**: the test reached and passed the assertion immediately before this one (Menejer's feasibility checker correctly shows `0 kg` available for THIS test's own failed-verdict serial), and the entire upstream chain (KIRIM, Moyka, Tayyor, both lab verdicts, the hard gate hiding the failed pallet) ran correctly to get there. Left as-is, not fixed — same reasoning as finding #3.

**New test, `step9-single-product-full-chain.spec.ts`:** the only requirement-#2 flow with no currently-runnable pre-existing coverage (the full single-product chain through to Menejer's finished-view actor/timestamp check) — `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts` covers the identical ground but can't run (finding #3). Self-contained, fresh fixtures. One authoring bug found and fixed while building it: navigated to Moyka immediately after clicking Ombor's accept-submit button without waiting for the insert to visibly land first (every other spec in this suite does wait) — raced Moyka's initial fetch against the still-in-flight `storage_intake` insert, so the row was legitimately absent on that specific page load. Fixed by adding the same post-accept visibility check every other spec already has. Second bug, not a bug at all: `useFinishedChiqimRequests.ts` deliberately filters out any `TEST-`-prefixed plate (by design, so real business data can't be confused with test fixtures in that specific view) — the dispatch plate needed to NOT be `TEST-`-prefixed, matching `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts`'s own `REAL_PLATE` convention, which the test's own comment already explains.

**Requirement #5 — historical `wash_cycles.final_loss_pct` values, rechecked, not just trusted from memory.** Queried the six serials with documented history across prior sessions (`140726-001/002/003`, `150726-001/002/003`) directly: `140726-001`→0%, `140726-002`→0%, `140726-003`→42.2% (voided), `150726-001`→0%, `150726-002`→0% (voided), `150726-003`→0%. Every value matches its last-documented state in DECISIONS.md exactly — no drift. Expected by design (locked `final_loss_pct` is read directly, never recomputed — confirmed in code, not just assumed) and now independently reconfirmed against live data.

**Final sweep result (single worker, fresh fixtures throughout):** 7 passed — both `effective-qty.spec.ts` tests, `kirim-client-targets.spec.ts`, `laborator-kirim.spec.ts`, `rewash-full-cycle.spec.ts`, `smoke.spec.ts`, `step9-single-product-full-chain.spec.ts` (new). 5 failed — 4 pre-existing broken fixtures (finding #3) + 1 pre-existing stale assertion with the underlying logic independently verified correct (finding #4). Zero failures traced to `effective_qty` application code. `npm test` → 72/72. `npx tsc -b --noEmit` → clean.

**System is clean to proceed to the reporting design phase.** No functional regression was found anywhere in application code from the `effective_qty` change. The two real issues found (workers config, query latency vs. timeout budget) were both test-infrastructure-only and are now fixed. The remaining five failing specs are pre-existing, independent of this change, and documented above rather than silently worked around.

## 2026-07-19 — Self-generating test fixtures across the whole e2e suite
**Context:** test infrastructure only, per the task — no app changes, except one genuine app bug found along the way and deliberately left unfixed (see the closing entry below), per the task's own "stop and report, don't fix here" instruction.

**Shared helper: `tests/e2e/helpers/fixtures.ts`.** `uniqueTestId(label?)` — TEST-prefixed, unique both across runs (a per-process run token: base36 timestamp + 4 random chars) and within one run (a monotonic counter). `uniqueRealLookingPlate()` — the one deliberate exception to the TEST- prefix (see below). `seedDispatchablePallets()` — seeds N real, immediately-dispatchable `finished_pallets` (in_stock, o'tdi-verdict lab-passed, unclaimed) via direct writes through the dev-only `window.supabase` client, switching role per table's real RLS owner (menejer: kirim_orders/kirim_lines; ombor: wash_cycles/finished_pallets; laborator: lab_results) rather than a service-role bypass — same discipline every existing test in this suite already uses for direct-DB confirmation, extended here to direct-DB creation. `seedFilteredFinishedRequest()` — seeds the negative-case fixture for the TEST- prefix filter (see below). Every spec in the suite now imports from this file; no spec contains a literal `TEST-...-NN` anymore.

**A real bug in my own fixture-generator code, found by running the suite twice, not assumed correct.** `uniqueRealLookingPlate()`'s first draft sliced the first 4 characters of the run token (`runToken.slice(0, 4)`) — the MOST significant, slowest-changing digits of the base36-encoded timestamp (roughly a 27-minute window), the opposite of what varies between two runs seconds apart. Two consecutive runs of `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts` collided on the exact same generated plate. Fixed by slicing the token's LAST 5 characters instead, which always includes the token's random suffix — confirmed by running that spec twice back to back afterward, both green.

**Repaired the four unrunnable CHIQIM specs — assertions preserved, only fixture values and locator scope changed:**
- `chiqim-flow.spec.ts`, `chiqim-full-chain.spec.ts`, `chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts` — swapped their one-time hand-written SQL fixture (voided `finished_pallets` rows from an earlier, unidentified session) for `seedDispatchablePallets`. `chiqim-undo-scan`'s load-bearing RLS-refusal assertion (a real DELETE blocked by the `ombor_deletes` USING clause, confirmed via `.select()` returning zero rows rather than an error) is untouched and still passes.
- `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts` — its `REAL_PLATE` (deliberately non-TEST-prefixed, since `useFinishedChiqimRequests.ts` filters TEST- plates out by design) and its `FILTERED_PLATE` negative case are now both generated fresh every run instead of reused from another spec's one-time leftover row. **The task's requirement 5 asked to confirm this fixes the self-defeating "already permanently completed" bug rather than assume it — done**: ran the spec twice back to back; both passed, including the "not yet visible before completion" assertion that the old shared fixture could only ever satisfy once, ever.

**Two real, pre-existing test bugs found and fixed along the way, both exposed only because fixtures finally survive long enough to reach them:**
1. `chiqim-flow.spec.ts`'s final assertion, `page.getByRole('button', { name: new RegExp(PLATE) })`, was unscoped — after finishing a dispatch, the same request re-renders in Ombor's W2 ("Yuklandi") with the identical date/plate/driver text `chiqim-full-chain.spec.ts` already documents this exact trap for. `.not.toBeVisible()` on the unscoped locator found the request again in W2 and failed. Fixed by scoping to W1 specifically, matching the already-correct pattern next door.
2. `chiqim-flow.spec.ts`'s `getByText('4,000 kg')` (unscoped) matched the just-created request's own confirmation panel AND any other 4,000kg-net finished request already sitting in Menejer's own finished-requests list on the same page — a real ambiguity, invisible before because the old fixture always failed earlier in the test. Fixed by scoping to the specific saved-line row.

**One real cross-spec fixture-lifecycle bug, found via inspection before it could break a two-run proof, not by trial and error.** `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts` scans its second (passing) pallet and confirms `"✓ Aniq mos keldi"` but never clicked "Yuklashni yakunlash" — the request stayed genuinely open forever. `chiqim-flow.spec.ts`'s literal original assertion, `"Ochiq so'rov yo'q."` (Ombor's ENTIRE open-request list is empty), would fail on any later run once that stray open request existed. **Asked the user how to resolve this specific tension** between requirement 4 ("preserve assertions exactly") and reality (36 pre-existing open `chiqim_requests` already in the live DB from long before this session, with the void mechanism for that table explicitly out of scope) — confirmed: scope `chiqim-flow`'s assertion to its own request rather than the whole list, since a global-empty check can never pass again regardless of fixture freshness. Separately, and not in tension with anything — closed out `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate`'s own second request (added the missing "Yuklashni yakunlash" + confirm), pure test cleanup that stops it polluting any other spec's open-request state going forward.

**Requirement 6 — `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate`'s stale-copy failure: genuinely stale, not a collision, confirmed by re-running with fresh fixtures twice.** The test expected `"eng ko'p: 0 kg"` (ChiqimForm's "no other stock at all" feasibility message) but got `"eng yaqin: 0 kg yoki 4,000 kg"` on one run and `"...yoki 2,000 kg"` on the next — the exact "above" figure floats with whatever unrelated Subxon/Kalibr 6 stock happens to exist elsewhere in the live DB at that moment, not with anything this test creates. The original comment's assumption (empty-stock case always yields the "below only" message) was wrong: `checkFeasibility` operates on the GLOBAL available pool minus the specifically-gated pallets, not an empty array. **Fixed the string**, per the task's own instruction: asserts on the one thing that's actually invariant (`nearestBelow` is 0) via `/(eng ko'p|eng yaqin): 0 kg/`, tolerating either legitimate message shape instead of hardcoding one.

**Two consecutive full-suite runs, no manual cleanup, as the actual proof (per the task's own testing instruction):**
- **Run 1: 12/12 passed** (5.9 min) — every spec, including all four repaired CHIQIM tests and the stale-string fix, green together in one sweep for the first time.
- **Run 2, immediately following, same live DB, zero intervention: 11/12 passed** (6.2 min). The one failure is real and is NOT a fixture problem — see the next entry.

**A genuine application race condition, found by this task's own two-consecutive-runs proof, deliberately NOT fixed here — per the task's explicit instruction to stop and report rather than fix app code.** `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s multi-product test failed on run 2 with a wrong reconciliation figure: `"-1,200"` instead of the correct `"-200"` (sum-of-lines vs. gate-net variance). Traced to a real out-of-order-response race in `src/lib/effectiveQty.ts`'s `useEffectiveQty` hook, introduced by this session's own earlier fix (the "Weight authority" entry above): its `refresh()` is called fire-and-forget from `OmborIntakeTab.tsx`'s `handleAccept` (`refresh(); refreshEffectiveQty()`, neither awaited) once per accepted line, with no request-ordering guard. On a two-line order, accepting line 1 then line 2 in quick succession can fire two overlapping `fetchEffectiveQty` calls; if the FIRST call's network response resolves AFTER the second (a real possibility under variable network timing — this only manifested 6 minutes into a full-suite run, never in any faster standalone run), its stale, line-1-only result overwrites the correct, both-lines result via `setData`. This is a real, if narrow, window where the app can briefly show a wrong number — not caused by anything test-fixture-related, and not fixable by generating better fixtures. Flagged for the user rather than patched, since the fix is application code (e.g. an AbortController or a request-sequence guard in `useEffectiveQty`, or awaiting the refresh calls in `OmborIntakeTab.handleAccept`) and this task's scope is test infrastructure only.

## 2026-07-19 — effectiveQty refresh race: request-sequencing guard shipped; the exact reported "-1,200kg" repro traced to a SEPARATE, still-open bug
**Context:** follow-up to the flagged race above. Scope: fix the out-of-order-refresh race in `useEffectiveQty` itself (not per call site), collapse the redundant `fetchEffectiveQty` fetch inside `useMoykaSerials` if small, reduced testing (reproduce the two-line accept case, run the suite once).

**The guard, shipped.** `useEffectiveQty` (`src/lib/effectiveQty.ts`) now tracks a `latestRequestId` via `useRef`, incremented synchronously at the start of every `refresh()` call; a response is only applied via `setData` if no newer call has started since (`requestId === latestRequestId.current`). This is a request-sequencing guard, not `AbortController`-based cancellation or an awaited call chain — chosen because (a) it requires no change to `fetchEffectiveQty` or any call site, satisfying "the fix belongs in the hook, not in each call site"; (b) it mirrors, in spirit, the existing "cancelled" idiom already used in this codebase (`useGateHistory.ts`, `useIntakeHistory.ts`) for the same "ignore a stale response" problem — that idiom is closure-scoped to one `useEffect` run (reset by React's own cleanup on re-run) and doesn't cover repeat *manual* `refresh()` calls across a hook's lifetime, so this uses a `useRef` counter instead, scoped to the whole hook instance. Confirmed correct by direct observation: instrumented with temporary logging and reproduced a real out-of-order resolution (request 4 resolving *after* request 5 had already started) — the guard correctly discarded request 4's stale result and applied request 5's. All temporary instrumentation removed before shipping (see below).

**🚩 The exact reported repro case ("-1,200kg" instead of "-200kg") is NOT fully explained by this race, and remains open.** Reproducing it directly (6 attempts standalone, ~50% failure rate) and instrumenting every layer (`useEffectiveQty.refresh`, `OmborIntakeTab.handleAccept`, `IntakeAcceptForm.handleSubmit`) showed something different from the originally-suspected mechanism: on the failing runs, **`IntakeAcceptForm.handleSubmit` for the SECOND line's accept never logged at all** — not a validation early-return, not a caught error, not a thrown exception (no console error, matching how the failure was originally found: no console-error assertion caught it). Only ONE of the two lines' `storage_intake` rows ends up inserted, which alone fully explains "-1,200" (sum-of-lines = 1000, not 2000, against gate net 2200 → -1200) without needing any stale-response overwrite at all — a materially different bug from "two correct responses race, older wins," closer to "the second of two rapid form submissions on the same mount silently never fires its submit handler." This has the flavor of the React-controlled-input race already documented twice elsewhere in this app's history (2c/2d entries, and the `rewash-full-cycle.spec.ts`/`laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts` comments) — a second rapid interaction on the same component mount misbehaving — but this instance is different in kind (the SUBMIT EVENT itself appears not to fire, not a stale-value submit) and was not run to a confirmed root cause before scope was cut short deliberately (per instruction: ship the guard, skip further reproduction). **Do not treat the guard above as a complete fix for the originally-reported symptom** — it is a correct, real fix for the out-of-order-resolution class of bug (verified working on its own terms), but the specific "-1,200kg" failure mode likely has this second, distinct cause still needing investigation. Flagging explicitly rather than closing the loop silently.

**Redundant-fetch cleanup: attempted, then reverted per instruction, deferred.** Built and verified (typecheck clean) a version where `fetchEffectiveQty` accepts optional pre-fetched `intakes`/`sends` and `useMoykaSerials.ts` passes its own already-fetched rows through, removing 2 of 5 internal queries on that hot path. Reverted before shipping — not because it didn't work, but because the user explicitly asked to defer it to a later task once the race investigation ran long. `fetchEffectiveQty`'s doc comment now notes the redundancy explicitly so it isn't forgotten.

**All temporary debug instrumentation removed before shipping** — `console.log` tracing was added to and then stripped from `effectiveQty.ts`, `OmborIntakeTab.tsx`, `IntakeAcceptForm.tsx`, and `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s console listener. Confirmed via `grep -rn DEBUG src/ tests/` returning nothing before the final run.

**Testing.** `npm test` → 72/72 (unchanged, no pure-function logic touched). `npx tsc -b --noEmit` → clean. Full e2e suite run once (not the two-consecutive-runs treatment — reduced per the task): 12/12 passed, including both `effective-qty.spec.ts` tests. Given the race above is confirmed intermittent (~50% failure rate in isolated repro attempts) and the ACTUAL failure mode for the specific reported symptom is still not root-caused, a single green run here is evidence of "no new regression," not evidence the underlying flake is gone — worth re-running a few times in any future session touching this area, and worth picking up the still-open "second accept's submit silently doesn't fire" investigation before considering this fully closed.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** the void mechanism for CHIQIM tables (36 pre-existing open `chiqim_requests`, unrelated to this session, left in place), the redundant-query cleanup flagged in the prior regression pass, §3.2 reporting work, any other application code.

## 2026-07-20 — Step 10 prompt 1: reporting query engine, results table, totals strip, filter bar (SPEC.md v1.10 §3.2.1-3.2.4)

**Context:** first prompt of Step 10 — the shared reporting engine every later saved view (serial passport, stock-on-hand, client report, yield, WIP, Rahbar aggregates — all still out of scope) builds on. Explicit instruction: inspect existing implementation before coding, stop and report if ambiguity remains rather than inventing.

**Inspection done before writing any code:** read every relevant migration (`0003_operational.sql`, `0004_storage.sql`, `0009` through `0024`) rather than trusting `docs/SPEC.md §8`'s own pseudocode, per this project's own repeated finding that Phase 0's real schema differs from it. Two real, load-bearing discoveries from that inspection, not assumptions:

- **`finished_pallets.status='dispatched'` is dead code.** Confirmed via `useAvailableFinishedStock.ts`'s own comment and a full grep — nothing in this app ever writes it. "Dispatched" is actually "claimed in `dispatch_manifest` AND that dispatch's `gate_weighings` (dir=chiqim) row has `completed_at` set." Missing this would have made the CHIQIM side of the engine silently return zero "jo'natilgan" rows forever.
- **`gate_weighings.stage1_completed_at`** (added migration 0022, after `useGateHistory.ts` was written — that file's own comment calling gate history "no reliable date column" predates it) is exactly the "gate stage 1" timestamp §3.2.3's KIRIM date-basis rule needs, with `kirim_orders.order_date` as the documented, in-practice-unreached fallback (accepting intake requires stage 1 first, §5.1, so the fallback only matters defensively).

**Row-granularity decision — the single most foundational call in this prompt, made via reasoning rather than asking, then documented (not silently assumed):** a KIRIM row is one `kirim_lines` entry (one Barcode #1/serial — "an arrival line," matching the spec text literally). A CHIQIM row is one `finished_pallets` entry (one Barcode #2), **not** a whole CHIQIM request. Reasoning: Barcode #2, wash cycle, and kalibr are each listed as independent, combinable filter dimensions (§3.2.2) and only make sense at pallet granularity — a request-level row leaves "which pallet on this truck do you mean" unanswered for all three. This mirrors KIRIM's own row already being at serial (not truck) granularity for the identical reason. Confirmed self-consistent against §3.2.6's very different shape (stock-on-hand is "grouped by client → product → calibre," not a flat row list) — so "later views are built on this engine" means they reuse its pieces (filter bar, `effective_qty` integration, totals strip, export), not that every future view is literally this same row query with one filter flipped.

**Status filter (omborda / band qilingan / jo'natilgan / bekor qilingan) — resolved as a pallet-lifecycle derivation, not the `order_status` enum.** The four Uzbek labels match pallet lifecycle language exactly, not `kirim_orders`/`chiqim_requests.status`'s own enum values (kutilmoqda/qabul_qilindi/olib_ketildi/yakunlandi). `derivePalletStatus()` (`src/lib/reportQuery.ts`) derives it from `finished_pallets.status`, `dispatch_manifest` claim, and the claiming request's gate stage 2 — voided always wins regardless of claim state (confirmed against real data: several live test-fixture pallets are simultaneously claimed in `dispatch_manifest` AND `status='bekor_qilindi'`, because past test cleanups voided fixture pallets directly without touching the manifest row it "left in place" — see the 2026-07-19 entries. `derivePalletStatus`'s voided-first check handles this real, already-existing data shape correctly, not just a hypothetical). The two dateless states (omborda/band qilingan) return nothing in this prompt's results table by default (no governing event to date-filter on) — deliberate, not a gap, since a "still in storage" pallet belongs to the future stock-on-hand view's different shape; flagged as SPEC.md §7's new open item 14 to re-confirm once that view is actually built rather than silently carrying the assumption forward.

**Voided Barcode #2 lookup (§3.2.2's own hard requirement) — resolved without inventing a false 1:1 mapping.** No column anywhere links a voided pallet to a specific "replacement" barcode (confirmed by grepping every migration and every void-writing call site, `OmborTayyorTab.tsx handleRewash`) — a re-wash voids an entire cycle's worth of non-Konditirskiy pallets at once and the next cycle's daily-receipt-form output ("one pallet per save," §5.3) can produce any number of new pallets, not necessarily one. What IS unambiguous: only a serial's currently-*active* cycle can ever be voided (`activeCycleNo()`), so the successor is always exactly `voidedCycle + 1` — never a question of *which* later cycle to check, only *how many* (zero, one, or several) pallets that cycle has produced so far. Implemented as `VoidedBarcodeInfo` (`voidedCycle`, `successorCycle`, `successorBarcodes[]`) — the UI renders "yangi barkod: X" for exactly one, "yangi barkodlar: X, Y" for several, and "hali yangi barkod chiqarilmagan" for zero. Verified live (see below) against a genuinely voided, never-dispatched pallet with no successor cycle yet.

**Excel export: `exceljs`, not `xlsx`/SheetJS.** `npm install xlsx` pulled a version flagged by `npm audit` with a high-severity prototype-pollution/ReDoS pair, "no fix available" on the npm registry (SheetJS only publishes patched 0.20.x+ builds from their own CDN, not npm, over a registry dispute). The exploitable path in both advisories is parsing untrusted input, which this export-only usage never does — but shipping a flagged, unfixable-via-npm dependency for a brand-new feature was the wrong default when an actively-maintained alternative exists. Switched to `exceljs` (`npm uninstall xlsx && npm install exceljs`) — zero high/critical advisories; carries one moderate transitive `uuid` advisory (missing buffer-bounds check when a caller explicitly passes a buffer to `uuid`, which `exceljs` never does) that's a materially smaller, harder-to-reach risk than what was avoided.

**`HistoryView.tsx` reused as-is, not modified — the filter-bar collapse behaviour is new, additive furniture, not a retrofit.** `ReportFilterBar.tsx` manages its own collapsed/expanded state internally and is passed as `HistoryView`'s existing `filters` slot; Ombor's and Qorovul's existing Hisobotlar screens (`OmborHisobotlar.tsx`, `QorovulHisobotlar.tsx`) keep their current always-expanded filter row completely unchanged, per CLAUDE.md scope discipline ("build only what the task specifies").

**Phone-density decision, stated explicitly per the task's own instruction — prioritised fields in a card + expand.** Not really a choice among three options in practice: every existing list in this app (`OmborChiqimTab.tsx`, `LaboratorChiqimTab.tsx`, `OmborHisobotlar.tsx`, `QorovulHisobotlar.tsx`) already uses exactly this shape, and a `grep` for `<table` across `src/` returns nothing — there is no HTML table anywhere in this codebase to begin with, and a real grid wouldn't reflow to phone width regardless. "Results table" in the task's own prose means this card list, not a literal `<table>`. Card shows date/plate/driver + owner on the header line, type + quantity + flags (provisional/variance/verdict/voided) on a second line; the other ~7 fields sit behind the same expand toggle `OmborChiqimTab` already established. Row expand shows this row's own extra fields only — explicitly **not** the full serial passport (§3.2.5, out of scope this prompt: no per-wash-cycle history, no dispatch list).

**Verification, beyond the required smoke test:** ran the built screen live against the real shared dev DB (298 real rows across both directions) and cross-checked two rows directly against `execute_sql`: a multi-line KIRIM order (`declared_total=2000`, `net_kg=2200` → both lines correctly show `1,000 kg` each, never the gate net, plus the shared `+200 kg` truck variance) and a dispatched pallet (`weight_kg=4600`, `verdict=o_tdi` → matches the row exactly). Confirmed the voided-barcode override specifically: narrowed the date filter to a window that excludes a real voided pallet's date entirely (totals correctly read 0/0/0, "0 ta natija") and confirmed the barcode2 search still surfaced it via the dedicated callout, un-gated by the date filter — the literal requirement, not just the happy path. Excel export triggered with no console errors.

**Testing.** `npm test` → 84/84 (72 pre-existing + 12 new `reportQuery.test.ts` cases, pure logic only — `computeTotals`, `matchesText`, `washCycleMatches`, `labVerdictMatches`, `derivePalletStatus`, `passesDateOrStatusOverride`). `npx tsc -b --noEmit` → clean. New e2e smoke test (`reporting-query-engine.spec.ts`) written per the task's own reduced-testing instruction: seeds one single-line KIRIM order straight to a known gate net via direct writes (same lightweight pattern `helpers/fixtures.ts` already established), confirms the Hisobot row and the totals strip both show the gate-net figure (cross-checked against a direct `gate_weighings` query taken *before* touching the UI), then seeds a genuinely voided, never-dispatched pallet and confirms the exact-match callout — not "0 ta natija" silence. First attempt at this new test failed on an RLS violation inserting `finished_pallets` (a bug in the test itself — still logged in as QOROVUL from the gate-weighing seed step, not OMBOR, when `finished_pallets`' `ombor_writes` policy needs `my_role()='ombor'`); fixed by adding the missing role switch, then passed cleanly on its own and as part of the full suite. Full suite run **twice**: first run (before that fix) 8/13 — 5 failures, one of which was the test bug above; second run (after the fix) **12/13**. The one remaining failure both times, `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s "Multi-product truck" test, is the exact **already-documented, already-open** "-1,200kg" race from the 2026-07-19 "effectiveQty refresh race" entry above (reproducing there at ~50% standalone, explicitly *not* considered closed by that entry) — not a file this session touched, and not a new regression. The other three failures seen on the first run (`chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts`, `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts`, `step9-single-product-full-chain.spec.ts`) all passed cleanly on the second run with no code change to those files, confirming they were transient/DB-state flakiness, not something this session's changes caused — none of the four touch any route, component, or file this prompt added or modified (`App.tsx`'s new routes, `MenejerHome.tsx`'s new tab, `RahbarLayout.tsx`'s new nav link, or anything under `src/lib/report*.ts`/`src/pages/reports/`/`src/components/report/`).

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** all saved views (§3.2.5-§3.2.10 — serial passport, stock-on-hand, client report, yield, WIP, Rahbar aggregates), PDF/print layout, Uz/Ru export localisation, the CHIQIM void mechanism, the redundant `fetchEffectiveQty` cleanup inside `useMoykaSerials.ts` (still deferred from the prior entry), and the still-open "-1,200kg" investigation itself (unchanged from the 2026-07-19 entry — this session did not re-open it).

## 2026-07-20 — Commit/push catch-up, effectiveQty race status check, and reporting results view: desktop rework (Step 10 prompt 2)

**Context:** three-part task. (1) Commit and push everything in the working tree — flagged as unexpectedly large by the user, review before committing. (2) Confirm, don't fix, the `useEffectiveQty` "-1,200kg" race status. (3) Rework the Hisobot results view for desktop — Menejer/Rahbar work this screen on PCs, not phones.

**Git review — the surprise went the other way.** Expected to find the Step 8 prompt 2 (2a-2d) + Step 9 (prompts 1-4) backlog HANDOFF.md flagged as uncommitted still sitting there. It wasn't: `git log` showed all five of those commits already made and merged into `main` via **PR #25** (merge commit `049aa1e`), evidently in a separate session between this repo's last handoff and now — this session never ran a single `git commit` before this task. Checked thoroughly for anything else unaccounted for (`git stash list` — empty; `git diff --stat` against HEAD — only the 7 files this and the immediately-prior Step 10 prompt 1 session touched; every other local/remote branch is pre-existing feature work, not a new surprise). **Net finding: nothing was sitting uncommitted from before this session's own reporting work.** The only uncommitted content in the tree was entirely Step 10 prompt 1's own reporting engine (docs/SPEC.md, docs/DECISIONS.md, package.json/lock, App.tsx, MenejerHome.tsx, RahbarLayout.tsx, plus the new `src/lib/report*`/`src/components/report/`/`src/pages/reports/`/the new e2e spec) — reported plainly rather than assumed, since the user's own phrasing expected otherwise.

**Also caught: this session was working directly on `main`, not a feature branch.** The working tree's checked-out branch was `main` (left there by whatever session merged PR #25) — committing the Step 10 work as instructed would have landed it directly on `main`, violating CLAUDE.md's own "feature branch per task, open PR, never merge" workflow. Caught before pushing: moved the already-made local commit onto a new `feature/phase2-step10-reporting-query-engine` branch (`git branch` at the commit, `git checkout` it, then `git branch -f main origin/main` to put `main` back exactly where the remote has it), then pushed **that** branch. No PR opened, per instruction — the user opens it manually.

**Commit granularity: one commit.** Considered splitting further (e.g. dependency bump separate from feature code), but everything in the tree was genuinely one indivisible unit of work — a single prompt, entirely new files plus routing plus docs plus one test, all serving one screen, built in one continuous pass. Splitting it would have been artificial, not "logical chunks." Matches this repo's own precedent (`f1abec7`'s commit message explicitly combines two prompts into one commit "since they turned out to edit the same lines... never really separable checkpoints" — the inverse case, same principle).

**useEffectiveQty race — confirmed status, not touched.** Read the 2026-07-19 "effectiveQty refresh race" entry, re-read `src/lib/effectiveQty.ts` and `src/pages/ombor/IntakeAcceptForm.tsx` directly, and reproduced live via this session's own full-suite run (twice, in the prior Step 10 prompt 1 task): **the general out-of-order-refresh guard (`latestRequestId` ref counter in `useEffectiveQty.refresh()`) is built and shipped** — confirmed present, unchanged, doing its job. **The specific "-1,200kg" symptom's actual root cause was never fixed, only diagnosed, and remains fully open.** `IntakeAcceptForm.tsx` is unmodified from its pre-investigation shape — no guard, no debounce, no re-entrancy protection of any kind around its submit handler. The prior session's own diagnosis (a second rapid form submission on the same `OmborIntakeTab` mount silently never firing its submit handler — not a stale-response race, a different bug in kind) was never acted on; scope was cut short deliberately at the time, per that entry's own account. Confirmed still reproducing today: `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s "Multi-product truck" test failed with the exact same signature both times this session ran the full suite (`-1,200 kg` where `-200 kg` is expected). **Status: partially built (the wrong-order-resolution class is fixed) / not started (the actual reported symptom's root cause). Not touched this task, per instruction — report only.**

**Desktop rework — inspected before changing anything.** Reporting is Menejer/Rahbar-only (confirmed via `RoleRoute` guards on both routes) — neither role's other screens exist on this app at all outside the desktop-oriented `RoleShell` header, unlike Ombor/Qorovul/Laborator whose card-based screens are genuinely used on a warehouse floor from a phone. The card+expand pattern from Step 10 prompt 1 was a reasonable read of "reuse the existing pattern" in isolation, but wrong once "who actually uses this screen, on what device" is factored in — exactly the correction the task asked for.

**What changed:** `src/pages/reports/ReportRowCard.tsx` deleted; replaced by `ReportResultsTable.tsx` (the `<table>` + `<thead>`, wrapped in `overflow-x-auto`, `min-w-[960px]` on the table itself so columns never shrink) and `ReportTableRow.tsx` (one `<tr>` per row, a second conditional `<tr colSpan={11}>` for the expand panel — reusing `KirimRowDetail.tsx`/`ChiqimRowDetail.tsx` completely unchanged, only the trigger moved from a card's header button to a per-row expand button, `e.stopPropagation()`'d against the row's own `onClick` so the two toggles can't double-fire against each other). Columns: Yo'nalish, Sana, Seriya/Barcode #2, Buyurtmachi, Tur, Kalibr, Miqdor (right-aligned, `tabular-nums`), Moshina, Haydovchi, Holat, expand. `ReportFilterBar.tsx`'s `expanded` state now defaults to `true` (was `false`) — the collapse toggle itself stays (cheap, still useful on a narrower window), only the default flipped. `TotalsStrip.tsx` untouched, as instructed.

**This is the first `<table>` in the codebase, deliberately** — confirmed via the same `grep -r '<table' src/` check as before (still zero everywhere else). Every operational screen (`OmborChiqimTab`, `LaboratorChiqimTab`, both existing Hisobotlar screens) stays exactly as it was; this is a divergence for ONE surface with a genuinely different audience/device, not a reversal of the card-pattern rule established in the prior entry — both are correct for what they each serve.

**Verified live at desktop width (1280x800):** the table renders with all ten primary columns visible, the filter bar starts expanded (no click needed), and expand-toggling a row correctly reveals the exact same detail content as before (spot-checked against this session's own earlier `TEST-HISOBOT-...` fixture row, still showing `1,050 kg` / `+50 kg farq` correctly). At mobile width (375px): confirmed via `getComputedStyle` that the table's wrapper has `overflow-x: auto` and a `scrollWidth` (1341px) well beyond its `clientWidth` (341px) — the table scrolls horizontally within its own contained box, while `document.body.scrollWidth` stays exactly at the viewport width, i.e. the page itself never gains a horizontal scrollbar. Columns don't shrink or wrap; the whole table just scrolls sideways, per the task's own requirement.

**Testing.** `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. `npm test` 84/84 (unchanged — no pure-logic files touched this task). Existing e2e smoke test (`reporting-query-engine.spec.ts`) needed a fix of its own after the rework: it unconditionally clicked the filter-bar toggle assuming a collapsed start (a real assumption this exact task invalidated) — now expanded by default, that click COLLAPSED the bar instead, timing out the next step. Fixed by removing the now-unnecessary click and updating the row locator from a card's class selector to `table tbody tr` (the only two lines the table swap actually broke); passed cleanly on its own afterward. Full suite run once per the reduced-testing instruction: **11/13 passing.** Two failures, neither new: `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s multi-product test is the same already-open "-1,200kg" race confirmed above (third reproduction this session, across three separate full-suite runs); `chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts` timed out waiting on a Menejer CHIQIM form dropdown — a file this task never touched (only `ReportFilterBar.tsx`/`ReportResultsTable.tsx`/`ReportTableRow.tsx`/`HisobotTab.tsx` and docs changed), and one that passed cleanly in this session's own immediately-prior run with zero code change to it or its dependencies in between — consistent with the same pre-existing, DB-state-driven flakiness this suite has repeatedly shown, not a regression from the table rework.

## 2026-07-20 — IntakeAcceptForm dropped submit: root-caused and fixed (TWO mechanisms, not one)

**Context:** the "-1,200kg instead of -200kg" bug, open since the 2026-07-19 "effectiveQty refresh race" entry, which explicitly diagnosed-but-didn't-fix it and flagged the prior session's own mechanism guess ("closer to... a second rapid form submission on the same mount not firing... has the flavor of the React-controlled-input race") as unconfirmed. This task's instruction: confirm or replace that diagnosis via direct reproduction, don't inherit it, then fix at the form/handler level.

**Diagnosis method:** temporary instrumentation (`console.log` with a `DEBUGRACE`-prefixed marker, mirroring the prior session's own approach) at every layer — `IntakeAcceptForm`'s render/`handleSubmit`/mount-unmount, `OmborIntakeTab`'s `handleAccept`/render/open-button clicks, `PhotoField`'s compress/`onChange`. Ran `tests/e2e/effective-qty.spec.ts -g "Multi-product"` directly (it reproduces the failure every single run, not intermittently, contrary to the "~50%" figure recorded for the standalone repro style used in the prior session) with the test's own console listener temporarily broadened to print these markers live. All instrumentation fully removed before the final fix shipped — confirmed via `grep -rn DEBUGRACE src/ tests/` returning nothing, same discipline as the prior session.

**The prior session's diagnosis did NOT hold, and was more specific than the evidence actually supported.** It correctly observed that `IntakeAcceptForm.handleSubmit` for the second line never fires, but characterized it as "the flavor of" a controlled-input race on a single, reused component mount. Direct reproduction shows two DIFFERENT, independent mechanisms, neither of which is a controlled-input race, and neither of which involves the SAME mount at all — line B's form is a completely separate component instance from line A's:

1. **Mechanism 1 — `activeSerial` is a single tab-wide "which row is expanded" value, and `handleAccept`'s completion callback closed it unconditionally.** `OmborIntakeTab.tsx` renders at most one `IntakeAcceptForm` at a time, gated by a single `activeSerial` string. Accepting line A starts an async upload+insert; if the operator opens line B's form before A's accept resolves (a completely normal multi-line workflow — not a rapid-click edge case, just two lines on one truck), `activeSerial` becomes B. When A's accept finally resolves, the old code unconditionally called `setActiveSerial(null)` — closing B's form, discarding whatever the operator had already filled in, with no error (from the outer "Qabul qilish" button's own perspective nothing went wrong, so nothing complained). Fixed in `OmborIntakeTab.tsx`'s `handleAccept`: `setActiveSerial((current) => (current === line.serial ? null : current))` — only clear the active row if it's still THIS accept's own row.

2. **Mechanism 2 — the real, dominant cause — `useIntakeLines`'s `refresh()` re-flips `loading` to `true` on every call, and `OmborIntakeTab` unmounts its ENTIRE tree while `loading`.** `handleAccept` calls `refresh()` (fire-and-forget) after every successful accept — necessary, since the "Kutilmoqda"/"Qabul qilingan" lists need the fresh data. But `useIntakeLines.refresh()` set `loading` back to `true` at the START of every call, not just the first, and `OmborIntakeTab.tsx` has `if (loading || moykaLoading) return null` — a guard clearly meant for "no data yet," not "a background revalidation is in flight." The consequence: line A's background refresh (triggered by A's OWN accept) blanks the WHOLE SCREEN while it's in flight, then remounts everything once it resolves — including a completely unrelated line B's form, mid-fill, as a BRAND NEW component instance with reset internal state (`pilePhoto` back to `null`). This is why fix #1 alone was insufficient and left the bug reproducing identically: `activeSerial` correctly stayed pointed at B the whole time, but B's own component got torn down and rebuilt anyway by the parent returning `null`, which fix #1 does nothing about. Confirmed directly with a temporary `useEffect(() => { ...mount...; return () => {...unmount...} }, [])` in `IntakeAcceptForm` — logged a genuine, isolated unmount of row B (not the immediate mount→unmount→mount triple that's just React StrictMode's dev-only double-invoke, a red herring present throughout every trace) landing exactly when A's `handleAccept` finished, followed by a fresh mount with `pilePhoto` back to `false`. Fixed in `useIntakeLines.ts`: a `hasLoadedOnce` ref gates `setLoading(true)` to the first call only — every later `refresh()` still updates `lines`, just without ever re-blanking the screen. `useIntakeLines` has exactly one consumer (`OmborIntakeTab.tsx`, confirmed via `grep -rn "useIntakeLines("`), so this doesn't risk any other screen's behaviour.
