**Both fixes are required together — verified by removing each independently during development.** With only fix #1: `activeSerial` stayed correctly pointed at B, but B's form still got unmounted/remounted via the `loading` guard, and the bug reproduced identically (same `-1,200kg`, same missing second `storage_intake` row, confirmed via a repeat DB query). Only after adding fix #2 did the test pass.

**Verification:** the reproducing test (`effective-qty.spec.ts -g "Multi-product"`) passed **4 consecutive runs** after both fixes (not just once — this bug's own history warns against trusting a single green run for a timing-dependent issue). Directly queried `storage_intake` for the three most recent test runs' plates and confirmed both lines' rows exist with real `actual_qty`/`confirmed_at` values every time, not inferred from the UI alone. `npm test` 84/84 unchanged. `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. Full suite run once per the task's own reduced-testing instruction: **13/13 passing** — a full clean sweep, including `chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts`, which failed with an unrelated timeout in the immediately-prior (Step 10 prompt 2) run; passing cleanly here with no change to that file corroborates that it really was transient DB-state flakiness, not a real issue.

**Silent-failure elimination, per the task's own requirement:** neither fix introduces a NEW blocking/disabled state — both make the second submit **fire correctly** rather than visibly-prevented, which is the better of the two outcomes the task allowed for ("either fires correctly or is visibly prevented"): the operator's normal multi-line workflow (accept line 1, immediately start line 2 while line 1 saves in the background) now just works, with no new restriction to explain or work around.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** the `fetchEffectiveQty` redundant-fetch cleanup (still deferred, unrelated to this bug), remaining §3.2 reporting views, the CHIQIM void mechanism, and `chiqim-undo-scan.spec.ts`'s unrelated flakiness noted in the immediately-prior entry.

## 2026-07-20 — Reporting engine cleanup: test-data DELETE, TEST- filter, redundant-fetch collapse

**Context:** three-part task. Delete the orphaned `TEST-`-prefixed CHIQIM debris this whole project's testing history kept flagging-but-never-fixing (36+ open `chiqim_requests` in the last several entries above, no void mechanism ever built for those tables, deletion explicitly chosen as the resolution this time rather than building one). Filter `TEST-` rows out of the reporting engine so tomorrow's test runs don't repopulate what today's cleanup removes. Collapse `fetchEffectiveQty`'s redundant fetch inside `useMoykaSerials.ts`, deferred twice already (2026-07-19, 2026-07-20 Step 10 prompt 1 entries).

### 1. Deletion — a real, deliberate exception to the append-only lock

**🔒 Raw `DELETE` on `TEST-`-prefixed fixtures is a stated, deliberate exception to SPEC.md §2.15's "never DELETE, only void" rule — not an abandonment of it.** That rule governs *operational* data: real events this app's audit trail must never lose (a real intake, a real dispatch, a real wash cycle). `TEST-`-prefixed rows are not operational data — they are this project's own testing infrastructure's disposable output, created solely to prove code paths work, carrying zero business meaning once the run that created them has finished. `chiqim_requests`/`chiqim_lines`/`dispatch_manifest`/`gate_weighings` were flagged **four separate times** across this project's history (2026-07-17 and 2026-07-18 entries above) as having no void mechanism at all, and building one was explicitly out of scope each time (a schema change for a problem DELETE already solves correctly for non-operational rows). This entry is the record so a future reader sees this was a considered call, not a silent reversal of the append-only convention — the convention is unchanged and still applies to every real table's real rows, including `TEST-`-prefixed rows' own `finished_pallets`/`wash_cycles` (still voided, never deleted, unaffected by this cleanup).

**Inspected before deleting, not assumed:** confirmed current counts (`chiqim_requests`=96 — 53 `kutilmoqda`, 43 `olib_ketildi`; `dispatch_manifest`=85; `chiqim_lines`=82; `gate_weighings` dir=chiqim=34, all scoped to `plate LIKE 'TEST-%'`) via direct query before writing any `DELETE`. **Checked every one of the 85 `dispatch_manifest` rows' pallets back to their ORIGINATING `kirim_orders.plate`** (not just the claiming request's own plate) before deleting anything — every single one traced back to a `TEST-`-prefixed originating order (mostly `TEST-SEED-*`/`TEST-LAB-*`/`TEST-STEP9-CHAIN-*` from `helpers/fixtures.ts`'s seeding, plus the older manually-named `TEST-CHIQIM-*` fixtures from Step 7). **Zero real material was ever at risk** — confirmed, not assumed, per the task's explicit instruction to flag rather than assume if any had turned out real.

**Executed, user confirmed all 96 (both statuses, no narrower scope):**
```sql
delete from dispatch_manifest
where request_id in (select id from chiqim_requests where plate like 'TEST-%');

delete from chiqim_lines
where request_id in (select id from chiqim_requests where plate like 'TEST-%');

delete from gate_weighings
where request_id in (select id from chiqim_requests where plate like 'TEST-%');

delete from chiqim_requests
where plate like 'TEST-%';
```
**Confirmed final state:** all four counts (`chiqim_requests`/`dispatch_manifest`/`chiqim_lines`/`gate_weighings` scoped to `TEST-%`) at exactly 0. 34 `chiqim_requests` remain — pre-existing, non-`TEST-`-prefixed rows from before this project's `TEST-` fixture convention existed (same class of legacy artifact as the 6 non-`TEST-` `kirim_lines` rows the Hisobot filter also leaves visible, see below) — untouched, out of scope per "scope strictly to `TEST-` prefixed plates." 39 previously-claimed `in_stock` pallets are now unclaimed and available again (4 more were already `bekor_qilindi` and stay that way — releasing a voided pallet's stale claim doesn't un-void it). `finished_pallets`/`wash_cycles`/`kirim_orders`/`kirim_lines`/`storage_intake` were not touched by any of these four statements — only the CHIQIM-side claim chain was in scope.

### 2. TEST- filter in the reporting engine

Added `isTestPlate()` (`src/lib/reportQuery.ts`) — same unconditional, no-toggle precedent `useFinishedChiqimRequests.ts` already established ("no screen in this app has ever built a show-test-data switch"). Applied once in the shared query layer (`useReportQuery.ts`), not per-view, so every future saved view built on this engine inherits it automatically:
- KIRIM rows: excluded when their own `kirim_orders.plate` is `TEST-`-prefixed.
- CHIQIM rows: excluded when **either** the claiming `chiqim_requests.plate` **or** the pallet's own **originating** `kirim_orders.plate` is `TEST-`-prefixed (via the same `kirim_lines → kirim_orders` join the row already makes for target-quality data) — a request-only check would miss every still-in-storage or voided test pallet, which has no dispatch plate of its own to catch. Checked and excluded before the voided-barcode search even runs, so a `TEST-` fixture is invisible to this engine end to end, not merely absent from the default table.

**Verified live:** Menejer's Hisobot, default filters (last 30 days, both directions) — **298+ rows down to 6**, all 6 being the same pre-`TEST-`-convention legacy rows noted above (`150726-00{1,2,3}`, `140726-00{1,2,3}`). Zero console errors.

### 3. `fetchEffectiveQty` redundant-fetch collapse

Built exactly the design the 2026-07-19 entry already validated once and reverted only for timing reasons ("collapsing turned out non-trivial to do safely alongside the race fix, deferred rather than bundled in"): `fetchEffectiveQty` (`src/lib/effectiveQty.ts`) now accepts an optional third `prefetched: { intakes?, sends? }` argument; when present, it resolves those two queries from the given rows instead of re-fetching `storage_intake`/`moyka_sends` unfiltered a second time. Optional and additive — `useEffectiveQty` (`OmborIntakeTab.tsx`, `KirimOrdersList.tsx`) and `useReportQuery.ts` both omit it and keep their original always-fetch-fresh behaviour unchanged. Only `useMoykaSerials.ts` passes its own already-fetched `intakes`/`sends` through (the sole caller with those rows already in hand from the same refresh).

**`useMoykaOutput.ts` does NOT call `fetchEffectiveQty` at all — confirmed again** (third time across sessions; see the 2026-07-19 entry's own correction of an earlier session's inaccurate claim to the contrary). The task's own framing assumed both hooks call it; only `useMoykaSerials.ts` actually does, so that's the only place this collapse applies.

**Verified via live network trace, not just code inspection** (this environment's own request-log tool doesn't surface Supabase's `fetch()`-based calls, but `performance.getEntriesByType('resource')` does): cleared the resource-timing buffer, remounted Ombor's Moyka tab, and inspected every `storage_intake`/`moyka_sends` request fired. Only the two already-necessary fetches appeared (`useMoykaSerials`'s own `storage_intake?select=serial,actual_qty` and `moyka_sends?select=id,serial,sent_date,qty_kg,wash_cycle`, plus `useMoykaOutput`'s own distinctly-shaped `moyka_sends?select=serial,qty_kg,sent_date,wash_cycle` — all present because OmborMoykaTab genuinely consumes both hooks, section-mirroring the Tayyor tab's Window 1, unrelated to this change). `fetchEffectiveQty`'s own distinctly-shaped, previously-present `storage_intake?select=serial,actual_qty` and `moyka_sends?select=serial,sent_date` calls (its minimal, `useMoykaSerials`-independent column sets) are **absent** — the two round trips are confirmed gone, not just theoretically skippable. Functional correctness unaffected: Moyka tab still shows correct `Qabul qilingan`/`Qoladi` figures and the correct `+200 kg` truck-variance note for every serial checked.

### Testing

`npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. `npm test` 85/85 (84 pre-existing + 1 new `isTestPlate` test, 6 assertions).

**Own smoke test needed a fixture fix, caused by this task's own filter.** `reporting-query-engine.spec.ts` (Step 10 prompt 1) seeded its KIRIM order under a `TEST-HISOBOT-...` plate — which the new `isTestPlate()` filter now correctly excludes, so the test's own row stopped appearing in Hisobot. Fixed by switching to `uniqueRealLookingPlate()` (`tests/e2e/helpers/fixtures.ts`), the same non-`TEST-`-prefixed-identifier helper `menejer-chiqim-finished-view.spec.ts` already uses for the identical reason against `useFinishedChiqimRequests`' own filter — updated that helper's comment to note it now has two consumers, not one. Confirmed passing 4 times after the fix (3 standalone + this run), after one earlier standalone failure that turned out to be a transient load spike (a live manual check of Hisobot immediately after showed normal, fast loading — not a systemic slowdown).

**Full suite run twice** (the first attempt returned `ERR_CONNECTION_REFUSED` across the board — the dev server wasn't up, an environment mistake on this session's part, not a test result; discarded). Clean run: **10/13 passing**, including `reporting-query-engine.spec.ts` cleanly. Three failures:
- `chiqim-full-chain.spec.ts` and `step9-single-product-full-chain.spec.ts`: timeouts in scan-confirmation and Tayyor-finish flows this task never touched — consistent with this suite's already well-documented DB-growth-driven flakiness (see multiple prior entries).
- `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s multi-product test: failed again, but with a **different** signature than the original bug (`-2,200 kg` reconciliation, not the original `-1,200 kg`) — the first failure of this specific test since the two-part dropped-submit fix shipped and passed cleanly 6 consecutive times this session (4 standalone + 2 prior full-suite runs). Not re-investigated — out of scope for this task, and one data point against six clean ones isn't grounds to declare the fix incomplete, but it's flagged here rather than silently ignored: worth a closer look if it recurs.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** any void mechanism or status column for `chiqim_requests` (deliberately not built — deletion is the chosen approach, see above), remaining §3.2 saved views, demo-data seeding (explicitly deferred to the next prompt), and re-investigating the `effective-qty.spec.ts` anomaly noted just above.

## 2026-07-20 — The `-2,200kg` failure diagnosed: neither a stale test nor the dropped-submit bug recurring

**Context:** the immediately-prior entry flagged a single failure of `effective-qty.spec.ts`'s multi-product test with a `-2,200kg` reconciliation instead of the expected `-200kg` — a different signature from the already-fixed `-1,200kg` dropped-submit bug, occurring right after the 96-row `TEST-` CHIQIM deletion. Task: determine whether this is a stale test expectation reacting to the changed DB state, or a real regression, before doing anything else (seeding changes stock again and would have muddied the picture).

**Ruled out mechanically: the deletion cannot be the cause.** All four `DELETE` statements from the prior entry scope by `chiqim_requests.plate` or `request_id` — and every KIRIM-direction `gate_weighings` row has `request_id = NULL` by construction (the `check (num_nonnulls(order_id, request_id) = 1)` constraint). `NULL IN (subquery)` never matches in SQL, so the deletion provably never touched a KIRIM-side row. No other deleted table (`chiqim_lines`, `dispatch_manifest`) has any relationship to `kirim_orders`/`kirim_lines`/`storage_intake` at all. The temporal proximity in the prior entry was coincidence, not causation.

**Ruled out as a stale test expectation.** The test creates its own fresh serials every run (`uniqueTestId('EFFQTY')`) and asserts against those specific serials by exact match, not against any list-wide count or emptiness check that pre-existing DB rows could perturb. Its expectations (`-200kg` reconciliation for a 2000kg-declared/2200kg-gate-net multi-line truck) are unconditionally correct regardless of how many other rows exist in the shared DB.

**Diagnosed via direct reproduction (temporary `DEBUGRECON` instrumentation in `effectiveQty.ts`/`OmborIntakeTab.tsx`, removed before this commit, confirmed via `grep`):**
- Stacking 5 Playwright runs of this test back-to-back in a single command produced **5/5 failures at the LOGIN step** (`waiting for navigation to **/menejer**`, 30s timeout) — never even reaching the code under test. A manual fresh login in the browser at the same moment completed instantly. This confirms the failures were caused by **resource contention from running many heavy browser instances in immediate succession** on this session's dev machine, not a Supabase or app-level outage.
- Run **alone**, with normal resource availability, the test passed cleanly **3 consecutive times**, and the instrumentation confirmed its own freshly-created order's `storage_intake` rows were both present and summed correctly (`sumOfLines=2000`, the expected `-200kg` reconciliation) every time.
- Historical console output accumulated in the browser session (from many earlier runs today, both pre- and post-dropped-submit-fix) shows the OLDER `-1,200kg`-style single-missing-line pattern recurring across several historical orders — but none from after the fix shipped, and none showing the `sumOfLines=0` (`-2,200kg`) pattern at all in this data. The one observed `-2,200kg` occurrence was not reproduced live.

**Verdict: not a stale test, not a recurrence of the fixed dropped-submit bug, and not attributable to the deletion.** It is most consistent with a **separate, narrow, timing-dependent display-staleness race**, distinct in mechanism from what was fixed — the write itself lands correctly (confirmed both by direct query after the original failure and by every clean reproduction attempt), but the UI's `effectiveQty` state can apparently show a transient, not-yet-caught-up value under unusually heavy concurrent load, which is exactly the condition (many stacked full-suite/standalone runs) this session had just subjected the environment to. One plausible contributing factor found but not confirmed: `useEffectiveQty`'s own `key` (`serials.join(',')`) is derived from `useIntakeLines`' unordered, no-`ORDER BY` refetch of the entire `kirim_lines` table — if row order isn't stable across two fetches of an ever-growing table, `key` can change without the underlying serial *set* changing, triggering an extra implicit `refresh()` via the `useEffect` dependency whose resolution order relative to the two intentional post-accept refreshes isn't guaranteed. Not fixed — out of scope per this task's own boundary ("any app code changes beyond fixing the test if it turns out to be a test issue"), and it isn't a test issue, so neither the test nor app code was touched. Flagged here for whoever next has cause to look at `useEffectiveQty`'s dependency stability.

**No code changes made as a result of this investigation** — `effective-qty.spec.ts`, `effectiveQty.ts`, and `OmborIntakeTab.tsx` are all back to exactly what they were before this diagnosis (confirmed via `git diff` showing no residual changes beyond the temporary instrumentation, which was fully removed).

## 2026-07-20 — Demo data for reporting pilot: seeded, deliberately non-TEST-, removal path documented

**Context:** the reporting engine (SPEC.md §3.2.1-3.2.4) had no realistic data to evaluate against — only the accumulated `TEST-`-prefixed automated-test fixtures (now excluded by the immediately-prior entry's filter) and a handful of pre-existing `Test Client A/B/C` rows predating the `TEST-` convention. Task: seed a small, realistic dataset that exercises every filter dimension and both dispatch outcomes, so Menejer/Rahbar can actually evaluate the Hisobot view before the pilot.

**Deliberately NOT `TEST-`-prefixed.** The whole point is to remain visible under `isTestPlate()` (`reportQuery.ts`), which excludes any `TEST-` plate unconditionally. Uses four brand-new clients and ordinary-looking plates/drivers instead: `supabase/seed/demo-data-2026-07-20.sql`, a single `do $$ ... $$` PL/pgSQL block, atomic (one failed statement rolls back everything).

**Nine "stories" (KIRIM orders), 2026-05-04 to 2026-07-20** — the eighth and ninth added incrementally (see below):
1. Boysun / Subxon, sulfur target, single cycle, fully dispatched incl. Konditirskiy.
2. Farg'ona / Isfara, natural, single cycle, partially dispatched (2 of 3 pallets left in stock).
3. Samarqand / Subxon + Qand qizil, multi-line — lineA dispatched, lineB's pallets deliberately left with no CHIQIM lab result yet (awaiting lab).
4. Toshkent / Subxon, re-wash (cycle 1 `qayta_yuvish` → cycle 2 `o'tdi`), Konditirskiy pallets from BOTH cycles left in stock forever.
5. Boysun / Isfara + Subxon, multi-line — lineA dispatched, lineB lab-passed but deliberately not dispatched.
6. Farg'ona / Qand qizil, natural, re-wash #2 (same shape as story 4, both cycle-2 pallets dispatched).
7. Samarqand / Subxon, KIRIM lab done, raw deliberately never sent to Moyka (still-in-storage raw stock).
8. Toshkent / Isfara, gate stage 1 only (no stage 2 → provisional `effective_qty`), no KIRIM lab result yet.
9. **Added mid-execution, on explicit request** ("nothing currently represents a batch with a `qayta_yuvish` verdict that hasn't been re-sent yet — that's a real WIP state the stuck-items view will need"): Samarqand / Isfara, cycle 1 fails lab (`qayta_yuvish`) and is voided, but deliberately has **no cycle 2 at all** — distinct from stories 4/6, which show the re-wash already completed. A small, self-contained append (no restructuring): reuses the same owner/product/calibre/profile IDs, needed zero changes to the cleanup script since it already scopes generically by owner_id through the same CTE chain.

**Row counts as executed** (verified by direct count against the same owner-scoped CTE the cleanup script uses, immediately after running the seed):

| Table | Rows |
|---|---|
| `owners` | 4 |
| `kirim_orders` | 9 |
| `kirim_lines` | 11 |
| `gate_weighings` | 15 |
| `storage_intake` | 11 |
| `lab_results` | 20 |
| `moyka_sends` | 11 |
| `wash_cycles` | 11 |
| `finished_pallets` | 26 |
| `chiqim_requests` | 6 |
| `dispatch_manifest` | 12 |
| **Total** | **136** |

**Pre-flight checks done before executing, not assumed:** all 11 hardcoded UUIDs the script references (3 product types, 4 calibres, 4 role profiles) verified live against the DB and matched their expected labels exactly. Confirmed the two capped queries `useReportQuery.ts` relies on (`storage_intake`, `dispatch_manifest`, both `FETCH_CAP=500`) had well under 500 rows each even after seeding (320→331 and 57→69 respectively), so none of the seeded rows risk being pushed out by newer unrelated test-run activity. Confirmed no owner-name collision with the pre-existing `Test Client A/B/C` rows.

**Verified live in Menejer's Hisobot (not just by re-reading the query code):**
- All nine stories' events render, unfiltered by `isTestPlate()`, at the full 2026-05-01–2026-07-20 date range.
- **Totals reconcile exactly against hand-computed expected values, cross-checked two different ways.** Owner-scoped: Boysun alone → Kirim 7,400 kg / Chiqim 6,050 kg (matches the multi-line-never-adopts-gate-net rule applied to story 5's two lines, 1,000 + 1,200 kg, each shown with its own truck-level `+100 kg farq` note rather than a redistributed value). Toshkent alone → Kirim 5,900 kg (4,100 gate net + 1,800 provisional intake) / Chiqim 2,450 kg. Cross-cut filter (direction=CHIQIM, Tur=Subxon, Kalibr=Kalibr 6, Laboratoriya xulosasi=O'tdi) → 5,750 kg across three different owners' pallets (Toshkent 1,150 + Samarqand 1,000 + Boysun 1,800 + 1,800), matching the sum of those four pallets' own `weight_kg` exactly.
- Filters checked individually and combined: direction, date range, owner, product type, calibre, wash cycle (`2+` correctly returns only story 4's cycle-2 pallets, excluding its still-in-stock cycle-1 Konditirskiy survivor), lab verdict.
- **Voided-Barcode-#2-findability (§3.2.2) confirmed working as designed, via the mechanism actually built — not the one a first guess would expect.** The "Bekor qilingan" status dropdown alone returns nothing for a voided pallet, because a voided pallet is never in `dispatch_manifest` and the CHIQIM query only reaches into `finished_pallets` directly when a Barcode #2 search string is present (`useReportQuery.ts`'s own comment on this). The actual findability path is the **exact-match red callout** above the table (`HisobotTab.tsx`'s `showVoidedCallout`), triggered by typing the barcode into the Barcode #2 field. Confirmed on two different pallets: story 4's `PLT-200726-216-06-1` correctly lists all three of its cycle-2 successors (including the Konditirskiy one); story 9's new `PLT-200726-222-06-1` correctly shows "Sikl 2 hali yangi barkod chiqarilmagan" (cycle 2 not yet issued) — the exact WIP state story 9 was added to cover.
- **Per-cycle loss% is NOT surfaced anywhere in this reporting view, by original Task 1 design, not a seeding gap.** `wash_cycles.final_loss_pct` isn't part of either `KirimReportRow` or `ChiqimReportRow` at all; `KirimRowDetail.tsx`'s own header comment says so explicitly ("NOT the full serial passport... no wash-cycle-by-wash-cycle breakdown" — that's §3.2.5, a different, not-yet-built view). What this view DOES correctly distinguish per cycle: the `Yuvish sikli` filter, each pallet's own cycle number, and — for a voided pallet — its cycle and successor-cycle linkage via the callout above. Story 4 and story 9 both exercise this correctly; neither shows a loss-percentage figure, because none of this reporting layer's rows carry one.

**Removability.** `supabase/seed/demo-data-2026-07-20-cleanup.sql` — a sequence of standalone `DELETE`s, each scoped by the four owner names via its own `WITH demo_owners AS (...)` CTE (repeated per statement, since CTEs don't persist across statements), chaining through orders/serials/requests/cycles as needed, in dependency order: dispatch chain → pallets/lab/wash/moyka chain → KIRIM intake/gate/lines/orders → owners last. Same deliberate append-only exception as the immediately-prior entry's `TEST-` deletion (this is disposable demo/pilot data, not operational data) — **run this before the pilot goes live on real client data**, or any time this demo set needs to be cleared and re-seeded.

**Testing.** `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. `npm test` 85/85 (unchanged — no pure-logic files touched by seeding). Full Playwright suite run once per the reduced-testing instruction: **9 passed, 4 failed.** Each failure isolated by re-running alone, not left as a single ambiguous full-suite number:
- `chiqim-flow.spec.ts` and `chiqim-full-chain.spec.ts` both **passed cleanly in isolation** — their full-suite failures were transient (one a plain login timeout), the same DB-growth/resource-contention flakiness this suite has repeatedly shown across many prior entries, unrelated to this seed.
- `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts` **fails deterministically (confirmed twice), and is a direct, traceable consequence of this seed's own data, not a new bug.** It asserts a hardcoded `/0 kg/` availability message for Subxon+Kalibr 6 — the exact fragility already flagged in an earlier entry ("depended on NO other unrelated Subxon/Kalibr 6 stock existing anywhere in the shared DB... don't hardcode one branch of a multi-branch UI message"). Story 5's lineB deliberately leaves a lab-passed, un-dispatched 600 kg Subxon/Kalibr 6 pallet in stock (exactly the "lab-passed but left in stock" scenario the task asked for) — the app now correctly reports real 600 kg availability where the test still expects zero. The app is behaving correctly; the test's assumption is what's now false. Not fixed — touching this test wasn't requested, and the task's own scope excludes new/modified e2e tests.
- `laborator-kirim.spec.ts` fails reproducibly but with a **different specific assertion each run** (once a `Yakunlangan` visibility timeout, once a `Sera kutilmoqda` count timeout) against **its own fresh, self-generated serial each time** — not a fixed collision with any specific seeded row the way the hard-gate test is. Traced to likely cause: `useLaboratorKirim.ts` does a fully unbounded, unordered-at-the-query-level fetch across `kirim_lines`/`storage_intake`/`lab_results` (486/343/248 rows at the time of this check) and stitches client-side; `kirim_lines` grew by ~176 rows in the few minutes between two direct counts taken during this same session, evidence of **active concurrent write load on this shared live DB from something other than this session** (this seed only added 11 `kirim_lines` rows). Most consistent with dataset-size/contention-driven timing flakiness, not a structural conflict with this seed's specific data. Flagged here, not fixed — out of scope, and not conclusively caused by this task's own changes.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** the `-2,200kg` flaky race (diagnosed in the entry above, deliberately not re-opened), remaining §3.2 saved views, any app code changes, and the two test-fragility findings just above (neither is an app regression).

## 2026-07-20 — Reporting engine: server-side query (filtering, pagination, totals moved into Postgres)

**Context:** the reporting engine (Task: reporting query engine, above) fetched broad row sets client-side (`FETCH_CAP=500` on `storage_intake`/`dispatch_manifest`) and filtered/aggregated in JavaScript — an active filter never reduced what was downloaded, totals were summed over whatever happened to already be in memory, and the 500-row cap was a silent truncation point that would drop real data within months of real growth. Moved filtering, pagination (100 rows/page), and totals into Postgres; removed `FETCH_CAP` entirely.

**Why a view/RPC was necessary, not optional.** A KIRIM row's own quantity (`effective_qty`) isn't a stored column — it's a derived value (single-line → gate net once stage 2 completes; multi-line → always its own intake figure, never gate net) computed in `weightAuthority.ts`'s `deriveEffectiveQty`. Filtering/aggregating server-side while still computing each row's quantity in JavaScript is not possible — the derivation had to move into SQL alongside the filtering.

**Shape** (`supabase/migrations/*_report_server_side_query.sql`): `report_kirim_rows`/`report_chiqim_rows` (one view per row-kind, `deriveEffectiveQty`/`derivePalletStatus` ported branch-for-branch, `TEST-` exclusion baked into the view's own `WHERE` so it's invisible to any query touching these views at all, not just the reporting engine's own code) → `report_rows` (`UNION ALL`) → `report_filtered_rows(...)` (the single place all 12 filter dimensions' `WHERE` logic lives) → `report_query_page(...)` (orders + paginates) and `report_totals(...)` (aggregates over the FULL filtered set, always exactly one row via `COALESCE(..., 0)` so an empty result still reports `0 kg`, not silence). Two separate RPCs, not one combined call: totals only need recomputing when filters change, not on every page turn. All `security_invoker`/`SECURITY INVOKER` — RLS on the underlying tables still governs visibility; this changes the query shape, not who can see what.

**Two deliberate simplifications from the original TypeScript, confirmed with the user before applying:**
1. A CHIQIM row's `owner_id` always comes from the pallet's originating KIRIM order (via `kirim_lines`→`kirim_orders`), dropping the old code's `request?.owner_id` fallback — `finished_pallets.serial` has a `NOT NULL` FK to `kirim_lines`, so that fallback was already dead in practice ("defensive only, never expected," same pattern used elsewhere in this codebase).
2. The voided-Barcode-#2 exact-match callout (§3.2.2) now queries `report_chiqim_rows` directly (`eq('barcode2', ...).eq('pallet_status', 'bekor_qilingan')`), bypassing `report_filtered_rows` entirely — it was already a structurally separate lookup (an unclaimed voided pallet has no dispatch date and would never survive the date-or-status filter), this just makes that separation explicit in the query layer too.

**Recommended indexes added alongside** (`kirim_orders.plate`, `gate_weighings(order_id/request_id, dir)`, `finished_pallets.serial`, `moyka_sends.serial`, partial indexes on `lab_results` by scope) — not required for correctness at today's row counts, but the whole point of this task is surviving months of real growth.

**🔒 `deriveEffectiveQty` now exists in two places, deliberately, not by oversight.** `weightAuthority.ts` (TypeScript) is still the only option for Ombor's live Moyka/intake screens, which need this value on every render/keystroke and can't practically round-trip to Postgres for it. `report_kirim_rows` (SQL) is the only option for the reporting engine now that filtering/pagination/totals live server-side. This is a real drift risk against CLAUDE.md's "derive, don't store" invariant, which assumes one place computes a given derived value — **the fix isn't eliminating the duplication (not possible here), it's a test that fails loudly the moment the two disagree.**

**`tests/e2e/report-effective-qty-parity.spec.ts` (new) is that test.** Seeds five scenarios directly via `window.supabase` (not the UI — `effective-qty.spec.ts` already covers the full accept-workflow), covering every named basis in `deriveEffectiveQty`: `declared_pre_intake` (no intake yet), `intake_provisional` single- and multi-line (intake exists, gate stage 2 not done — the "not yet gate stage 2" branch is checked before the single/multi split, so both need covering separately), `intake_multi_line_final` (gate stage 2 done, two lines, each keeps its OWN intake figure), and `gate_net_final` (single-line, gate stage 2 done, gate net wins). For each serial, calls `deriveEffectiveQty()` directly (imported into the spec file, not through the browser) with the same known inputs used to seed the row, reads `report_kirim_rows` for that serial, and asserts `qty_kg`/`provisional` match exactly. Uses `uniqueRealLookingPlate()`, not `TEST-` (the view's own `TEST-` exclusion would otherwise hide these fixtures from itself) — confirmed via `pg_policies` which role owns which table's INSERT before writing the seeding helper (menejer: `kirim_orders`/`kirim_lines`; ombor: `storage_intake`; qorovul: `gate_weighings`, single INSERT with both stage 1 and stage 2 fields together — the RLS policy checks only `my_role()='qorovul'`, no constraint forcing a two-step insert-then-update).

**Testing.** `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. `npm test`: 79/79 — 13 tests removed (`matchesText`/`washCycleMatches`/`labVerdictMatches`/`derivePalletStatus`/`passesDateOrStatusOverride`/`isTestPlate`/`computeTotals`, all now dead client-side since filtering/totals moved server-side and `computeTotals` is no longer called anywhere — export now reuses the caller's already-current `report_totals` result instead of re-summing), 7 added for `mapDbRowToReportRow` (the one pure function left: translating the flat SQL row shape back into `KirimReportRow`/`ChiqimReportRow`, including the PostgREST numeric-as-string defensive coercion). New `report-effective-qty-parity.spec.ts` passes (all 5 scenarios, 7 serials).

**Honest note on the pagination proof's scope:** the live non-`TEST-` dataset (seeded demo data + legacy `Test Client A/B/C` rows) is only 42 rows total — short of the 100-row page size, so there's no real "page 2" in production data today to click through. Verified the underlying mechanism directly instead: ran `report_query_page` with `p_limit=10` across 5 offsets (0/10/20/30/40) over the full 42-row filtered set and confirmed the reconstructed union is exactly 42 distinct rows (no gaps, no overlap) summing to precisely what `report_totals` reports for the same filter (64,885 kg in / 13,300 kg out) — proving totals are computed over the FULL filtered set regardless of page size, and that pagination windows are complete and non-overlapping. Confirmed live through the actual UI too (not just raw SQL): the same filter combinations (unfiltered, owner=Boysun, direction=CHIQIM+Subxon+Kalibr 6+O'tdi) return numbers matching both the SQL-level check and last session's hand-verified figures exactly, and clicking Export fires the real `report_query_page` RPC (confirmed via `performance.getEntriesByType('resource')`, since this environment's network-request reader doesn't capture Supabase's `fetch()` calls) rather than reusing whatever was on screen.

**No silent truncation path remains.** `FETCH_CAP` is gone entirely — the DB scans however many rows actually match. The only remaining "limit" is the explicit page size (100, visible as "page N of M" in the UI) and export's own chunk-loop safety net (`EXPORT_MAX_CHUNKS=50` × 1000 rows = 50,000-row ceiling) — if that's ever hit, `fetchAllReportRowsForExport` throws `ExportTooLargeError` with a message telling the user to narrow filters, rather than silently handing back a partial file.

**Full suite run once, per the reduced-testing instruction: 11 passed, 3 failed — all three pre-existing, none caused by this task.** `chiqim-flow.spec.ts` passed cleanly re-run alone (transient full-suite contention, the same recurring pattern this suite has shown across many prior entries). `laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts` and `laborator-kirim.spec.ts` are the exact two failures the immediately-prior entry already diagnosed and explicitly scoped out of this task — not re-investigated.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** remaining §3.2 views (passport, stock-on-hand, WIP, client report, yield, aggregates) — this is the foundation they inherit, not their implementation. The two failing e2e tests diagnosed in the immediately-prior entry, and the `-2,200kg` race — neither re-opened.

## 2026-07-21 — Serial passport (§3.2.5): full lifecycle drill-down from any Hisobot row

**Context:** SPEC.md §3.2 had a forward-reference to §3.2.5 ("the full serial passport, out of scope this prompt") since Step 10 — this task wrote its first real body. One parent serial's whole life, reached as a drill-down from any Hisobot row (KIRIM or CHIQIM, always resolving to that row's parent serial), grouped by lifecycle stage: order → gate → intake → wash cycles 1..N → dispatches → current position.

**One new RPC, confirmed before applying:** `get_serial_passport(p_serial text) returns jsonb` (`supabase/migrations/0027_serial_passport.sql`) — a single nested JSON document in one round trip, given how heterogeneous the shape is (order is one row; cycles and dispatches are each arrays of objects with their own nested pallet arrays). Reads underlying tables directly — **not** through Ombor's finished-goods view (`useMoykaOutput.ts`), whose own SPEC.md §5.3 v1.10 amendment explicitly names this exact requirement ("Ombor's finished-goods view shows the active cycle only; the serial passport... must read underlying records rather than this view"). Reuses `report_kirim_rows`/`report_chiqim_rows` (Task: server-side query, above) for `effective_qty` and pallet-status/void-successor derivation only — both views already read every cycle unconditionally, so reusing them doesn't reintroduce the active-cycle limitation being fixed, and avoids a third implementation of either derivation.

**Two design points confirmed with the user before applying:**
1. **`currentPosition` needed three states, not two.** Original draft only split `omborda` (in storage) vs. collected. Corrected: a manifest-scanned pallet is deducted from *available* stock the instant it's scanned (§5.4) — well before the CHIQIM gate's second weighing — but that isn't the same as physically gone. Split into `omborda` / `band qilingan` (reserved, claimed but truck hasn't cleared gate stage 2 — still on site) / `jo'natilgan` (departed) — only the last counts as collected. Flagged because §3.5's future client report reads this same split for "held for client," which must include reserved-but-not-departed.
2. **Reusing `report_kirim_rows`/`report_chiqim_rows` inherits their `TEST-` exclusion** — a `TEST-`-prefixed serial's passport comes back mostly empty (`effectiveQty` null, cycle pallets/`currentPosition` empty, though `order`/`gate`/`intake`/`kirimLab` still populate since those CTEs read raw tables). Confirmed harmless: a `TEST-` serial never appears in Hisobot in the first place, so there's no row to reach its passport from in production. Documented in the migration's own comment as a note for whoever eventually writes an e2e test against this RPC directly — it will need `uniqueRealLookingPlate()`, the same lesson `reporting-query-engine.spec.ts` and `report-effective-qty-parity.spec.ts` already learned.

**Interpretive call, flagged rather than silently decided:** the task's own "Intake" bullet lists Ombor's figure/actor/timestamp/Barcode #1 but doesn't mention the KIRIM descriptive lab check (moisture/SO₂, no verdict) — however SPEC.md §5.5.2 explicitly states that check "feeds... the serial passport." Confirmed with the user: included, appended to the Intake section (intake-time information, not tied to any one wash cycle).

**🔒 Real bug found and fixed while building this, unrelated to the passport SQL itself.** Sanity-checking the RPC against story 4 (Toshkent's re-wash) surfaced a dispatch with `net_kg: -2450` — a negative gate weight. Traced to the CHIQIM demo-data seed script (Task: demo-data seeding, this session): `gate_weighings.gruzheny_kg`/`pustoy_kg` were swapped on every CHIQIM dispatch. Confirmed against the real app code (`QorovulChiqimTab.tsx`): CHIQIM reverses KIRIM's stage order — stage 1 writes `pustoy_kg` (empty truck arrives), stage 2 writes `gruzheny_kg` (loaded truck departs) — the seed script had this backwards for all 6 of its CHIQIM dispatches, producing a negative `net_kg` invisible until now (the reporting engine never displayed a CHIQIM row's own gate weight, only the pallet's `weight_kg`). Confirmed with the user before fixing (a live-data `UPDATE`, not covered by this task's own stated view/RPC-only permission scope): swapped the two columns on all 6 affected rows (plates `01A333HH`/`01A987ZZ`/`10B111KK`/`10B555XX`/`20C777YY`/`30D999FF`) — every `net_kg` now positive (950/5100/1900/3200/1900/2450 kg respectively). Fixed the same 6 inserts in `supabase/seed/demo-data-2026-07-20.sql` so a future re-seed won't reintroduce it.

**Contents, in lifecycle order** (`src/pages/reports/SerialPassportModal.tsx`, first modal in this codebase — same "first of its kind, deliberately" precedent as the reporting engine's first `<table>`, since the content is too dense for the row-expand `<tr>` it's reached from): Buyurtma (client, declared qty, targets, truck/driver/date, `effective_qty` + variance) → Darvoza (both gate stages, photos, actors, timestamps) → Qabul qilish (Ombor's figure labelled as a per-line split, not a measurement, §2.16) + the KIRIM lab check → Yuvish sikllari, repeated per cycle (kg sent, every pallet including voided ones and their successor, Konditirskiy retained across cycles, CHIQIM lab verdict) → Jo'natishlar, one block per dispatch this serial contributed to → Joriy holat, three-state breakdown by kalibr.

**Reached via a button inside the existing row-expand panel** (`KirimRowDetail.tsx`/`ChiqimRowDetail.tsx`'s own "Seriya pasportini ko'rish →"), not a new route and not replacing the existing lightweight expand — confirmed with the user before building. `HisobotTab.tsx` holds the selected-serial modal state.

**Testing — verified against the seeded demo data, all three of the task's named hard cases confirmed live:**
- **Story 4 (Toshkent, re-wash, both Konditirskiy pallets retained across cycles):** cycle 1 shows both voided Kalibr 6 pallets correctly listing all 3 cycle-2 successors, and its own Konditirskiy pallet (`PLT-200726-216-KN1`) still `Omborda`; cycle 2 shows its own Konditirskiy pallet (`PLT-200726-216-KN2`) also `Omborda`. `currentPosition`'s Konditirskiy row correctly rolls up both (500 + 400 = 900 kg) into one total — the "retained across cycles" requirement, confirmed as a real rollup, not just a visual note.
- **Story 9 (voided, no successor yet):** both voided pallets show "Bekor qilindi → hali yangi barkod chiqarilmagan" (no successor issued yet) — the exact WIP state this story exists to cover, correctly distinct from story 4's populated-successor case. No dispatches, `currentPosition` correctly empty (both pallets voided, nothing else to show).
- **Story 2 (partially dispatched):** cycle 1's pallet list shows `PLT-...-06-1` as `Jo'natilgan`, the other two (`...-06-2`, `...-08-1`) as `Omborda`; `currentPosition` correctly splits Kalibr 6 into 1,000 kg omborda + 1,000 kg jo'natilgan, Kalibr 8 into 900 kg omborda — both collected and remaining visible simultaneously, as required.
- Natural product handling confirmed on the same story 2 pass: both the order's own target and the KIRIM lab result correctly print "Talab yo'q · naturel" / "yo'q · naturel" rather than a blank or zero.

`npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean. `npm test`: 79/79 unchanged (no pure-logic files touched this task). Full Playwright suite run once per the reduced-testing instruction: **12 passed, 2 failed — the exact same two pre-existing, already-diagnosed failures from the immediately-prior entries (`laborator-chiqim-hard-gate.spec.ts`, `laborator-kirim.spec.ts`), nothing new.** No regression introduced by this task.

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** stock-on-hand, WIP, client report, yield, Rahbar dashboard (later prompts) — this is the foundation they inherit, same relationship as the reporting engine to its own saved views. PDF/print, Uz/Ru export localisation, the two known-failing e2e tests, the `-2,200kg` race — none touched.

## 2026-07-21 — Stock-on-hand + WIP saved views: pre-build verification, one data fix

**Context:** Before building §3.2.6 (stock-on-hand) and §3.2.9 (WIP/stuck), the task required re-confirming the demo data's KIRIM-side `gate_weighings` independently — the immediately-prior "Serial passport" entry above only checked and fixed the CHIQIM side; if KIRIM carried the same reversal, every demo `effective_qty` would be wrong.

**KIRIM confirmed correct, not reversed.** Queried `gate_weighings` live for all demo KIRIM orders: every row has `gruzheny_kg > pustoy_kg` (loaded > empty, correct direction), `net_kg` lands 2-4% above `declared_total` (plausible truck variance) on every completed row, and the one provisional row (story 8) correctly has `pustoy_kg`/`net_kg` null pending gate stage 2. No fix needed.

**One data inconsistency found and fixed, distinct from the swap the prior entry already corrected:** story 2's (Farg'ona, `10B555XX`) CHIQIM `gate_weighings` had `net_kg=3200` against a single dispatched pallet actually weighing 1000kg — the swap fix corrected direction but never re-checked each story's own values against its dispatch. Corrected live (`gruzheny_kg` 4200→2000, `net_kg` now 1000) and in `supabase/seed/demo-data-2026-07-20.sql`, matching the 1000kg tare every other story's truck already uses.

**Correction to this session's own initial read:** first pass through the seed file (read before `git fetch` picked up PR #31) mistook the already-merged CHIQIM swap and story 9 as still live-only/undocumented. Re-reading the "Serial passport" entry above showed both were already fixed/added there, file included — only the story-2 mismatch above was genuinely new.

**Also confirmed before designing the new views:** SPEC.md has no written content past §3.2.5 — §3.2.6/§3.2.9 are new spec text this task authors, not a pre-existing locked design, and the companion doc SPEC.md pointed to (`docs/SPEC-reporting-v1.10-revision.md`) doesn't exist in this repo. Per user direction: original numbering kept (§3.2.6 stock-on-hand, §3.2.7 client report reserved, §3.2.8 yield reserved, §3.2.9 WIP, §3.2.10 Rahbar aggregates reserved) and written directly into SPEC.md from here on; the dangling companion-doc reference is removed as part of this task.

## 2026-07-21 — Clean-room reset for client-report verification

**Context:** Building the §3.5/§3.2.7 client report (next prompt) needs a dataset whose balance arithmetic can be checked by hand against a known-correct reference — the existing 9-story demo set was written for the reporting/stock-on-hand/WIP views and sits too close together in time (2026-05-04 to 2026-07-16) to exercise opening/closing period balances meaningfully. Rather than layer a tenth ad-hoc story onto an already-mixed dataset, and since the accumulated e2e test debris (193 `TEST-` lab-turnaround rows alone, per the immediately-prior entry) was already muddying at least one figure, this session wiped every operational table and reseeded from a single, fully-documented script.

**Wipe — confirmed with the user before executing, exact counts shown first.** `supabase/seed/wipe-all-operational-data.sql` (new file): 15 `delete from` statements in dependency order, no `WHERE` clause — `dispatch_manifest`(95→0), `gate_weighings`(302→0), `chiqim_lines`(64→0), `chiqim_requests`(75→0), `lab_results`(277→0), `finished_pallets`(441→0), `wash_cycles`(256→0), `moyka_sends`(199→0), `storage_intake`(385→0), `kirim_lines`(544→0), `kirim_orders`(376→0), `owners`(7→0), `notes`(0→0), `audit_log`(299→0), `serial_counter`(7→0). Kept untouched: `product_categories`(1), `product_types`(5), `calibres`(4), `profiles`(9), `settings_limits`(7).

**`owners` cleared entirely, not scoped.** Confirmed live before wiping: all 7 existing rows were fixtures — the 4 reporting-demo owners plus `Test Client A/B/C` (three orphans from unrelated earlier sessions with no cleanup script of their own, which is exactly how they'd been leaking through the plate-based `TEST-` filter into real-looking client lists). Zero genuine standing business clients existed. `owners.name` is `UNIQUE`, so leaving the 4 demo names in place would have made the reseed's own first `INSERT` fail outright — "keep master data: owners" is satisfied by keeping the table and letting the reseed recreate what it needs with fresh ids, not by preserving fixture rows.

**Reseed — `supabase/seed/demo-data-2026-07-20.sql` extended, not replaced**, keeping the whole thing genuinely repeatable from one file. Original 9 stories unchanged (already verified correct in the two entries above). Added a 5th owner, **Nukus Agro Eksport**, and three new stories (10-12) purpose-built for client-report balance verification over **2026-06-01 to 2026-06-30**:
- Story 10 — arrived 2026-05-20 (before period), washed 2026-06-05 (during) → opening RAW contributor. Deliberately makes gate net (3,100) ≠ `actual_qty` (3,000) ≠ declared (3,000), to catch a report that reads the wrong quantity — the exact bug class the stock-on-hand build (previous entry) found and fixed for raw balances. Output includes Konditirskiy (145 kg), added after the user pointed out the original design never exercised the client-owned/collectible output line at all.
- Story 11 — arrived and washed in May (before period), dispatched 2026-06-20 (during) → opening FINISHED contributor, fully cleared out within the period.
- Story 12 — arrived 2026-06-25 (during period), natural (no SO₂ target), never washed → closing RAW contributor.

**Interpretation confirmed with the user before writing the reference:** §3.5 describes only per-serial arrival/dispatch/remainder — no period opening/closing-balance concept is written down anywhere in SPEC.md yet, since the client report itself hasn't been built. Two rules the user corrected/confirmed for the hand-computed reference: (1) every quantity is `effective_qty` (§2.16), never `actual_qty`/declared; (2) finished stock is "produced but not DEPARTED," not "produced and unclaimed" — the same three-state model (`omborda`/`band_qilingan`/`jo'natilgan`) the passport and stock-on-hand already use, so only actual gate-stage-2 completion removes a pallet from the balance, not merely being claimed onto a manifest. Both rules are written into the seed file's own reference block, flagged as a proposal for whoever builds the report next, not a locked spec decision.

**Hand-computed reference (full derivation in the seed file, directly above story 10) — verified against live data after reseeding, not just derived on paper:**

| | Raw | Finished (K6 / K8 / K4 / Konditirskiy) |
|---|---|---|
| Opening (2026-06-01) | 3,100 kg | 1,400 / 900 / 0 / 0 → 2,300 |
| + received / produced in period | 1,800 kg | 1,800 / 0 / 1,000 / 145 → 2,945 |
| − sent / dispatched in period | 3,100 kg | 1,400 / 900 / 0 / 0 → 2,300 |
| = Closing (2026-06-30) | 1,800 kg | 1,800 / 0 / 1,000 / 145 → 2,945 |

Period process loss: 155 kg / 5.0% (story 10 only, the sole story both sent and finished inside June — matches its own `wash_cycles.final_loss_pct` directly, a second independent check). Dispatched in period: 2,300 kg.

**Verification, post-reseed:** all three Nukus stories queried directly and confirmed to match the reference exactly (serials `210726-012/013/014`) — including story 10's deliberate `net_kg` (3,100) vs. `actual_qty` (3,000) mismatch. Row counts matched hand-derived expectations exactly across all 12 tables (`owners`=5, `kirim_orders`=12, `kirim_lines`=14, `gate_weighings`=19, `storage_intake`=14, `moyka_sends`=13, `wash_cycles`=13, `finished_pallets`=31, `lab_results`=25, `chiqim_requests`=7, `dispatch_manifest`=14, `chiqim_lines`=0 — this seed has never populated `chiqim_lines`, unchanged from before). The four existing views all queried clean against the fresh data: `report_kirim_rows`=14 (exactly `kirim_lines`), `report_chiqim_rows`=31 (exactly `finished_pallets`), `stock_on_hand_rows`=14, `wip_rows`=6; `get_serial_passport('210726-012')` returned fully correct nested data for story 10 (all three pallets including Konditirskiy shown `omborda`, `effectiveQty.valueKg`=3100, truck variance +100 kg/+3.3%).

**`demo-data-2026-07-20-cleanup.sql` updated** to include `'Nukus Agro Eksport'` in every owner-name scope, so it stays a complete, consistent scoped-cleanup companion to the wipe script.

**🚩 Re-running the e2e suite will reintroduce `TEST-` debris.** This clean room only holds while no `TEST-`-fixture-creating test runs. Client-report verification against this dataset should happen **before** any e2e run, or be scoped to querying the Nukus Agro Eksport client specifically (its data has no interaction with `TEST-` fixtures regardless of how many accumulate elsewhere).

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** building the client report itself (next prompt), yield, Rahbar dashboard, Rahbar settings. The full Playwright suite was deliberately not run, per the task's own instruction — it would have immediately repopulated the debris this reset just removed.

## 2026-07-21 — Client report (§3.2.7): the external-facing balance document

**Context:** The prior entry's clean-room reset existed to make this task's own acceptance criterion checkable by hand: run the report for Nukus Agro Eksport, June 2026, and reproduce a pre-computed reference exactly. This entry covers the build itself — one new RPC (`get_client_report`, `supabase/migrations/0029_client_report.sql`, same single-JSONB-document shape as `get_serial_passport`), its TS types/hook/label dictionary/Excel export, and the `ClientReportTab.tsx` screen — plus three real bugs the acceptance check itself surfaced.

**Six design points confirmed with the user before writing SQL** (all now in SPEC.md §3.2.7, each marked 🔒): `effective_qty` only, never `actual_qty`/declared; "olib ketilgan" (departed) means the claiming dispatch's CHIQIM gate stage 2 actually completed, not merely claimed onto a manifest (band_qilingan still counts as held, same three-state model the passport and stock-on-hand already use); Konditirskiy is additive client-owned output, never a deduction line; the §3.2.3 date-basis exception ("davrda qayta ishlangan" uses cycle-1's own completion date, never `moyka_sends.sent_date`); raw is consumed once per serial at cycle 1 (a re-wash re-send never adds to received/processed again — only its own loss and output count); Excel-only output, report-scoped Uz/Ru label dictionary, no PDF and no global i18n (neither exists in this codebase; an earlier browser-print proposal was dropped in favor of Excel, which the codebase already has a security-reviewed dependency for — `exceljs`, not `xlsx`/SheetJS, per §3.2.4's own precedent).

**🔒 Raw-balance cap made visible, not silently clamped — confirmed live that real prior data trips it.** `least(actual_sent, effective_qty)` is what's subtracted from the raw balance (so the balance arithmetic always ties), but the RPC also returns the uncapped `processedActualSentKg`, the difference as `processedOverageKg`, and a `cappedSerials[]` drill-down list — rendered in the UI as an amber warning banner, not swallowed. Serial `140726-003` in the original (pre-clean-room) dataset had already tripped this silently; the fixture's story 14 (below) exists to keep the case covered permanently.

**Cross-period re-wash: attribute to the period the cycle itself completed, shown as its own labelled line — not folded into the period its raw was consumed in.** The alternative (retroactively attributing a later cycle's loss/output back to its raw's original period) was rejected because reports are regenerated fresh from live data on every run, not frozen snapshots — a client who already received June's report would see it silently change months later if a re-wash of that same raw happened to complete in September. Implemented as `client_cycles.in_period_consistent` (`cycle_no=1 or cycle1_completed_date between p_from and p_to`); rows failing that check are pulled into a separate `crossPeriodRewash[]` array and rendered as their own table, labelled with the cycle's own completion date plus the raw-consumption period it references back to, rather than silently added to or subtracted from the main balance.

**🔒 Same-period re-wash: calibre/Konditirskiy output only counts live pallets, but loss counts every cycle's full send.** A voided cycle's output is superseded and must not double-count against whatever later cycle replaced it, but its loss is a fixed historical fact (material was genuinely lost) and stays counted even after voiding. Implemented as two different filters over the same `client_cycles` CTE: `live_calibre_kg`/`live_konditirskiy_kg` (status `in_stock` only) feed the balance's calibre/Konditirskiy lines, while `loss_kg` (`sent_kg - all_calibre_kg - all_konditirskiy_kg`, unfiltered by status) feeds the loss line. Verified against Toshkent's story 4 (the one real pre-existing re-wash in the dataset): raw consumed once (4,100 kg) = live calibre (2,450) + live Konditirskiy (900) + total loss across both cycles (750) — reconciles exactly.

**Three bugs found during the acceptance check itself, all fixed before applying:**
1. **`lossPct` denominator bug.** Originally divided the period's total loss by `loss_main`'s own summed `sent_kg` across every counted cycle — for a re-washed serial this double-counts the re-sent material (story 4's re-send of 3,000 kg on top of the original 4,100 kg gave a `sent_kg` of 7,100, understating loss at 10.6%). Fixed to divide by `raw_processed_actual_total` (the true raw actually consumed, counted once) — story 4 now correctly reads 750/4,100 = 18.3%. Re-verified June, September, and story 4 afterward; no other figure regressed.
2. **Fixture-dating bug (my own error, not an RPC bug).** Stories 13-14 (added to the Nukus fixture specifically to exercise the cap and cross-period cases) were originally dated March/April 2026 — before June. Their never-dispatched finished pallets legitimately carried forward into June's opening finished balance under the RPC's own correct "held, not departed" logic, breaking the already-locked June reference (opening showed 5,530 kg instead of 2,300 kg). Fixed by deleting both stories (dependency-ordered delete, scoped by plate) and re-inserting with dates shifted to August/September, moving the cap/cross-period test period from June to September so it no longer pollutes the locked June numbers.
3. **Cap visibility gap, confirmed not present.** Checked whether `stock_on_hand_rows`/`wip_rows` could render a negative raw balance for story 14's deliberate overage (1,600 kg sent against a 1,500 kg gate net) — both views' existing `WHERE balance > 0` filters already exclude negative rows (the same effect as `useMoykaSerials`'s `Math.max(0, ...)` floor, just via a `WHERE` clause instead of a floor function). Confirmed live in the browser post-build: Nukus's "Xom, yuvilmagan" row reads a positive 1,800 kg for September, no negative row anywhere in the 16-row table. No code change needed.

**Acceptance check — all three locked references reproduced exactly, verified both at the SQL level and live in the browser (`/menejer/mijoz-hisoboti`, Uz and Ru):**
- **June 2026, Nukus Agro Eksport:** raw opening 3,100 / received 1,800 / processed 3,100 (calibre 2,800 + Konditirskiy 145, loss 155 kg / 5.0%) / closing 1,800; finished opening 2,300 / produced 2,945 (K6 1,800, K4 1,000, Konditirskiy 145) / dispatched 2,300 / closing 2,945 — every line, including the by-type and by-calibre breakdowns and the single dispatch's pallet detail (1,400 kg K6 + 900 kg K8 = 2,300 kg), matches the reference exactly.
- **September 2026, Nukus Agro Eksport (story 13/14's relocated test period):** raw opening 1,800 / received 1,500 / processed 1,500 (capped; actual sent 1,600, overage 100 kg shown explicitly with serial `210726-018` named) / closing 1,800; loss 80 kg / 5.0% against the *uncapped* 1,600 kg actually sent — reconciles as designed, the visible gap between the 1,500 kg processed line and the 1,600 kg loss-basis being exactly the overage the warning banner explains. Cross-period table shows story 13's cycle 2 (serial `210726-017`, 1,800 kg sent, 1,710 kg calibre, loss 90 kg / 5.0%), correctly excluded from September's own raw received/processed totals since its raw was consumed in August. Finished side: produced 3,230 kg (1,520 + 1,710) against September's two cycles, closing 6,175 kg, no dispatches.
- **Story 4 re-wash check (Toshkent, spot-checked via SQL):** raw once (4,100 kg) = live calibre (2,450) + live Konditirskiy (900) + total loss both cycles (750) — ties exactly, confirming raw is never double-counted per cycle while loss correctly reflects both.

**Browser verification note:** direct `navigate` to the new route and `computer`-tool clicks on the in-app nav link both silently failed to change `window.location.pathname` in this session's Browser-pane tool — worked around by dispatching the anchor's `click()` directly via `javascript_tool`, which did trigger React Router's navigation correctly. Confirmed this is a tool-level quirk, not an app routing bug, by re-reading `App.tsx`'s route nesting (structurally identical to the already-working `qoldiq`/`kutilmoqda` routes) before reaching for the workaround.

`npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 79/79 unchanged. Full Playwright suite not run, same reduced-testing rationale as the immediately-prior clean-room entry (would reintroduce `TEST-` debris into the just-verified clean dataset).

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** PDF output (no such dependency exists or was added), global i18n (report-scoped label dictionary only), §3.2.8 yield, §3.2.10 Rahbar aggregates.

## 2026-07-21 — Yield view (§3.2.8) + Rahbar dashboard (§3.2.10): the last two reporting views

**Context:** The final pair of reserved section numbers from the original v1.10 revision plan. Two pre-build checks were required before writing any SQL: dry-matter coverage on the seeded fixture, and whether a capacity-utilisation figure exists anywhere.

**Pre-build answer 1 — dry-matter coverage confirmed solid, not thin.** Queried the live fixture directly: 12 of 16 real serials (75%) have both a KIRIM and a CHIQIM moisture reading. The 4 missing are all legitimately in-progress states (one never-tested arrival, one washed-but-lab-pending, two never-washed raw balances) — not a data-quality gap. Dry-matter is built as a headline column on the yield view, not a footnote.

**Pre-build answer 2 — capacity utilisation has no source anywhere, confirmed rather than guessed.** No `settings_limits` key, no other table. Presented to the user as an explicit choice (add a key with a real figure, or drop the metric) rather than inventing a placeholder number. **User's answer, more precise than either option offered:** add the `settings_limits` key but leave it **unset** by default (no real production data exists yet, so any figure would be a guess and a guessed denominator produces a meaningless %) — the dashboard must hide the utilisation line entirely while unset, never show 0%/"n/a"/a placeholder. This required `alter table settings_limits alter column value drop not null` — the first key ever allowed to be blank in that table. **User also added a requirement not in the original task:** pair capacity utilisation with the existing `lab_turnaround_avg()` (§3.2.6) as a second headline stat, since the CHIQIM lab check is a deliberate hard gate on dispatch (§5.5.3) — washing capacity can look fully healthy while dispatch stalls behind an untested backlog, and either number alone can mislead.

**A related gap found during inspection, not asked about in the task but resolved the same way as the capacity question would suggest:** no existing `settings_limits` threshold covers a *rate* (the other three §2.14 exceptions — ageing, lab-overdue, high-loss — are all per-row facts; re-wash rate is a ratio over a group). Unlike capacity, a rate threshold is the same *kind* of number this codebase has repeatedly proposed-with-a-sensible-default-and-confirmed (`abnormal_loss_pct=22`, `tahlil_kechikdi_days=2`, etc.), so a new `high_rewash_rate_pct=20` default was folded into the same migration's SQL for confirmation rather than treated as a second blocking question.

**Design, one row per fully-processed serial (not per event, not per cycle) — confirmed this is what makes "raw counted once regardless of cycles" meaningful in the first place.** `yield_rows`: a serial appears once its CURRENT (highest) `wash_cycles` row is `final`. Reuses §3.2.7's exact `all_*`/`live_*` split: `all_*` (every pallet a cycle ever produced, voided or not) feeds loss, summed across every one of the serial's cycles; `live_*` (`in_stock` only) feeds output/calibre-mix so a voided cycle's superseded output is never double-counted. Loss %'s denominator is `raw_consumed_kg` — cycle 1's own actual, uncapped `moyka_sends` total — never summed sends (0029's original bug, built correctly here from the start rather than discovered twice).

**🚩 A genuine bug found and fixed within minutes of applying the first version of this migration.** The initial `loss_kg` formula subtracted `total_all_calibre_kg`/`total_all_konditirskiy_kg` **summed across every cycle** from `raw_consumed_kg` (cycle-1-only) — an apples-to-oranges mismatch (single-cycle numerator against multi-cycle-summed subtrahend). Caught immediately by sanity-checking against the already-locked story-4 reference (Toshkent re-wash, 750 kg / 18.3% loss): the buggy formula gave `-2,250 kg` / `-54.9%`. Root cause: a cycle 2 re-wash's own `sent_kg` (the previous cycle's voided output flowing back into Moyka, §2.13) must be summed into the loss calculation's own minuend alongside every cycle's `all_*` output — exactly 0029's own `loss_main.loss_kg` shape (`sum(sent_kg) − sum(all_calibre_kg) − sum(all_konditirskiy_kg)`, all three sums spanning the identical set of cycles), which the first draft substituted the wrong variable into. Fixed via a corrective `create or replace view` (added `total_sent_kg` to the `rollup` CTE); re-verified against all three multi-cycle serials in the live fixture afterward — story 4 (Toshkent) now reads exactly 750 kg/18.3%, and story 13's cycle 2 (Nukus, cross-checked independently against the already-verified September client-report numbers) decomposes correctly into an implied 200 kg cycle-1 loss + the client-report's own confirmed 90 kg cycle-2 loss = 290 kg total, 14.5%.

**🔒 Two changes requested after the initial SQL proposal, both applied before anything else was built:**
1. **Re-wash-pending serials excluded outright, not shown with misleading numbers.** The first draft's `finished_serials` filter admitted a serial whose current cycle is `final` but carries an un-actioned `qayta_yuvish` verdict with no successor cycle yet (fixture story 9, real serial `210726-011`) — voided pallets, live output 0, while the loss line still counted the pre-voiding output, giving a nonsensical 0% yield next to ~15% loss and a false ~100% dry-matter loss. Fixed by reusing `wip_rows`' own `qayta_yuvish_pending` condition exactly (lab verdict `qayta_yuvish` + no `wash_cycles` row at `cycle_no+1`) as an explicit exclusion — confirmed live afterward that `210726-011` no longer appears in `yield_rows` (`count(*) = 0`), while it still correctly appears in the WIP view until Ombor completes the re-send.
2. **Loss-basis difference from §3.2.7 made visible, not just internally consistent.** This view deliberately uses the uncapped `raw_consumed_kg` as the loss denominator (the right basis for judging machine/process performance), while §3.2.7 caps at `effective_qty` so its balance ties — meaning the same serial (fixture story 14, `210726-018`) reads a different loss % on the two screens. Rather than resolve the discrepancy, both are kept and explained: `raw_overage_kg` is rendered directly on the row (a red "+100 ortiqcha" badge next to the raw figure, not tucked into an expand-only panel) whenever it's positive, and the header prints the basis outright (`YIELD_LOSS_BASIS_NOTE`) so a Rahbar comparing this screen against a client statement sees why, rather than distrusting either number.

**Date-basis deliberately diverges from §3.2.7's — flagged as a design call, not asked as a question, since it follows directly from the two views' different purposes.** §3.2.7 dates a serial's "processed" line by cycle-1 completion specifically because it's a period balance sheet that must never retroactively change after being handed to a client. This view has no such constraint (it's a live-recomputed summary, not a delivered document), so a re-washed serial's entire yield — every cycle, raw consumed, output, loss — is attributed to the period its LAST cycle completed in, told once rather than fragmented the way §3.2.7 deliberately fragments cross-period re-washes.

**Rahbar dashboard scoped Rahbar-only, unlike §3.2.5-§3.2.9 — the task's own title ("Rahbar dashboard") and §6.1/§6.2's framing (the owner's own landing page and exceptions list) both point the same way.** Rebuilt `RahbarHome.tsx` (previously a placeholder) with monthly trends + period-scoped client ranking + product mix; added a new `RahbarExceptionsTab.tsx` at `/rahbar/diqqat-talab`. Three of the four exception kinds reuse existing views/thresholds outright (ageing from `stock_on_hand_rows`, lab-overdue from `wip_rows`, high-loss from the existing `abnormal_loss_pct`) — only high-rewash needed new SQL.

**🚩 One more bug found during browser verification, fixed immediately: `RahbarExceptionsTab.tsx` called `useCalibres()` without destructuring it and passed a stub `(id) => id` as the passport modal's `calibreLabel` prop** — the drill-down from an exceptions row displayed raw calibre UUIDs instead of "Kalibr 4"/"Kalibr 6". Fixed by wiring the real `calibres` lookup through; re-verified live (drilling into `210726-004`'s passport from the "Tahlil kechikdi" exception row now shows resolved labels).

**Verification:** every multi-cycle/edge-case fixture serial checked directly via SQL against already-locked references before building any UI (story 4 → 750 kg/18.3%, story 13's cycle 2 → decomposes consistently with the September client-report numbers, story 11 → correctly excluded, story 14 → `raw_overage_kg=100` visible). All four Rahbar RPCs and the `yield_rows` view queried directly and sanity-checked. Full UI verified live in-browser as both a Menejer and a Rahbar test login (`.env.test` accounts, phone-based auth): yield table (filters, row expand, calibre mix, dry-matter detail, overage badge), Rahbar monthly trends (capacity column/stat correctly absent while unset), client ranking, product mix, and the exceptions tab (all four kinds present, passport drill-down working) all confirmed rendering with the exact figures the SQL verification predicted. `npx tsc -b --noEmit` clean, `npm test` 79/79 unchanged (no pure-logic files touched). Full Playwright suite not run, same reduced-testing rationale as every prior entry this session (would reintroduce `TEST-` debris).

**Out of scope, not touched (per the task):** Rahbar settings (products/calibres/clients/users administration), PDF, global i18n, the two known-failing e2e tests, the `-2,200kg` race.

## 2026-07-21 — Rahbar settings (§3.3): master data + threshold management, the last build item before testing

**Context:** The final piece before testing begins — Rahbar manages product categories/types/calibres, clients, and every `settings_limits` threshold; Menejer manages clients only. Master data must be deactivated, never deleted, and must keep rendering correctly on historical rows.

**Pre-build inspection answered the task's own question directly: an active/inactive concept already existed on 3 of 4 tables, just unused by any UI.** `owners`, `product_types`, and `product_categories` all already had an `active` boolean column (default `true`) sitting unused since no admin screen existed to flip it. Only `calibres` was missing one — added via this task's own migration. This confirmed the schema work was smaller than expected; the real work turned out to be elsewhere.

**🚩 The real risk, found during inspection before writing any admin UI: `useOwners`/`useProductTypes` were ALREADY filtering `active=true`, and were reused for both purposes at once.** A "new entry" dropdown (KIRIM/CHIQIM forms) correctly wants active-only. But the exact same hooks were also the id→name resolver for every historical/reporting screen — passport, stock-on-hand, WIP, yield, client report, Hisobot, the Rahbar dashboard, every role's own history tab. The moment ANYTHING is ever deactivated, every one of those would have silently started showing a raw uuid (or, for Qorovul's history, a bare `—`) instead of the real name — a bug this task's own build would introduce, not one that already existed, since deactivation itself didn't exist until now.

**Audited all 22 files calling these three hooks (a dedicated research pass, not a guess) before touching a single call site.** Found: 3 files are genuinely creation-only and correct as-is (`KirimForm`, `ChiqimForm`, `FinishedReceiptForm` — all resolve only just-saved, guaranteed-active rows). 1 is a pure filter-bar with no resolution of its own (`ReportFilterBar`, fixed indirectly via its parent `HisobotTab`). The remaining **18 files would break** — not just the reporting layer named in the task's own requirement B-equivalent testing checklist, but every role's own operational history screens too (Laborator KIRIM/CHIQIM, Ombor's four tabs, Qorovul's three tabs, Menejer's own order-history lists). One of those, `OmborTayyorTab`'s re-wash handler, had a **logic** bug exposure, not just a display one: `numberlessCalibres` was built from the active-filtered list, so a deactivated Konditirskiy calibre would be misclassified as an ordinary calibre and wrongly voided during a re-wash — material-handling correctness, not cosmetics.

**Presented the full audit and asked the user how far the fix should reach, since the task's own "no UI work on operational screens" line was in direct tension with fixing all 18.** User's answer: fix all 18, not just the reporting layer named in the task — "the 'no UI work on operational screens' line meant no redesign, not leave-correctness-bugs... showing a raw UUID for historical master data is a bug this task itself introduces... nobody will connect the cause months later." Applied exactly that scope.

**Fix: an opt-in `includeInactive` parameter on all four master-data hooks (`useOwners`/`useProductTypes`/`useCalibres`/new `useProductCategories`), default `false`.** Every existing call site keeps its exact current behaviour unless it explicitly opts in — a one-line change per file, not a UI redesign, and genuinely zero risk to the 4 files correctly left untouched. All 18 breaking files (plus `ClientReportTab`'s owner-selector, which the audit flagged as its own sharp case — you must be able to generate a report for a deactivated client) now pass `includeInactive: true`. `OmborTayyorTab` needed a real split, not just a flag flip: `useCalibres(true)` feeds both `calibreLabel` resolution and the re-wash handler's `is_numberless` check correctly, while a derived `activeCalibres = calibres.filter(c => c.active)` — not the raw hook result — is what's actually passed to `FinishedReceiptForm`'s own new-pallet creation dropdown, so a deactivated calibre still can't be chosen for new receipts.

**🔒 Also gave all five master-data hooks a `refetch()` function** (previously none had one) so the new admin screens can reload their own list after a create/rename/deactivate without a full page reload — a small, uniform addition across `useOwners`/`useProductTypes`/`useCalibres`/`useProductCategories`/`useSettingsLimits`, not a one-off for this screen.

**RLS: two things resolved with the user before applying, per the explicit permission gate.**
1. **Confirmed a housekeeping gap from the immediately-prior task, then closed it.** The user asked directly whether two migrations applied live in that task (`yield_view_and_rahbar_dashboard`, and a same-session `loss_kg` bug-fix correction) both now had local files, since a fresh `supabase db push` otherwise wouldn't reproduce live schema. Verified rigorously rather than assuming: pulled the live `yield_rows` view definition and both `settings_limits` rows via direct query and diffed them against the file already written — confirmed byte-for-byte equivalent logic. Both migrations' net effect is captured in one file (`0030_yield_view_and_rahbar_dashboard.sql`, reflecting the final corrected state) rather than two files including a deliberately-buggy intermediate step, since nothing is served by a fresh install reproducing a bug that was fixed within minutes of being found.
2. **Menejer's `owners` UPDATE policy is row-level, not column-restricted — confirmed with the user, not left silently either way.** The user caught, unprompted, that a row-level grant lets Menejer technically flip `active` too, not just rename — wider than "clients only" intended. Considered a real column-level restriction (Postgres native `GRANT UPDATE (name)` can't distinguish app-roles here, since every app-role shares one Postgres role `authenticated` with role-checks done entirely inside RLS `USING`/`WITH CHECK` — only a trigger or a dedicated RPC could genuinely enforce column-level scoping). Decided against either: disproportionate complexity for a reversible, low-stakes gap, given the Menejer clients screen built this task simply never renders a deactivate control — the only path to exploiting the wider grant is a deliberate direct API call, not an accidental UI click. Documented explicitly in both SPEC.md §6.4 and here, per the user's instruction not to leave it unstated either way.

**RLS tightening beyond what was asked: removing DELETE from the existing admin policies wasn't a new restriction, it was closing a gap already documented as the intended design.** SPEC.md §2.15 already said "INSERT/UPDATE only on admin tables" before this task touched anything — but the live `rahbar_admin_*` policies on `owners`/`product_types`/`product_categories`/`calibres`/`settings_limits` were all `FOR ALL`, including DELETE, presumably a shortcut from before any admin UI existed to exercise the difference. Replaced each with separate INSERT/UPDATE-only policies (verified live afterward: no `cmd=ALL` policy remains on any of the five tables) — extends "Never DELETE — void" (§2.15) from operational records, where it already applied, to master data, where it's this task's own explicit requirement.

**Uniform collision handling, confirmed with the user rather than assumed from the task's own owners-only example.** `owners.name` is the only UNIQUE constraint the task named explicitly, but `product_categories.name` is also globally unique and `product_types`/`calibres` are unique per-category (name/code respectively) — confirmed live via `pg_constraint` before building. One shared `friendlyDbError` helper (`src/lib/masterDataAdmin.ts`) catches Postgres `23505` uniformly across all four admin forms and shows "Bu nom allaqachon mavjud..." instead of a raw database error, rather than writing the same catch four times.

**First CRUD admin table in this codebase — built from the closest existing furniture, not a new interaction pattern invented for its own sake.** No prior screen anywhere in the app lists existing master data with inline rename + toggle-active; the closest precedents were the reporting tables' `th`/`td` shell (structure) and `UsersAdminPage.tsx`'s stacked-rounded-border-section-plus-form style (visual language). `ClientsSection.tsx` combines both and is shared verbatim between Rahbar's Sozlamalar (`allowDeactivate={true}`) and Menejer's Mijozlar (`allowDeactivate={false}`) — one component, one prop difference, not two parallel implementations.
